# M08 Phase 9 — Cluster Synthesis — structural input

**Date:** 2026-05-21
**Cluster:** M08 — Pride, Arrogance and Boasting

---

## §1 — Cluster overview

M08 (Pride, Arrogance and Boasting) holds 5 inner-being characteristics:

| Char | Short name | One-line definition |
|---:|---|---|
| 1 | Arrogant self-elevation | The inner state in which the heart or will lifts itself above its proper station before God and others, claiming standing, honour, or status that does not belong to it. |
| 2 | Presumptuous defiance | The inner state in which the will asserts itself against known divinely-established limits, appointed authority, or revealed commands with a boiling-over force — pride-as-deliberate-defiance rather than merely elevated self-regard. |
| 3 | Boasting and self-display | The inner impulse to self-glorify through words, visible claims, and public assertion of one's own worth, achievement, credentials, or future plans — pride moving outward through speech and self-presentation. |
| 4 | Vain conceit | Pride operating specifically in the cognitive faculty as a false, inflated self-assessment — the mind's wrong picture of itself that produces blindness to truth, fuels controversy, generates communal disorder, and causes the person to claim resources, status, or recognition beyond what is warranted. |
| 5 | Pride of power and position | The inner arrogance that arises when strength, social authority, material prosperity, or national might becomes the ground for self-exaltation and contemptuous elevation above others. |

Each characteristic produced 189 findings in its Phase 9 batch (1,323 rows total in `cluster_finding`).

---

## §2 — Confirmed cluster observations (with resolution notes)

These four observations were raised at characteristic-mapping time and confirmed during Phase 9. They name the boundaries already validated and are direct inputs to the synthesis.

### Observation #10 — INTEGRATION_NOTE (linked to Char 14)

**Title:** CHAR-1 volume-split across M08-A1 / M08-A2 / M08-A3 / M08-A4

**Description:**

> CHAR-1 (Arrogant self-elevation) is the cluster's dominant characteristic (151 of 293 substantive verses = 51.5%). Per v2_8 §8.0 rule 2, volume-split across four sub-groups by seat-of-pride axis: M08-A1 (heart, 33V — including post-Phase-8.5 promotion of G0193 contribution implicit via mti_term routing), M08-A2 (eyes/outward bearing, 11V), M08-A3 (national/collective, 40V), M08-A4 (general dispositional, 69V — post-Phase-8.5). The characteristic identity persists across the four sub-groups; Phase 9 catalogue prompts should evaluate CHAR-1 as a single inner-being faculty manifesting in four registers, not as four separate characteristics. Splitting axis is the anatomical/framing locus where the pride is named (heart vs eyes vs collective subject vs unspecified).

---

### Observation #11 — INTER_RELATIONSHIP (linked to Char 16)

**Title:** M08-C boasting ↔ M22 praise/glory as register-adjacent through shared vocabulary

**Description:**

> Phase 3 cross-register analysis (per v2_7 §6.3.2 verse-level relationship test) confirmed the kauchaomai family (kauchaomai/kauchēma/kauchēsis) and ha.lal verb carry three distinct registers within M08-C's 70-verse corpus: (a) condemned self-directed boasting (M08-C-VCG-01); (b) Pauline examined-boasting discourse — boasting only in the Lord / in weakness / in the cross (M08-C-VCG-02); (c) God-directed glorying / praise (M08-C-VCG-03, the M22 register). The same lexemes express both M08 (self-boasting) and M22 (praise-of-God) inner-being content; the register-distinction is verse-level. Phase 9 T6 (Structural Relationships with Other Characteristics) should articulate the M08 ↔ M22 register-adjacency: praise becomes boasting when self-directed; boasting becomes praise when God-directed. When M22 opens, the M08-C-VCG-03 verses (~20-23 verses) and the relevant ha.lal verses may be picked up as cross-cluster contributions to M22's praise vocabulary.

---

### Observation #12 — INTER_RELATIONSHIP (linked to Char 18)

**Title:** M08-E pride-of-power ↔ M23 strength/dominion as misuse-of-faculty register

**Description:**

> Phase 3 cross-register analysis confirmed several M08-E terms (ga.on proud-might, archō domineering-authority, hupsēlofroneō wealth-pride, ma.rom fortified-elevation, shal.le.tet imperious self-will, a.din voluptuous ease, qo.mah Eze 19:11) carry their primary register in M23 (strength/power/dominion); they remain in M08 because their verses evidence strength-misused-as-self-exaltation. The pride-of-power register is structurally the M23 faculty turned inward toward self-aggrandisement. Phase 9 T6 should articulate the M08 ↔ M23 misuse-of-faculty pairing: M23 carries strength/capacity as the inner-being faculty; M08-E carries the corruption of that faculty when it becomes the ground for arrogance. When M23 opens, the M08-E sub-group's term list informs which strength terms have a documented misuse-pole at the verse level.

---

### Observation #13 — INTEGRATION_NOTE (cluster-wide)

**Title:** Phase 5.5 set-aside: 174 non-M08-content verses (Option 2 researcher decision)

**Description:**

> At Phase 5.5 (2026-05-20), 174 verses from polysemic M08 terms were set_aside via CC patch before Phase 6 routing (researcher Option 2 decision). Breakdown: (a) 122 verses with M22-register content (divine majesty / God-directed exaltation) from rum, ga.on, ga.a.vah, ga.vah, ha.lal, ge.ut, go.vah, ma.rom, ga.ah — terms STAY in M08 via §6.3.2 because their pride verses survived, but these individual verses carry M22 not M08 content; set_aside_reason='non-M08 content — M22-register (divine majesty / God-directed exaltation); term STAYS in M08 via other verses (v2_8 §6.3.2)'. (b) 52 verses with no inner-being content (archō temporal/narrative markers; ra.hav positive-assertiveness; H7312 Pro 25:3); set_aside_reason='non-M08 content — narrative marker / neutral assertiveness; no inner-being state evidenced'. These verses are recoverable for cross-cluster analysis if needed (M22 may pick up the 122 M22-register verses when it opens) but do not contribute findings to M08. Substantive M08 corpus reduced from 470 → 296 → 293 (post-Phase-7 duplicate cleanup).

---

### Observation #14 — INTEGRATION_NOTE (linked to Char 14)

**Title:** Phase 8.5: G0193 akratēs promoted from BOUNDARY to M08-A4-VCG-01

**Description:**

> At Phase 8.5 (2026-05-21), the single BOUNDARY-verdict term G0193 akratēs (intemperate, 1 verse at 2Ti 3:3) was PROMOTED to M08-A4-VCG-01 (NT vice-catalogue register) per researcher decision. Rationale: akratēs sits in the same scriptural vice catalogue as filautos (2Ti 3:2) and huperēfanos (2Ti 3:2), which are already routed to M08-A4-VCG-01. Per the AI's Phase 3 framing, akratēs is the enabling-condition register through which CHAR-1 operates unchecked — the breakdown of inner discipline that lets pride run free. The term is therefore a qualifying/supportive contributor to CHAR-1's NT vice-catalogue VCG rather than its own characteristic. M08-BOUNDARY sub-group + M08-BOUNDARY-VCG-01 soft-deleted; cluster now has 8 sub-groups + 24 VCGs.

---

## §3 — Per-prompt synthesis matrix

For each of the 189 prompts (T0.1.1 … T7.3.4), the 5 characteristics' findings are stacked verbatim below. Read all 5 before authoring the cluster-scope row in your output.

### T0

#### T0.1 — Divine Nature Reflected

##### T0.1.1 — What does the verse evidence reveal about the nature or character of God that this characteristic reflects or images?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The verse evidence reveals that God alone holds the prerogative of genuine exaltation, and that CHAR-1 is the creature's usurpation of that singular divine position. The structural logic is stated explicitly in the day-of-the-Lord material: Isa 2:11 (vc=34601, M08-A3-VCG-04) — "the lofty pride of men shall be humbled, and the Lord alone will be exalted in that day"; Isa 2:17 (vc=34602, M08-A3-VCG-04) — "the lofty pride of men shall be brought low, and the Lord alone will be exalted in that day." Both verses frame CHAR-1's humbling as the condition for the restoration of God's exclusive exaltation. Psa 75:7 (vc=34230, M08-A4-VCG-05) states the governing principle: "it is God who executes judgment, putting down one and lifting up another" — exaltation is God's sovereign act, not the creature's. CHAR-1 therefore reflects, by inversion, the divine attribute of true exaltation: the characteristic is what arises when the creature competes for what belongs to God alone.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The verse evidence reveals that CHAR-2 (Presumptuous defiance) reflects the divine nature by standing in direct opposition to it: CHAR-2 is the creature's will asserting itself against the very limits God has established, and the evidence consistently frames God as the one who establishes those limits and judges their violation. Neh 9:10 (vc=34125, M08-B-VCG-01): "you performed signs and wonders against Pharaoh and all his servants and all the people of his land, for you knew that they acted arrogantly against our ancestors" — God's counter-action to CHAR-2 reveals his character as the sovereign who defines the limits the will transgresses. Deu 17:12 (vc=34110, M08-B-VCG-02): the man who acts presumptuously against the appointed judge "shall die; so you shall purge the evil from Israel" — God's ordination of authority structures is what CHAR-2 violates. CHAR-2 does not image any divine attribute positively; it images the creature's attempt to claim the sovereignty over limits that belongs to God alone.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

The verse evidence reveals that CHAR-3 reflects and distorts the divine nature as the ultimate and only legitimate ground of boasting. Jer 9:23 (vc=33342, M08-C-VCG-01): the wise must not boast in wisdom, the mighty not in might, the rich not in riches — three prohibited objects that together identify all creaturely achievement as illegitimate boasting-ground. The verse's positive implication: God alone, as the one to be known, is the legitimate object of glory. 1Cor 1:29–31 (vc=33877, vc=33878, M08-C-VCG-01/03): God's sovereign design "so that no human being might boast in the presence of God" and "let the one who boasts, boast in the Lord" — God is the one who structures the created order to direct all boasting toward himself. CHAR-3 (self-directed boasting) reflects, by inversion, that God is the sole legitimate object of the glorying-impulse that CHAR-3 redirects toward the self.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The verse evidence reveals that CHAR-4 (vain conceit — the mind's inflated false self-picture) reflects, by inversion, God's nature as the one who gives the accurate measure by which the mind should assess itself. Rom 12:3 (vc=60866, M08-D-VCG-02): "think of yourself with sober judgment, each according to the measure of faith that God has assigned" — God is the one who assigns the measure; CHAR-4 is the mind's exceeding of that assigned measure. 1Ti 3:6 (vc=33924, M08-D-VCG-02): the conceited person falls into "the condemnation of the devil" — CHAR-4 at its extreme reflects the adversarial paradigm of the creature exceeding its proper cognitive station. 1Ti 6:4 (vc=33925, M08-D-VCG-02): conceit produces "a complete lack of understanding" — God's nature as truthful, accurate knowledge is inverted in CHAR-4's cognitive blindness.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

The verse evidence reveals that CHAR-5 reflects, by usurpation, God's nature as the sole and genuine source of all power and might. Lev 26:19 (vc=33982, M08-E-VCG-01): God threatens to "break the pride of your power" — only God can break structural power-pride, confirming that God himself holds what CHAR-5 claims to hold. The Eze 30 corpus (vc=33996, 33997, 33998, M08-E-VCG-01): God repeatedly declares he will bring down Egypt's "proud might" — the reversal evidences God as the one who holds the genuine power that CHAR-5 misattributes to the nation. 1Ti 6:17 (vc=60878, M08-E-VCG-02): the wealthy are warned not to "set their hopes on the uncertainty of riches, but on God, who richly provides everything" — God as the genuine provider of all material goods is what CHAR-5 ignores in claiming wealth as a self-exaltation ground.

---

##### T0.1.2 — Does Scripture explicitly attribute this characteristic to God — and if so, what does that attribution reveal about its significance in the human person?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Scripture does not attribute arrogant self-elevation to God. The 174 Phase 5.5 set-aside verses (the M22-register rum, ga.on, ga.vah material) carried divine-majesty content that belongs to God's own register and was correctly excluded from CHAR-1's corpus. What the remaining §3 evidence consistently shows is CHAR-1 as the creature's counterfeit of what God legitimately holds: Dan 11:36 (vc=34235, M08-A1-VCG-02) — the king "exalts himself and magnifies himself above every god" by his own will, explicitly placing CHAR-1 as a movement against God's divine position; Eze 28:2 (vc=34040, M08-A1-VCG-02) — "your heart is proud, and you have said, 'I am a god, I sit in the seat of the gods'" — the creature claiming divine status is what CHAR-1 names at its sharpest. The silence of the evidence regarding God possessing CHAR-1 is itself the finding: arrogant self-elevation is exclusively creaturely, a distortion that competes with the divine rather than reflecting it.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (S)

Scripture does not attribute presumptuous defiance to God within the 45-verse §3.A corpus. God is consistently evidenced as the one who establishes the authority and revealed commands that CHAR-2 transgresses, and as the one who judges CHAR-2. Deu 18:20 (vc=34119, M08-B-VCG-01): "the prophet who presumes to speak a word in my name that I have not commanded him to speak" — God is the source of the command that the presumptuous prophet violates. The evidence is entirely silent on God possessing the boiling inner self-will that defines CHAR-2.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (S)

Scripture does not attribute CHAR-3 (self-directed boasting) to God within §3.B. The God-directed boasting of M08-C-VCG-03 (Rom 5:2, vc=33874; 1Cor 1:31, vc=33878; Phili 3:3, vc=33879) is not God boasting about himself but the believer glorying in God — a human act directed toward God. God as the subject of self-directed boasting is not evidenced. The evidence is silent on God possessing CHAR-3.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (S)

Scripture does not attribute vain conceit to God within the 12-verse §3.C corpus. God is the one who assigns the proper cognitive measure (Rom 12:3, vc=60866) against which CHAR-4 is the transgression. God possessing an inflated false self-picture is constitutively impossible — his self-knowledge is perfect and cannot exceed what he actually is.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (S)

Scripture does not attribute CHAR-5 to God within §3.D. The verse evidence consistently positions God as the one who judges and breaks structural power-pride (Lev 26:19; Eze 7:24, vc=33993; Eze 30:6, vc=33996) rather than as a possessor of CHAR-5. God's genuine strength and might belong to M23 (strength/power/dominion) and M22 (divine majesty), not to M08-CHAR-5.

---

##### T0.1.3 — Where Scripture is silent about God's possession of this characteristic, what does that silence suggest about the characteristic's place in the divine image?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The silence is theologically load-bearing. The §3 corpus consistently deploys CHAR-1 as what stands against God — against his judicial authority (Psa 94:2, vc=33952, M08-A4-VCG-02: the proud "deserve" divine retribution), against his sole supremacy (Isa 2:11–12, M08-A3-VCG-04: "the Lord alone will be exalted"), against his revealed character (Isa 37:23, vc=34304, M08-A4-VCG-05: raising the voice against "the Holy One of Israel"). The fact that God is never the subject of CHAR-1 in this corpus — while God is consistently the one who opposes, humbles, and reverses CHAR-1 — places CHAR-1 outside the divine image as such. The characteristic is not an image-bearing quality distorted; it is the creature's attempt to occupy God's own position, which makes it categorically different from characteristics that are genuine creaturely analogues to divine attributes.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The silence is analytically significant: CHAR-2 (the will boiling over against divinely-established limits) is constitutively impossible for God to possess, since God himself establishes those limits. The characteristic requires an external authority to defy — there is no authority external to God against which God could presume. Deu 17:12 (vc=34110, M08-B-VCG-02) and Deu 18:20 (vc=34119, M08-B-VCG-01) both frame CHAR-2 as transgression of limits that God himself has ordained (the appointed judge, the commanded word). The silence confirms CHAR-2 as a characteristically creaturely distortion: only a creature who stands under authority can defy that authority presumptuously.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

The silence is structurally significant: CHAR-3 (self-glorification) would require a subject who inflates their own standing beyond what they deserve or beyond proper creaturely acknowledgment. God, being fully what he is, cannot self-inflate — there is no gap between his actual worth and his self-presentation. 1Cor 4:7 (vc=33871, M08-C-VCG-01): "what do you have that you did not receive? If then you received it, why do you boast as if you did not receive it?" — the premise of CHAR-3 is misattribution of what was received as self-generated. God receives nothing from outside himself; all goods originate from him, making the logical structure of CHAR-3 (claiming as self-generated what was received) inapplicable to God.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The silence is definitionally necessary. CHAR-4 is the mind's false, inflated self-assessment — a gap between the person's actual worth/standing and their cognitive picture of it. God's self-knowledge is perfectly accurate; there is no gap between what God is and what God knows himself to be. The structure of CHAR-4 (inflation beyond actual measure — fusioō/tufoō: to puff up beyond actual substance) presupposes a creature with limited actual standing who overclaims; God cannot overclaim because he is the measure itself. The silence confirms CHAR-4 as exclusively creaturely.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

The silence is theologically instructive. CHAR-5 arises when strength, authority, or wealth becomes the ground for self-exaltation and contempt of others. God's strength is genuine rather than inflated beyond what he possesses — there is no gap between his actual power and his self-presentation. The silence confirms CHAR-5 as exclusively creaturely: it is the creature's false claim to power-derived self-sufficiency ("I am, and there is no one besides me" — Isa 47:8, vc=9563, M08-E-VCG-02: Babylon's self-declaration) that CHAR-5 names, a declaration structurally inapplicable to God who actually is the sole ground of all being.

---

#### T0.2 — Created Purpose

##### T0.2.1 — What does the verse evidence suggest about the purpose this characteristic serves in the human person as created — what does it equip the person to be, do, or become?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (S)

The verse evidence is silent on any created purpose for arrogant self-elevation. Every verse in §3 treats CHAR-1 as either condemned (Pro 16:5, vc=12083, M08-A1-VCG-03: "everyone who is arrogant in heart is an abomination to the Lord"), causally linked to destruction (Pro 16:18, vc=34073, M08-A1-VCG-03: "pride goes before destruction"), or identified as a fallen inner movement to be opposed and reversed (Psa 18:27, vc=34242, M08-A2-VCG-01: "the haughty eyes you bring down"; Jam 4:6, vc=33931, M08-A4-VCG-01: "God opposes the proud"). No verse in the corpus treats self-elevation as a God-given capacity functioning properly. The silence regarding a created purpose is analytically significant: CHAR-1 appears to have no positive functional role in the evidence — it is consistently the disorder, not the design.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (S)

The verse evidence is entirely silent on any created purpose for presumptuous defiance. Every verse in §3.A treats CHAR-2 as a transgression to be condemned, purged, or punished. Deu 17:13 (vc=34124, M08-B-VCG-01): "all the people shall hear and fear and not act presumptuously again" — the explicit goal is eradication of the behaviour, not any affirmation of its purpose. No verse in the 45-verse corpus evidences CHAR-2 serving a positive created function.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

The verse evidence distinguishes between a created purpose (glorying/exulting in something) and CHAR-3's fallen self-directed form. The VCG-03 material evidences that the capacity to glory, exult, and boast is positively deployed when God-directed: Rom 5:2 (vc=33874, M08-C-VCG-03): boasting in hope of God's glory; 1Cor 1:31 (vc=33878): "let the one who boasts, boast in the Lord"; Jam 1:9 (vc=33880, M08-C-VCG-03): the lowly believer "boasts" in his God-given exaltation — all evidencing the glorying-impulse functioning as created when directed toward God and received goods. CHAR-3 (M08-C-VCG-01, self-directed condemned boasting) is this same created capacity misdirected toward the self, creaturely achievement, wealth, or power.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (S)

The verse evidence is entirely silent on any created purpose for vain conceit. Every verse in §3.C treats the inflated cognitive self-assessment as a moral failure to be corrected (Rom 12:3: "do not think of yourself more highly than you ought"), a blindness to truth (1Ti 6:4, vc=33925: conceit paired with "understanding nothing"), or a path to judgment (1Ti 3:6, vc=33924: "the condemnation of the devil"). No created purpose is evidenced.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

The verse evidence implies that strength, power, and wealth are legitimate God-given goods whose created purpose is to serve God's people and honour God. Lev 26:19 (vc=33982, M08-E-VCG-01): "the pride of your power" — the power itself was God-given; CHAR-5 is the misuse of that power as a self-exaltation ground rather than its created purpose (service to God and others). Eze 16:49 (vc=33979, M08-E-VCG-01): Sodom's "pride" paired with "excess of food and prosperous ease" — the excess itself evidences God-given material good misused. CHAR-5 has no created purpose as a characteristic; the power and strength that generate it have a created purpose (service, stewardship) that CHAR-5 corrupts.

---

##### T0.2.2 — Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic is part of the original created design, a response to the fallen condition, or both?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The evidence consistently places CHAR-1 within the fallen condition, not the original created design. Mar 7:22 (vc=33928, M08-A4-VCG-01) situates pride explicitly among "the evil things that come out of a person" — constitutively internal but categorised as moral corruption. Pro 16:5 (vc=12083, M08-A1-VCG-03) — "everyone who is arrogant in heart is an abomination to the Lord" — treats CHAR-1 as a universal feature of the fallen inner person, not as created design. The NT vice catalogues (Rom 1:30, vc=33932, M08-A4-VCG-01: haughtiness among vices of a morally disordered mind; 2Ti 3:2, vc=33933, M08-A4-VCG-01: arrogance as a defining inner trait of last-days moral collapse) position CHAR-1 within the characterology of human fallenness. No verse in §3 attributes CHAR-1 to the original created order. The evidence is consistent: CHAR-1 is a fallen characteristic.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The evidence consistently places CHAR-2 within the fallen condition. The historical narrative of Israel's repeated presumptuous defiance frames it as the pattern of the fallen community's response to God's commands: Neh 9:16 (vc=34120, M08-B-VCG-01): "our ancestors acted presumptuously and stiffened their neck and did not obey your commandments"; Neh 9:29 (vc=34126): "even after warnings, they acted presumptuously again" — the repetition underscores that CHAR-2 is a characteristic feature of fallen humanity's disposition toward divine authority, not a designed capacity. Authadēs in Tit 1:7 (vc=42740, M08-B-VCG-03) — the opposite of what an overseer must be — confirms CHAR-2 as a moral failure to be overcome, not a design feature.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

The evidence distinguishes clearly. The glorying/exulting capacity is created and legitimate (VCG-03 evidence above — God-directed glorying is commanded, modelled, and approved). The self-directed form of boasting (VCG-01) is consistently condemned as fallen: 1Jo 2:16 (vc=33865, M08-C-VCG-01): "the pride of life [alazoneia] is not from the Father but is from the world" — explicitly distinguishing the worldly-origin (fallen) of CHAR-3's VCG-01 form from the Father. Eph 2:9 (vc=65604, M08-C-VCG-01): salvation by grace through faith "not a result of works, so that no one may boast" — God's design specifically excludes the ground for CHAR-3's VCG-01 form. CHAR-3's condemned self-directed form is a response to the fallen condition; the underlying boasting-capacity is created.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The evidence uniformly places CHAR-4 within the fallen condition. All 12 verses address CHAR-4 as a moral failure to be corrected or condemned. 2Ti 3:4 (vc=33926, M08-D-VCG-02): tufoō (being swollen with conceit) is grouped in the end-times vice catalogue with recklessness, love of pleasure over God — a characterology of moral collapse. 1Cor 8:1 (vc=33935, M08-D-VCG-01): "knowledge puffs up, but love builds up" — the inflated cognitive state is the fallen response to received knowledge, contrasted with the created-design expression of love. No verse treats CHAR-4 as a created design feature.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

The evidence uniformly places CHAR-5 within the fallen condition. Eze 16:49 (vc=33979, M08-E-VCG-01): Sodom's pride is explicitly listed as a root sin — one of the originating inner causes of Sodom's moral collapse; Eze 28:5 (vc=34046, M08-E-VCG-02): "your heart became proud" — the heart's CHAR-5 elevation is a consequence of success, not the created design. 1Ti 6:17 (vc=60878, M08-E-VCG-02): the wealthy warned against hupsēlofroneō (wealth-pride) — an inner danger, not a design feature. CHAR-5 is consistently evidenced as a fallen response to received power, wealth, or position.

---

##### T0.2.3 — Is there evidence that this characteristic is oriented toward a future fullness — something the person is moving toward, not only what they currently are?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The evidence consistently orients CHAR-1 toward a future humbling and reversal, not toward any fullness. The day-of-the-Lord material makes this eschatological trajectory explicit: Isa 2:11 (vc=34089, M08-A2-VCG-01): "the haughty looks of man shall be brought low"; Isa 2:12 (vc=33957, M08-A3-VCG-04): "the Lord of hosts has a day against all that is proud and lofty, against all that is lifted up — and it shall be brought low"; Eza 31:14 (vc=54400, M08-A3-VCG-04): "all this is in order that no trees by the waters may grow to towering height... for they are all given over to death." The structural wisdom maxim (Pro 16:18, vc=34073, M08-A1-VCG-03) — "pride goes before destruction" — identifies CHAR-1's orientation as toward collapse, not toward fullness. CHAR-1 has no positive eschatological trajectory; it moves toward the judgment that reverses it.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The evidence points CHAR-2 toward future judgment, not fullness. Mal 4:1 (vc=34107, M08-B-VCG-02): "the arrogant and all evildoers will be stubble; the day that is coming shall set them ablaze, says the Lord of hosts, it will leave them neither root nor branch" — CHAR-2's eschatological orientation is toward total destruction. Jer 50:31–32 (vc=34116, vc=34117, M08-B-VCG-02): Babylon ("the most proud one" / "arrogance") stumbles and falls with no one to raise it — the arrogant inner disposition finds its terminus in irrecoverable collapse. There is no positive future fullness evidenced for CHAR-2.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Yes — but only for CHAR-3's VCG-03 (God-directed) and VCG-02 (Pauline examined) registers. 1Th 2:19 (vc=33913, M08-C-VCG-03): "what is our hope or joy or crown of boasting before our Lord Jesus at his coming? Is it not you?" — boasting as an eschatological act before Christ; Phili 2:16 (vc=33910, M08-C-VCG-03): "my pride on the day of Christ" — boasting in the eschatological day is the goal. 2Cor 1:14 (vc=33907, M08-C-VCG-03): "on the day of our Lord Jesus you will boast of us as we will boast of you." For M08-C-VCG-01 (condemned self-boasting), the eschatological orientation is toward elimination: 1Cor 1:29 (vc=33877): God's election designed so that "no human being might boast in the presence of God" — self-boasting has no positive eschatological future.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4 is oriented toward judgment and correction, not fullness. 1Ti 3:6 (vc=33924, M08-D-VCG-02): the conceited new leader falls into "the condemnation of the devil" — a judicial terminus. 1Cor 4:19 (vc=33939, M08-D-VCG-01): Paul will expose "not the talk of these arrogant people but their power" — the conceited person's talk will be exposed as empty when their actual power is tested. 1Cor 5:2 (vc=33940, M08-D-VCG-01): the puffed-up community should have been mourning instead — the proper orientation is grief and correction, not any positive fullness.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5 is oriented entirely toward future humbling and desolation. Eze 33:28 (vc=33999, M08-E-VCG-01): "her proud might shall come to an end" — paired with total desolation of Israel's structural power. Lev 26:19 (vc=33982, M08-E-VCG-01): God will "break the pride of your power" — reversal as the structural future. Jer 51:53 (vc=65670, M08-E-VCG-02): "even if Babylon should mount up to heaven, and even if she should fortify her strong height, yet destroyers would come from me against her" — the highest possible structural power position has no positive eschatological future. Hab 2:9 (vc=34169, M08-E-VCG-02): "shame on him who builds his house by unjust gain, setting his nest on high to keep himself safe from the reach of harm!" — shame, not fullness, is the eschatological orientation.

---

#### T0.3 — Image-Bearer Expression

##### T0.3.1 — In what way does this characteristic express the divine image in the human person — what aspect of being made in God's likeness does it instantiate?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The verse evidence does not frame CHAR-1 as an expression of the divine image but as its distortion. The evidence that comes closest to addressing this is Eze 28:2 (vc=34040, M08-A1-VCG-02): the prince of Tyre's heart is proud and he claims "I am a god, I sit in the seat of the gods" — the divine-image capacity to stand before God and exercise authority over creation is here twisted into a claim to be God rather than a creature who bears God's image. Isa 14:13 (vc=34233, M08-A4-VCG-05): "You said in your heart, 'I will ascend to heaven; above the stars of God I will set my throne on high'" — the capacity of the human will to aspire and declare is directed against the divine order rather than within it. CHAR-1 instantiates the divine-image capacity for self-directed agency and aspiration, but misdirects it: the creature uses image-bearing capacity to claim the Creator's position.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 expresses the divine image not as a proper expression but as its distortion. The created capacity for volitional self-direction — which legitimately enables the human person to respond to God, exercise dominion, and act with agency — is here turned against God's own authority. Isa 13:11 (vc=34104, M08-B-VCG-02): "I will put an end to the pomp of the arrogant" — CHAR-2 is the image-bearing capacity for purposeful, energetic agency misdirected into self-assertion against the very author of that capacity. Psa 19:13 (vc=34095, M08-B-VCG-02): "keep back your servant also from presumptuous sins; let them not have dominion over me" — the psalmist names CHAR-2 as inner impulses that seek to "gain dominion" over the will, inverting the proper order in which the person exercises God-given dominion.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

CHAR-3 expresses the divine image through the created glorying-capacity — the human person's capacity to exult in, celebrate, and publicly affirm what they consider supreme. This capacity is genuine image-bearing: the human person, made to glorify God, possesses the faculty of glorying that is meant to overflow in God-directed praise (VCG-03). CHAR-3's VCG-01 form is this capacity misdirected: 1Cor 4:7 (vc=33871, M08-C-VCG-01) — the person who boasts as if they had not received their gifts is using the glorying-capacity to attribute to the self what should be attributed to God. The divine image's glorying-capacity is genuine; its self-direction is the distortion.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4 expresses the divine image through the created cognitive faculty's capacity for self-knowledge and self-assessment — which is here distorted into overclaiming. The human person, made with the capacity to know the self accurately in relation to God, uses that cognitive faculty to inflate the self beyond its actual measure. Rom 12:3 (vc=60866, M08-D-VCG-02): the commanded alternative ("sober judgment, each according to the measure of faith God has assigned") names the created-design expression of the same cognitive faculty — accurate self-knowledge within God-given parameters. CHAR-4 is the image-bearing cognitive capacity turned into false self-elevation.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5 expresses the divine image through the created capacity for strength, authority, and stewardship of power — which is here corrupted into self-exaltation. The human person, made to exercise God-delegated dominion over creation, possesses genuine power and authority as image-bearers. CHAR-5 is this legitimate delegated power claimed as self-generating and deployed for self-exaltation rather than God-honouring stewardship. Eze 28:5 (vc=34046, M08-E-VCG-02): "your heart became proud" because of wealth gained through wisdom — the wisdom and wealth were genuine image-bearing capacities; CHAR-5 is their corruption into the ground for arrogant self-elevation.

---

##### T0.3.2 — Does the evidence suggest that this characteristic is shared between God and the human person, or is it exclusively a creaturely analogue to something in God?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The evidence confirms CHAR-1 as exclusively creaturely, not shared with God. The 174 set-aside M22-register verses that carry the vocabulary of divine exaltation (rum, ga.on in the divine-majesty register) were excluded at Phase 5.5 precisely because they belong to God's own legitimate exaltation, not to CHAR-1. What remains in §3 is consistently the creature's movement against God's position: Psa 75:6–7 (vc=34301, vc=34230, M08-A4-VCG-05) — "not from the east or from the west... comes lifting up, but it is God who executes judgment, putting down one and lifting up another." This structural declaration excludes any human claim to self-elevation as legitimate: the creature does not share in the divine prerogative of exaltation. CHAR-1 is the creature reaching for what God alone holds, which confirms its exclusively creaturely character.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Exclusively creaturely. CHAR-2 requires an authority external to the self to defy — which by definition excludes God, who is himself that authority. The entire §3.A corpus positions CHAR-2 as transgression against God's commands (Deu 18:20, vc=34119), appointed authorities (Deu 17:12, vc=34110), and revealed law (Psa 119:21, vc=34098, M08-B-VCG-02: arrogant ones "wander from your commandments"). God establishes; CHAR-2 transgresses what God establishes. The relationship is structurally asymmetric, confirming CHAR-2 as exclusively creaturely.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

CHAR-3 in its condemned self-directed form is exclusively creaturely. God as the sole source of all good cannot engage in the misattribution that defines VCG-01 CHAR-3 (1Cor 4:7: boasting as if one had not received — inapplicable to God who receives nothing but is himself the source). However, the glorying-capacity that CHAR-3 distorts has a divine analogue: God delights in his own glory and directs his people to glory in him — the God-directed boasting of VCG-03 is a creaturely participation in the divine self-glorification that belongs properly to God. CHAR-3's condemned form is exclusively creaturely; the underlying capacity participates in something genuinely divine.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Exclusively creaturely. The inflation vocabulary (fusioō — to puff up; tufoō — to be swollen with conceit) names a gap between actual substance and claimed substance — like a balloon inflated beyond what it materially contains. God has no such gap; his cognitive self-assessment perfectly matches his actual being. The huperfroneō vocabulary (Rom 12:3, vc=60866: thinking more highly than warranted — huper + froneō: thinking above) presupposes a creaturely "warrant" that limits how highly one may think; God has no such limiting warrant from outside. CHAR-4 is structurally possible only for a creature whose actual measure is limited and God-assigned.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Exclusively creaturely. The ga.on proud-might vocabulary in its M08-E register names the creature's misuse of received power as the ground for self-exaltation. The 122 M22-register ga.on/rum verses (set aside at Phase 5.5) carry God's genuine power and might — that material belongs to M22, not CHAR-5. What remains in §3.D is the creature's claiming of structural power as a self-sufficient, self-exaltation ground. Isa 47:8 (vc=9563, M08-E-VCG-02): "I am, and there is no one besides me" — Babylon's power-based self-declaration claiming what belongs to God alone. CHAR-5 is exclusively creaturely: it is the creature claiming power-grounded self-sufficiency that only God actually possesses.

---

##### T0.3.3 — What does the presence or absence of this characteristic in a person reveal about the condition of the divine image in that person?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The evidence reveals that CHAR-1's presence marks the divine image in severe disorder. The most direct evidence is Luk 1:51 (vc=33930, M08-A1-VCG-03): God "has scattered the proud in the thoughts of their hearts" — the very thoughts of the heart, the inner person's deepest cognitive-volitional centre, are named as the site of arrogance. Psa 10:4 (vc=34074, M08-A2-VCG-02): "in the pride of his face the wicked does not seek him; all his thoughts are, 'there is no God'" — CHAR-1 produces functional atheism, the displacement of God from the inner horizon entirely, which is the divine image oriented away from its source and ground. Pro 16:5 (vc=12083, M08-A1-VCG-03): "everyone who is arrogant in heart is an abomination to the Lord" — the image-bearer's heart becomes what God finds most repugnant. Conversely, Psa 131:1 (vc=34059, vc=34224, M08-A1-VCG-03, M08-A2-VCG-01) evidences the alternative: the heart not lifted up and eyes not raised high as the image-bearing posture of creaturely lowliness before God.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2's presence reveals the divine image in a specific and severe disorder: the will — the faculty through which the image-bearer is meant to respond in obedience to divine direction — has turned against the divine authority it is meant to honour. Neh 9:16 (vc=34120, M08-B-VCG-01): "they acted presumptuously and stiffened their neck and did not obey your commandments" — the stiff neck and disobedience are the visible indicators of an image-bearing will that has inverted its proper orientation. 2Pe 2:10 (vc=42739, M08-B-VCG-03): "self-willed, they do not tremble before the glorious ones" — the absence of proper creaturely reverence before divine authority is the diagnostic marker of CHAR-2's presence; the image-bearing capacity for reverence is inverted into defiant self-assertion.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

CHAR-3's presence (VCG-01 self-directed form) reveals the divine image's glorying-capacity turned inward, making the self rather than God the object of exultation. 1Cor 1:29 (vc=33877, M08-C-VCG-01): God's design is to shut down human self-boasting "in the presence of God" — its presence before God is an image-disorder. Jam 4:16 (vc=33886, M08-C-VCG-01): boasting "in arrogance" is "evil" — the image-bearing capacity for public celebration of what is good is directed toward the self and judged as moral failure. The God-directed boasting of VCG-03 (Rom 5:2; 1Cor 1:31; Phili 3:3) evidences the restored image-bearing condition: the glorying-capacity is reoriented toward God and received goods.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4's presence reveals the divine image's cognitive faculty in specific disorder: the mind that should know itself accurately within God-given measure has instead constructed a false picture of itself inflated beyond that measure. 1Ti 6:4 (vc=33925, M08-D-VCG-02): conceit paired with "understanding nothing" — the inflated mind's actual cognitive condition is one of comprehensive blindness despite its self-image of competence. 1Ti 3:6 (vc=33924): the conceited person falls into "the condemnation of the devil" — the image-bearing cognitive faculty has been corrupted to the point of aligning with the adversarial paradigm case. CHAR-4's absence (sober judgment within God-assigned measure) reveals the cognitive faculty functioning as designed.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5's presence reveals the divine image's stewardship capacity corrupted into self-exaltation: the person or nation with real power uses that power to claim self-sufficiency and elevation above others, rather than employing it in God's service. Eze 16:49 (vc=33979, M08-E-VCG-01): Sodom's pride (CHAR-5 as root sin) is paired with failure to aid the poor and needy — the image-bearing capacity for using power in service of others has been inverted into its self-serving opposite. 1Ti 6:17 (vc=60878, M08-E-VCG-02): the wealthy warned against hupsēlofroneō — the image-bearer who stewards wealth well commands it toward generous good; CHAR-5 inverts this toward arrogant self-regard.

---

#### T0.4 — Typological Significance

##### T0.4.1 — Does Scripture use this characteristic typologically — deploying it to point toward or participate in a reality beyond the immediate (covenantal, eschatological, christological)?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Yes. The verse evidence carries typological deployment concentrated in two registers. First, the great-tree allegory of Eze 31: the towering cedar "whose heart was proud of its height" (vc=34048, vc=34078, vc=65799, M08-A1-VCG-02: Eze 31:10 through three terms — ga.vah, go.vah, rum) typologically represents Israel's kings and nations, and Eze 31:14 (vc=54400, M08-A3-VCG-04) generalises the judgment to all future aspiration to pride-elevation: "God's judgment is designed to prevent any future tree from aspiring to such elevation." Second, the day-of-the-Lord material: Isa 2:12 (vc=33957, M08-A3-VCG-04): "the Lord of hosts has a day against all that is proud and lofty" — CHAR-1 is deployed as the eschatological target of divine judgment, the characteristic whose universal humbling constitutes the eschatological reversal. The Isa 14:13 declaration (vc=34233, M08-A4-VCG-05) — "I will ascend to heaven; above the stars of God I will set my throne" — functions as the paradigm statement of CHAR-1's final form, typologically representing all creaturely self-elevation at its extreme.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The evidence carries typological deployment in two registers. First, the prophetic-historical type: Israel's repeated presumptuous defiance in the wilderness (Deu 1:43, vc=34123; Neh 9:16, vc=34120; Neh 9:29, vc=34126) functions as the paradigmatic case of CHAR-2 that is repeatedly referenced in later literature as the type of human self-will against divine authority. Second, the NT archō register: Mar 10:41–42 (vc=55587, vc=55588, M08-B-VCG-03) — Jesus' reference to rulers "who lord it over" and "who are great ones who exercise authority" — functions typologically as the pattern of CHAR-2 that servant-authority inverts. The domineering authority of the Gentiles is the typological negative that the servant model of Jesus displaces.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Yes. 1Cor 1:29–31 (vc=33877, vc=33878, M08-C-VCG-01/03) deploys the full typological structure: God's sovereign election of the weak is designed to eliminate human self-boasting, and this design finds its eschatological expression in the cross — "let the one who boasts, boast in the Lord." The cross functions typologically as CHAR-3's definitive counter: at the cross, all human achievement-boasting is structurally evacuated (the crucified Lord eliminates all human credential-ground — 2Cor 11:18/30; Gal 6:14). Gal 6:14 (vc=33869, M08-C-VCG-02): "may I never boast except in the cross of our Lord Jesus Christ, by which the world has been crucified to me, and I to the world" — the cross as the typological telos of the examined-boasting discourse.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Yes. 1Ti 3:6 (vc=33924, M08-D-VCG-02) contains the most direct typological reference in M08: the new convert who falls into CHAR-4 falls into "the condemnation of the devil" — the adversary's condemnation is named as the typological paradigm case of cognitive self-inflation beyond one's proper creaturely station. CHAR-4 is not merely a moral failure but a participation in the pattern of the adversarial figure's primordial cognitive overclaiming. This is unique within M08-CHAR-4: only this characteristic explicitly connects human pride to the adversarial prototype through a typological reference.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Yes. The Eze corpus provides the primary typological deployments. Eze 16:49 (vc=33979, M08-E-VCG-01): Sodom's CHAR-5 functions typologically as the paradigm case of structural power-and-ease becoming the ground for pride — "pride, excess of food and prosperous ease" as the root-sin sequence, referenced and re-applied in later literature. Eze 19:11 (vc=54398, M08-E-VCG-02): the towering vine-ruler whose height and visible dominance become the material for a lament — the typological deployment of structural height as pride's visible form. The ga.on proud-might corpus (Eze 30:6, 30:18, 32:12 — M08-E-VCG-01: Egypt's repeating proud-might) functions as a typological pattern: national structural power claiming self-sufficient might, repeatedly humbled by God's intervention.

---

##### T0.4.2 — If typological use is present, what is the direction of the typology — does the human instance point toward the divine, or does the divine instance establish the pattern for the human?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The direction runs from the human instance toward its eschatological reversal by the divine. The human instances of CHAR-1 (Babylon's pomp, vc=33988, M08-A3-VCG-02: "your pomp is brought down to Sheol"; the Assyrian king's boasting, vc=34599, M08-A1-VCG-02: "the arrogant heart of the king of Assyria"; the will's declaration in Isa 14:13, vc=34233, M08-A4-VCG-05) accumulate as participants in a pattern — all human self-elevation as a single phenomenon — whose final resolution is divine action on the day of the Lord. There is no divine instance establishing a positive pattern for the human to follow; the divine response to CHAR-1 is consistently opposition and reversal, not modelling. The typological direction is: human CHAR-1 → eschatological judgment → the Lord alone exalted.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The direction runs from the human-historical instances toward their eschatological judgment and their christological inversion. Israel's wilderness presumption (Deu 1:43; Neh 9:16) is the human-historical instance that participates in the pattern of all creaturely self-will against divine authority. The christological inversion (Mar 10:41–42; Mar 8:32, vc=55607 — Peter presuming to correct Jesus): human CHAR-2 is the pattern that Christ's servant-authority reverses, not by itself being an instance of CHAR-2 but by modelling its structural opposite. The typological direction is from human CHAR-2 instances toward christological counter-pattern.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

The direction runs from human self-boasting through the cross as counter to eschatological God-directed boasting as the restored end. CHAR-3's VCG-01 form (human self-boasting in wisdom, might, wealth) is the fallen starting point. The cross evacuates all such grounds (Gal 6:14; 1Cor 1:29–31) as the christological pivot. The VCG-03 end-point is eschatological God-directed glorying (1Th 2:19; Phili 2:16). The typology's direction: human self-boasting → cross-mediated evacuation → God-directed boasting as restored image-bearing. The direction is through the cross, not around it.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The direction runs from the adversarial paradigm case (the devil's original CHAR-4, implied in "the condemnation of the devil") downward to the human instance. The human CHAR-4 (the new convert's conceit) participates in the same pattern of cognitive self-inflation that the adversarial figure exemplifies — and will receive the same judgment ("condemnation"). The direction is: adversarial prototype → human participation in the same pattern → same condemnation.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

The direction is from the historical instances toward the structural pattern and its eschatological reversal. The repeated humbling of Egypt's proud might (Eze 30:6, 30:18, 32:12, 33:28) accumulates as a typological pattern: structural power-pride consistently → divine humbling → desolation. Isa 47:8 (vc=9563): Babylon's self-declaration ("I am, and there is no one besides me") participates in the same typological pattern — the creature claiming divine self-sufficiency. The typological direction is: historical power-pride instances → structural pattern of God's reversal → eschatological establishment of God alone as the ground of legitimate power.

---

##### T0.4.3 — If no typological use is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Typological use is evidenced across two registers (see T0.4.1): the Eze 31 great-tree allegory (vc=34048, vc=34078, vc=65799, vc=54399, vc=54400) and the day-of-the-Lord material (Isa 2:12, vc=33957; Isa 14:13, vc=34233). This prompt is closed by T0.4.1–2.

---

Typological use is evidenced in the wilderness-presumption historical type and the NT servant-authority counter-pattern (Mar 10:41–42, vc=55587/55588). This prompt is closed by T0.4.1–2.

## T1 — Description and Classification (24 prompts)

### T1

#### T1.1 — Name and Naming

##### T1.1.1 — What is this characteristic called in the programme — and what does the name itself signal about its essential nature?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The programme name is "Arrogant self-elevation." The name encodes three essential elements that the verse evidence directly substantiates. First, the direction: elevation — an upward movement, rooted in the spatial metaphor running through the Hebrew vocabulary (rum — to be high/to rise; ga.on — rising grandeur; ga.vah — to exalt/rise proudly) and the Greek (huperēfanos — appearing above; hupsēlos — high). Second, the agent: self — the inner person as the one doing the lifting, not receiving it from outside or from God; Psa 75:6 (vc=34301, M08-A4-VCG-05) — "not from the east or from the west... comes lifting up" — names the illegitimacy of self-directed elevation. Third, the mode: arrogant — the elevation is illicit, claimed rather than given, competing with what belongs to God alone. The name already distinguishes CHAR-1 from legitimate dignified standing (which the evidence is silent on as CHAR-1) and from God's genuine exaltation (M22, set aside at Phase 5.5).

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The programme name is "Presumptuous defiance." The name encodes two essential elements: (a) defiance — the characteristic is directed against an external authority (divinely-established limits, appointed persons, revealed commands); and (b) presumptuous — the will acts beyond what it has been authorised to claim, assuming a right or freedom it does not possess. The name distinguishes CHAR-2 from simple disobedience (which might be reluctant or passive) and from CHAR-1 (elevated self-regard): CHAR-2 is the active, forceful, deliberate assertion of the self against a specific known limit. The Hebrew root zid (boiling, seething) is directly encoded in "presumptuous" — the characteristic is not cool calculation but a will that boils over, as Deu 1:43 (vc=34123, M08-B-VCG-01) evidences: Israel "acted presumptuously and went up into the hill country" despite God's explicit prohibition.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

The programme name is "Boasting and self-display." The compound name encodes two registers: "boasting" names the speech-act dimension (the verbal assertion of one's own worth, achievement, or credentials — kauchaomai/ha.lal), and "self-display" names the visible/social presentation dimension (the public making-known of the self as worthy — alazoneia, alazōn). The name signals that CHAR-3 is constitutively public and external: unlike CHAR-1 (inner dispositional elevation) or CHAR-2 (volitional transgressive act), CHAR-3 moves into speech and social visibility. Jam 4:16 (vc=33886, M08-C-VCG-01): "you boast in your arrogance" — the arrogance (CHAR-1 substrate) finding verbal expression in boasting (CHAR-3).

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The programme name is "Vain conceit." "Conceit" names the cognitive register — a false mental conception of the self; "vain" names the emptiness of that conception — inflated without actual substance, as fusioō (to puff up) names the condition of being swollen beyond one's actual content. The name precisely targets CHAR-4's defining feature: a mind that has constructed an inaccurate, inflated picture of itself. The name distinguishes CHAR-4 from CHAR-1 (dispositional self-elevation), CHAR-2 (volitional transgression), and CHAR-3 (verbal self-display) — CHAR-4 is the inner cognitive form of pride. Rom 12:3 (vc=60866, M08-D-VCG-02): "do not think of yourself more highly than you ought" — huperfroneō names precisely this: thinking (froneō) above (huper) what is warranted.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

The programme name is "Pride of power and position." The name encodes the specific medium through which this form of pride operates: "power" names structural force (military might, physical strength, national capacity — the ga.on proud-might register), and "position" names social and material standing (wealth, fortified height, authority). Together they distinguish CHAR-5 from CHAR-1 (dispositional elevation), CHAR-2 (volitional defiance), CHAR-3 (verbal boasting), and CHAR-4 (cognitive conceit) — CHAR-5 is the structural-power register of pride. Lev 26:19 (vc=33982, M08-E-VCG-01): "the pride of your power" — the compound phrase is native to the evidence itself.

---

##### T1.1.2 — What do the primary Hebrew and Greek terms reveal at the definitional level — before deeper lexical analysis begins?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

At the definitional level, the primary terms converge on a single spatial-metaphorical core: upward movement of the self beyond proper station. Hebrew rum (H7311A) — to be high, to rise, to lift up — is the most voluminous term; its active form evidences the will's upward drive (Num 15:30, vc=65731, M08-A4-VCG-05: acting "with a high hand" as deliberate self-exaltation against God; Isa 14:13, vc=34233, M08-A4-VCG-05: "I will ascend to heaven"). Hebrew ga.vah (H1361) — to exalt, to rise proudly — is most closely associated with the heart-seat idiom (Eze 28:2, vc=34040, M08-A1-VCG-02: "your heart is proud"; 2Ch 26:16, vc=34044, M08-A1-VCG-01: "he grew proud"). Greek huperēfanos (G5244) — from huper (above) + phainomai (to appear) — names the person who presents themselves above others, adding a visible/social precision the Hebrew vocabulary does not emphasise (Luk 1:51, vc=33930, M08-A1-VCG-03: arrogance in "the thoughts of their hearts"; Jam 4:6, vc=33931, M08-A4-VCG-01: the inner stance that draws divine opposition). Before deeper analysis, the terms uniformly name: upward, self-directed, beyond proper creaturely limit.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The primary terms converge on a single core: forceful self-willed assertion against an external authority. Hebrew zid (H2102) — to boil, seethe; the root metaphor is of a liquid boiling over its container — the will exceeding the boundaries established by divine command. Deu 18:20 (vc=34119, M08-B-VCG-01): "the prophet who presumes [zid] to speak a word in my name that I have not commanded." Hebrew za.don (H2087) — insolence, presumptuousness — the quality that drives wilful transgression; Pro 13:10 (vc=34113, M08-B-VCG-02): "by insolence [za.don] comes nothing but strife." Hebrew zed (H2086) — the arrogant/insolent person who treats divine law with contempt; Psa 119:21 (vc=34098, M08-B-VCG-02): "you rebuke the insolent [zed], accursed ones, who wander from your commandments." Greek authadēs (G0829) — self-pleasing, self-willed, refusing to be constrained by others; Tit 1:7 (vc=42740, M08-B-VCG-03): an overseer must not be "self-willed [authadēs]." Greek tolmētēs (G5113) — one who dares recklessly; 2Pe 2:10 (vc=4670, M08-B-VCG-03): the "bold man" who does not tremble before glorious ones. All terms name the same inner reality from different angles: the will's self-authorised transgression.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Primary Hebrew terms: ha.lal (H1984H) in its self-directed boasting sense — the verb meaning to shine, to celebrate, to praise, used self-directedly as self-glorification; 1Ki 20:11 (vc=33353, M08-C-VCG-01): "let not him who puts on his armour boast like him who takes it off" — premature glorification before achievement is complete. Ro.hav (H7296): prideful excess — Psa 90:10 (vc=34222, M08-C-VCG-01): life's best span is "toil and trouble," undercutting the inner boast about its worth. Primary Greek terms: kauchaomai (G2744) — to boast, exult, glory; its noun forms kauchēma (G2745, the object or ground of boasting) and kauchēsis (G2746, the act of boasting); these span all three VCGs — the same terms cover condemned, examined, and God-directed registers. Alazoneia (G0212) and alazōn (G0213) — the inner boasting disposition and the boaster as a person-type (Jam 4:16, vc=33866; 1Jo 2:16, vc=33865; 2Ti 3:2, vc=33868; Rom 1:30, vc=33867).

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Three distinct Greek terms evidence the definitional dimensions. Fusioō (G5448) — to inflate, to puff up; the pneumatic metaphor of inflation (wind or air filling and expanding what was solid) names the absence of actual substance beneath the self-inflation. 1Cor 8:1 (vc=33935, M08-D-VCG-01): "knowledge puffs up [fusioō], but love builds up" — inflation as the cognitive response to received knowledge without the relational anchor of love. Tufoō (G5187) — to be wrapped in smoke, to be puffed up with conceit; the smoke metaphor names cognitive obscuring — the mind clouded so that it cannot see clearly. 1Ti 6:4 (vc=33925, M08-D-VCG-02): conceit paired with "understanding nothing." Huperfroneō (G5252) — to think above (huper + froneō) what is warranted; Rom 12:3 (vc=60866, M08-D-VCG-02): "do not think of yourself more highly than you ought, but think with sober judgment." All three terms name the same cognitive register through different metaphors: inflation (fusioō), smoke-obscuration (tufoō), and above-measure thinking (huperfroneō).

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Six distinct terms constitute CHAR-5's vocabulary. Ga.on (H1347) in the proud-might subset — national pride/power/might as inner confidence: Eze 30:6 (vc=33996, M08-E-VCG-01): "Egypt's proud might" — the nation's structural power generating collective inner pride. Hupsēlofroneō (G5309) — wealth-pride, literally "high-mindedness about riches": 1Ti 6:17 (vc=60878, M08-E-VCG-02): "not to be haughty [hupsēlofroneō]" for those who are wealthy. Ga.vah (H1361) — to be proud/exalted: Eze 28:5 (vc=34046, M08-E-VCG-02): "your heart became proud [ga.vah]" through wealth. Shal.le.tet (H7986) — imperious self-will: Eze 16:30 (vc=57959, M08-E-VCG-02): "impetuousness is located in the heart." A.din (H5719) — voluptuous ease/self-indulgence: Isa 47:8 (vc=9563, M08-E-VCG-02): Babylon's love of pleasures as the inner ground for self-sufficiency declaration. Ma.rom (H4791) — height, lofty place used as a power-strategy: Jer 49:16 (vc=34167, M08-E-VCG-02): physical height as the proud heart's false security. All terms name the same inner reality: structural goods (strength, wealth, height, ease) misused as the ground for proud self-sufficiency.

---

##### T1.1.3 — Does the name carry directional, relational, or constitutional implications that orient the enquiry from the outset?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The name carries all three. Directional: the characteristic moves upward — Deu 17:20 (vc=34231, M08-A1-VCG-01): "his heart may not be lifted up above his brothers"; Dan 11:36 (vc=34235, M08-A1-VCG-02): the king "exalts himself and magnifies himself above every god." The direction is constitutively comparative — elevation is always elevation over someone or something. Relational: the upward movement is measured against God and other human beings simultaneously; Psa 138:6 (vc=12086, vc=34300, M08-A4-VCG-02) evidences the relational consequence: "the haughty he knows from afar" — divine relational distance as the structural outcome. Constitutional: the evidence immediately locates CHAR-1 in the heart (Pro 16:5, vc=12083, M08-A1-VCG-03: "arrogant in heart"), the spirit (Pro 16:18, vc=34073, M08-A1-VCG-03: "haughty spirit"), and the eyes/posture (Pro 6:17, vc=34247, M08-A2-VCG-01: "haughty eyes") — pointing to a characteristic that penetrates to the deepest constitutional levels of the person.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The name carries all three. Directional: CHAR-2 moves against — against the authority that established the limit, against the command that defined it. Deu 1:43 (vc=34123, M08-B-VCG-01): "you acted presumptuously and went up" — the movement is upward and against despite divine prohibition. Relational: CHAR-2 requires a relational other (God, appointed authority, revealed law) against whom to assert; it is inherently comparative and oppositional. Psa 86:14 (vc=34097, M08-B-VCG-02): "the insolent have risen up against me, a band of ruthless men seek my life; they do not set God before them." Constitutional: the zid/zed/za.don vocabulary roots CHAR-2 in the will — the volitional faculty, not the affective or cognitive. It is an act of the will's self-assertion more than a felt impulse or a cognitive error.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

The name carries directional and relational implications. Directional: "boasting" is always about something — the direction of the boast determines its legitimacy. Jer 9:23 (vc=33342, M08-C-VCG-01) identifies three wrong directions (wisdom, might, wealth) that imply one right direction (knowing God). The kauchaomai family inherits this directional structure — the same verb boasting toward self (VCG-01), toward God (VCG-03), or toward legitimate examined grounds (VCG-02). Relational: boasting/self-display requires an audience — CHAR-3 is constitutively social; it is performed for others' reception. Pro 25:14 (vc=33358, M08-C-VCG-01): boasting of a gift never given — the gift-claim is for social consumption and produces nothing. Constitutional: alazoneia (Jam 4:16, vc=33866; 1Jo 2:16, vc=33865) names the inner disposition that generates the boasting act.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The name carries constitutional implications primarily. "Conceit" locates the characteristic in the cognitive faculty — the mind's self-assessment function. Rom 12:3 (vc=60866, M08-D-VCG-02): "think of yourself" — the froneō root directly addresses the thinking/mind faculty. The constitutional implication is that CHAR-4 operates at the mind/cognitive level rather than the heart/volitional level (CHAR-1/2) or the speech/social level (CHAR-3). Relational implications: 1Cor 13:4 (vc=33936, M08-D-VCG-01): "love is not arrogant [fusioō]" — CHAR-4 is relationally incompatible with love; the inflated cognitive self-picture displaces the other-oriented cognition that love requires.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

The name carries relational and constitutional implications. Relational: "power and position" are inherently relational — they are defined relative to others (power over others; position above others). Eze 16:49 (vc=33979, M08-E-VCG-01): Sodom's CHAR-5 is evidenced by failure to aid the poor — the structural superiority expressed in contempt and neglect of the vulnerable. Constitutional: the ga.on proud-might vocabulary names both the structural external power and the inner confidence that rests on it — CHAR-5 is constitutionally anchored in the heart (Eze 28:5 — heart proud; Eze 16:30 — impetuousness in the heart) even though its medium is external structural goods.

---

#### T1.2 — Kind

##### T1.2.1 — What kind of inner-being phenomenon does this characteristic appear to be — an act, a disposition, a condition, a quality, or something else?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

CHAR-1 is primarily a disposition — a settled inner orientation of the self toward its own elevation — that also takes act-forms and expresses outwardly as a condition. The dispositional classification is directly evidenced: Dan 4:37 (vc=34094, M08-A4-VCG-04): "those who walk in pride" — pride as a habitual gait, a settled mode of moving through life; Isa 16:6 (vc=33943, M08-A4-VCG-04): "how proud he is" — pride as a known, reported stable characteristic; Pro 16:5 (vc=12083, M08-A1-VCG-03): "everyone who is arrogant in heart" — a constitutive inner quality. The act-form is also evidenced: Num 15:30 (vc=65731, M08-A4-VCG-05): acting "with a high hand" — a specific volitional episode; 1Ki 11:26 (vc=34237, M08-A1-VCG-02): "lifted up his hand against the king" — a singular act of self-assertion. The disposition precedes and generates the acts; the wisdom corpus (Pro 16:18, vc=34073, M08-A1-VCG-03; Pro 16:5, vc=12083) treats CHAR-1 as a stable inner characteristic with predictable causal consequences, not as a momentary state.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 is primarily an act-form (the volitional act of transgressing a known limit) with a dispositional substrate that generates and sustains it. The act-form evidence: Deu 1:43 (vc=34123, M08-B-VCG-01) — "you acted presumptuously and went up" — a specific transgressive episode; Deu 18:20 (vc=34119) — "the prophet who presumes to speak" — a specific wilful speech-act. The dispositional substrate evidence: Pro 21:24 (vc=34096, vc=34114, M08-B-VCG-02) — "haughty, arrogant, 'scoffer' is his name; he acts with arrogant pride [za.don]" — za.don as the settled characteristic of the scoffer; Eze 7:10 (vc=34118, M08-B-VCG-02): arrogance "has blossomed, pride has budded" — dispositional growth imagery. CHAR-2 is primarily a characteristic of the act-register (distinct from CHAR-1's dispositional register), but sustained acts of presumptuous defiance generate the za.don dispositional identity evidenced in the scoffer.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

CHAR-3 is primarily a communicative/expressive act (the speech-act of boasting and the social act of self-display) with a dispositional substrate (alazoneia — the inner boasting-orientation). The act-form dominates: the kauchaomai vocabulary is primarily verbal — to boast, to exult in, to commend oneself. Jam 4:16 (vc=33886, M08-C-VCG-01): "you boast in your arrogance. All such boasting is evil" — the boasting is the act; the arrogance is its source (CHAR-1 as substrate). The dispositional substrate: alazoneia (1Jo 2:16, vc=33865, M08-C-VCG-01): "the pride of life [alazoneia] is not from the Father but is from the world" — an inner orientation that generates the boasting act. CHAR-3 is the verbal/public expression of CHAR-1's inner elevation.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4 is primarily a cognitive/epistemic phenomenon — a false, inflated inner mental assessment of the self. This distinguishes it from CHAR-1 (dispositional), CHAR-2 (volitional-transgressive), and CHAR-3 (communicative/expressive). Rom 12:3 (vc=60866, M08-D-VCG-02): the command addresses the thinking faculty directly — froneō (to think, to set the mind). 1Ti 6:4 (vc=33925, M08-D-VCG-02): conceit and "understanding nothing" paired — CHAR-4 is a cognitive condition producing cognitive failure. Col 2:18 (vc=33941, M08-D-VCG-01): "inflated [fusioō] by his sensuous mind" — the mind itself is named as the seat of the inflation.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5 is primarily a dispositional state — the inner arrogance and self-confidence that structural power generates and sustains. The ga.on proud-might vocabulary names both the inner disposition (pride as an inner state) and its structural basis (might/power/strength). Lev 26:19 (vc=33982, M08-E-VCG-01): "the pride of your power" — pride (ga.on) is the inner state; power is its ground. Eze 28:5 (vc=34046, M08-E-VCG-02): "your heart became proud" — the dispositional elevation is explicitly named as the characteristic, with wealth as its generating condition. CHAR-5 is a settled inner posture of power-grounded self-sufficiency and contempt for others, sustained by structural goods.

---

##### T1.2.2 — Is this characteristic simple in structure or does it appear to have constituent elements at first encounter?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

CHAR-1 is complex in structure. The seat-of-pride axis that generated the four sub-groups (M08-A1 through M08-A4) is itself evidence of internal differentiation within a single characteristic: the same inner movement of self-elevation is named through the heart (Pro 16:5, vc=12083, M08-A1-VCG-03: "arrogant in heart"), the eyes (Pro 6:17, vc=34247, M08-A2-VCG-01: "haughty eyes"), the national/collective register (Isa 16:6, vc=33989, M08-A3-VCG-01: "we have heard of the pride of Moab"), and the general dispositional form (Pro 16:18, vc=34073; Rom 1:30, vc=33932, M08-A4-VCG-01). Within the sub-groups, further constituent registers appear: prosperity-triggered elevation (M08-A1-VCG-01: Deu 8:14, Hos 13:6), royal power elevation (M08-A1-VCG-02: Eze 28:2, Dan 11:36), volitional self-assertion against God (M08-A4-VCG-05: Isa 14:13, Num 15:30), and the self-love root that generates the whole (M08-A4-VCG-01: 2Ti 3:2, vc=1899: filautos). CHAR-1 has constituent elements — triggers, sub-registers, and generative roots — while remaining a single characteristic identity.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 has constituent elements differentiated by direction of transgression and vocabulary register. Three registers are evidenced: (a) M08-B-VCG-01 (9 verses) — the zid-boiling register: direct presumptuous defiance of a named divine command or prohibition (Deu 1:43; Deu 18:20; Neh 9:10/16/29); (b) M08-B-VCG-02 (25 verses) — the zed/za.don insolence register: contemptuous disregard for divine law, appointed authority, and revealed truth, generating social insolence and relational aggression (Psa 119 corpus, Pro 11:2, Pro 13:10, Jer 50:31); (c) M08-B-VCG-03 (11 verses) — the NT self-willed/presumptuous-daring register: authadēs (self-willed dismissal of legitimate constraint), tolmētēs (reckless presumption before divine beings), archō M08-relational verses (domineering authority-assertion in narrative). These are constituent registers within a single characteristic — all involving the will asserting itself against a known limit — not separate characteristics.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

CHAR-3 has significant internal complexity due to its three-VCG structure. M08-C-VCG-01 (26 verses, condemned self-boasting): ha.lal self-directed, alazoneia, condemned kauchaomai uses — the straightforwardly fallen form. M08-C-VCG-02 (21 verses, Pauline examined boasting discourse): 2Cor 10–12 corpus — boasting examined, bounded, and redirected; legitimate within God-assigned spheres; CHAR-3's impulse subjected to discernment. M08-C-VCG-03 (23 verses, God-directed boasting): kauchaomai directed wholly toward God, relational commendation, eschatological confidence — the redeemed form. The three VCGs represent three registers of the same underlying impulse-to-glory: fallen-misdirected (VCG-01), examined-redirected (VCG-02), redeemed-God-directed (VCG-03).

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4 has constituent elements across two VCGs. M08-D-VCG-01 (7 verses): intellectual/partisan conceit — inflation through received knowledge (1Cor 8:1, vc=33935), partisan attachment to leaders (1Cor 4:6, vc=33937), contemptuous confidence toward an absent authority (1Cor 4:18, vc=33938), inappropriate ease before community moral failure (1Cor 5:2, vc=33940), ungrounded spiritual-experience inflation (Col 2:18, vc=33941). M08-D-VCG-02 (5 verses): miscalibrated self-assessment — overreaching the measure of faith (Rom 12:3, vc=60866), leadership-conceit leading to judgment (1Ti 3:6, vc=33924), truth-blinding conceit (1Ti 6:4, vc=33925), end-times character conceit (2Ti 3:4, vc=33926), relational-disorder conceit (2Cor 12:20, vc=33942). Both VCGs involve inflated cognitive self-assessment; the constituent difference is the occasion of inflation and its primary expression.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5 has constituent elements across two VCGs. M08-E-VCG-01 (8 verses): national proud-might — collective structural power (military, national, institutional) generating collective inner pride (Lev 26:19; Eze 7:24; 16:49; 24:21; 30:6; 30:18; 32:12; 33:28). M08-E-VCG-02 (9 verses): wealth, position, and self-secured elevation — material prosperity, fortified height, and ease as individual or national grounds for pride (Isa 47:8; Jer 49:16; Jer 51:53; Eze 16:30; Eze 19:11; Eze 28:5; Obd 3; Hab 2:9; 1Ti 6:17). Both VCGs evidence the same inner-dynamic (structural goods → inner arrogance) through different structural media (national military might vs wealth/height/position).

---

##### T1.2.3 — What is the current best working description of this characteristic — encapsulating its constitutional location, the faculties it primarily engages, and its impact on the person?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Arrogant self-elevation is the constitutive inner movement in which the self — located primarily in the heart (M08-A1: Pro 16:5, vc=12083; Eze 28:2, vc=34040) but also manifesting through the eyes and posture (M08-A2: Pro 6:17, vc=34247; Pro 30:13, vc=34249) and attributable to nations and collectives (M08-A3: Isa 16:6, vc=33989; Hos 5:5, vc=34000) — lifts itself above its proper creaturely station before God and others, claiming standing, honour, or status that does not belong to it. It operates as a settled disposition (Dan 4:37, vc=34094: "those who walk in pride") that is generated by a self-love root (2Ti 3:2, vc=1899: filautos) and activated by prosperity, power, beauty, or achievement (Deu 8:14, vc=34223; 2Ch 26:16, vc=34044; Eze 28:17, vc=34047). Its primary impact is forgetfulness of God (Hos 13:6, vc=34232: "their heart was lifted up; therefore they forgot me"), corruption of wisdom (Eze 28:17, vc=34047), and progression toward collapse (Pro 16:18, vc=34073: "pride goes before destruction").

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Presumptuous defiance is the inner-being state in which the will — located constitutionally in the volitional faculty and expressed through the stiff-necked refusal to submit — asserts itself against known divinely-established limits, appointed human authority, or revealed divine commands with a boiling-over force. It is the volitional/active form of pride: where CHAR-1 elevates the self in disposition, CHAR-2 activates that elevation as a deliberate transgression of a specific boundary. Primary vocabulary: zid (the boiling-over internal force of the transgressive will), za.don (the insolent inner quality that characterises the habitual defier), zed (the person-type of arrogant law-contempt). It generates predictable consequences: disgrace (Pro 11:2, vc=34109, M08-B-VCG-02), strife (Pro 13:10, vc=34113), and eschatological destruction (Mal 4:1, vc=34107, M08-B-VCG-02).

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Boasting and self-display is the inner impulse to self-glorify through words, visible claims, and public assertion of one's own worth, achievement, credentials, or future plans — the outward/verbal expression of CHAR-1's inner elevation. The characteristic spans three registers evidenced in §3.B: (a) condemned self-directed boasting in creaturely assets (Jer 9:23, vc=33342; 1Jo 2:16, vc=33865; Jam 4:16, vc=33886); (b) the Pauline examined-boasting discourse — the same impulse subjected to theological examination within apostolic ministry (2Cor 10–12, M08-C-VCG-02); (c) God-directed boasting as the redeemed form — the glorying-impulse wholly redirected to God, received goods, and the community of faith (Rom 5:2, vc=33874; 1Cor 1:31, vc=33878; Phili 3:3, vc=33879). Primary vocabulary: kauchaomai/kauchēma/kauchēsis family (Greek), ha.lal self-directed (Hebrew), alazoneia/alazōn (inner boasting disposition).

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Vain conceit is pride operating specifically in the cognitive faculty as a false, inflated self-assessment — the mind's wrong picture of itself that produces blindness to truth (1Ti 6:4, vc=33925: understanding nothing), fuels controversy and relational disorder (1Ti 6:4: craving for controversy; 2Cor 12:20, vc=33942: fusiōsis among relational sins), generates communal dysfunction (1Cor 4:6, vc=33937: partisan inflation; 1Cor 5:2, vc=33940: puffed-up community), and causes the person to claim resources, status, or recognition beyond what is warranted (Rom 12:3, vc=60866: thinking beyond one's measure of faith). Vocabulary: fusioō (inflated without factual basis), tufoō (puffed up with smoke-like conceit), fusiōsis (conceit generating communal disorder), huperfroneō (thinking above what is warranted).

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Pride of power and position is the inner arrogance that arises when strength, social authority, material prosperity, or national might becomes the ground for self-exaltation and contemptuous elevation above others — pride expressed through a specific medium.
