Second, self-assessment: Rom 12:16 (vc=60877, M08-A4-VCG-01) — "never be wise in your own sight" — pride produces an inflated and inaccurate self-assessment; 1Sa 2:3 (vc=12084, M08-A4-VCG-05) — "the Lord is a God of knowledge, and by him actions are weighed" — pride misjudges its own standing before the divine cognitive standard. The impairment is not of all cognition but of the self-directed cognitive assessment that would give the person an accurate picture of where they stand before God and others.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 impairs cognition through self-deception: Obd 3 (vc=34108, M08-B-VCG-02) and Jer 49:16 (vc=34115) both name deception as the cognitive consequence — the person genuinely believes they are secure or right when they are not. Mal 3:15 (vc=34106, M08-B-VCG-02): the arrogant "seem to prosper" — an inverted cognitive evaluation of moral-consequential reality. Luk 3:8 (vc=55578, M08-B-VCG-03): the cognitive claim "we have Abraham as our father" is a self-justifying miscalculation of one's standing before God.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

CHAR-3 impairs cognition through: (a) attribution failure — 1Cor 4:7 (vc=33871): misattributing received goods as self-generated; (b) self-comparison distortion — 2Cor 10:12: "without understanding" — the self-comparison process generates a cognitive picture of the self that lacks genuine understanding. For VCG-02 examined boasting: 2Cor 1:12 (vc=33912, M08-C-VCG-02): conscience's testimony as the cognitive ground of legitimate self-commendation — conscience-based cognition enables accurate examined boasting.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4 impairs cognition in two specific registers: (a) Self-knowledge — Rom 12:3 (vc=60866): thinking above one's warranted measure; (b) General epistemic capacity — 1Ti 6:4 (vc=33925): "understanding nothing" — the inflation corrupts the entire cognitive apparatus so that nothing is accurately understood. The impairment is self-reinforcing: the inflated self-picture is generated by the cognitive faculty, and then that same inflated picture corrupts the cognitive faculty's operation for all subsequent assessment.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5 impairs cognition through self-deception: Obd 3 (vc=65674): "the pride of your heart has deceived you" — the cognitive assessment of invulnerability is a deception; the person's actual vulnerability before God is the reality that CHAR-5's cognitive inflation conceals. Isa 47:8 (vc=9563): the self-sufficiency claim ("I am, and there is no one besides me") is cognitively false — Babylon's structural power is finite and reversible, but CHAR-5 generates a cognitive picture of ontological self-completeness.

---

##### T3.2.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with cognition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The pattern confirms that CHAR-1 is a cognitively distorting characteristic — it does not merely feel wrong or orient wrong, it thinks wrong. The proud person constructs a cognitive picture of themselves (above God, above others) that is systematically at variance with reality as God assesses it. Luk 1:51 (vc=33930, M08-A1-VCG-03) — arrogance as the structured pattern of thought "in the thoughts of their hearts" — confirms that CHAR-1 is not an impulse but a cognitive framework through which the proud person processes reality. Eze 28:17 (vc=34047) shows the consequence of this cognitive distortion: wisdom is corrupted, leading to decisions that are objectively destructive. This cognitive self-distortion is what makes CHAR-1 systemically self-defeating: the proud person cannot accurately predict their own consequences because their cognitive framework is built around a false self-elevation.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The pattern reveals that CHAR-2's cognitive distortion is specifically self-protective: it produces the false confidence (Obd 3; Jer 49:16) that enables the will to act presumptuously without internal resistance. The cognitive miscalculation is functional for CHAR-2 — it allows the will to proceed without the corrective brake that accurate self-assessment would provide. CHAR-2 weaponises self-deception in service of transgression.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

CHAR-3's cognitive pattern reveals that the characteristic is constitutively about self-assessment: what one believes about oneself generates what one boasts about. CHAR-3's condemned form requires cognitive misattribution (self-generated rather than received); its examined form requires cognitive accuracy (conscience-grounded assessment); its God-directed form requires cognitive redirection (knowing God, not self, as the object of glory — Jer 9:23, vc=33342, M08-C-VCG-01 negative; Jer 9:24 positive implied).

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The cognitive pattern reveals that CHAR-4 is a uniquely cognitive form of self-corruption: it uses the mind's self-assessment faculty to generate a false picture, and then that false picture corrupts all subsequent cognitive function. 1Ti 6:4 (vc=33925): the terminal state of sustained CHAR-4 is comprehensive epistemic blindness ("understanding nothing") — confirming that the cognitive self-corruption is progressive and comprehensive.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5's cognitive pattern reveals that structural power generates the most extreme form of cognitive self-deception: not merely self-inflation (CHAR-4's fusioō) but ontological self-declaration ("I am, and there is no one besides me" — Isa 47:8, vc=9563). The structural goods (wealth, power, fortification) provide the material basis for the cognitive self-assessment, making it feel more evidenced than CHAR-4's ungrounded inflation — but the evidence is ultimately false, as God's judgment consistently demonstrates.

---

#### T3.3 — Memory

##### T3.3.1 — Does this characteristic engage the memory faculty — the holding and retrieving of inner-being reality across time — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Yes, primarily by disabling specific memory. Deu 8:14 (vc=34223, M08-A1-VCG-01): "your heart will be lifted up and you forget the Lord your God who brought you out of the land of Egypt, out of the house of slavery" — the heart-lift directly produces forgetfulness of God's redemptive history; the memory of divine provision and deliverance is the specific content that CHAR-1 displaces. Hos 13:6 (vc=34232, M08-A1-VCG-01): "when they had grazed, they became full, they were filled, and their heart was lifted up; therefore they forgot me" — the same sequence: prosperity → heart lifted → God forgotten. 2Ch 32:25 (vc=34045, M08-A1-VCG-01): "Hezekiah's heart was proud rather than grateful — inner self-exaltation displaced proper thankfulness for divine benefit" — CHAR-1 displaces the memory-sustained gratitude that divine benefit should generate.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Yes. The Neh 9 corpus (vc=34125, vc=34120, vc=34126, M08-B-VCG-01) evidences the specific memory failure that characterises CHAR-2 at the communal level: Israel "acted presumptuously" despite the memory of God's prior redemptive acts (Neh 9:10: "you performed signs and wonders") and prior covenant commands. The repeated pattern ("even after warnings, they acted presumptuously again" — Neh 9:29) confirms that CHAR-2 operates despite available memory of divine action, not in its absence.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Yes, partially. 1Ki 20:11 (vc=33353, M08-C-VCG-01): "let not him who puts on his armour boast like him who takes it off" — premature boasting involves forgetting (or ignoring) that the outcome is not yet achieved; the memory of past uncertainties would prevent the boast. 1Cor 4:7 (vc=33871): boasting "as if you did not receive it" — the memory of the reception of one's goods (and their source) is precisely what the boaster has failed to hold. CHAR-3 in its VCG-01 form operates by setting aside the memory of received goods and uncertain futures.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (S)

The verse evidence in §3.C is silent on CHAR-4 engaging the memory faculty. No verse addresses memory retention or forgetfulness in relation to vain conceit. The epistemic failure of 1Ti 6:4 ("understanding nothing") may imply a form of active non-retention, but this is not explicitly evidenced.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (S)

The verse evidence in §3.D is largely silent on CHAR-5 engaging the memory faculty directly. The closest evidence is the general pattern of CHAR-1's memory-displacement (forgetting God after prosperity), which CHAR-5 participates in through the ease/prosperity trigger, but §3.D does not explicitly name forgetting in relation to CHAR-5 specifically.

---

##### T3.3.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair memory in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

CHAR-1 impairs a specific class of memory: the memory of God's provision and redemptive action. Deu 8:14 (vc=34223, M08-A1-VCG-01) is the paradigm: prosperity activates CHAR-1, and CHAR-1 produces forgetfulness of what God has done. Hos 13:6 (vc=34232, M08-A1-VCG-01) confirms the causal chain: fullness → lifted heart → forgetting God. The impairment appears selective — CHAR-1 disables the memory of received divine benefit while the proud person presumably retains memory of their own achievement. This selective memory-impairment enables the cognitive reattribution pattern noted in T3.2: goods received from God are cognitively reassigned as self-generated, which requires not remembering their divine origin. CHAR-1 thus weaponises selective forgetting in the service of the self-exaltation project.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 bypasses memory — it acts despite what is remembered, not because memory is absent. Neh 9:16 (vc=34120, M08-B-VCG-01): the ancestors who "acted presumptuously" had the memory of God's deliverance from Egypt (Neh 9:9–15 context); the presumption overrides the memory-generated obligation to obedience. CHAR-2 does not erase memory (unlike CHAR-1's forgetfulness of God) but overrides the moral weight that memory should carry. The will's self-assertion bypasses the memory's corrective function.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

CHAR-3 bypasses the memory of two specific realities: (a) the received quality of one's goods (1Cor 4:7 — "you did not receive it" forgotten); (b) the uncertainty of future outcomes (Pro 27:1, vc=33359: "do not boast about tomorrow" — the memory that tomorrow's outcome is unknowable is overridden by the boast's certainty-claim). These bypasses are functional for CHAR-3: if the boaster remembered that their goods were received and the future is uncertain, the boast could not proceed.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (S)

Silent. No evidence in §3.C on CHAR-4's relationship to the memory faculty.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (S)

Silent within §3.D specifically. See T3.3.1.

---

##### T3.3.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with memory reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The pattern reveals that CHAR-1 has a constitutive relationship with memory: it specifically disables the memory of divine provision. This is analytically significant because it names the mechanism through which CHAR-1 sustains itself: the lifted heart forgets God (Deu 8:14, vc=34223), and in forgetting God it loses the corrective frame that would place the self in its proper creaturely station. Gratitude — which depends on remembering what was received and from whom — is displaced (2Ch 32:25, vc=34045). Without gratitude, the self's achievements and blessings appear self-generated, which reinforces the self-elevation. CHAR-1 is thus memory-parasitic: it sustains itself by disabling the very memory that would undercut it.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2's relationship to memory is distinct from CHAR-1's: where CHAR-1 erases the memory of divine provision (Deu 8:14: "you will forget the Lord"), CHAR-2 overrides what is remembered. The Neh 9 pattern shows a community that repeatedly transgresses despite remembered covenant history — CHAR-2 is not ignorance but wilful override of known obligation. This makes CHAR-2 more explicitly culpable than mere forgetfulness: the person or community acts against what they know.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

CHAR-3's relationship to memory confirms its cognitive-distortion character: it requires selective amnesia (forgetting the received quality of goods and future uncertainty) to sustain its self-glorifying content. This connects CHAR-3 to CHAR-1's forgetfulness-of-God pattern (T3.3 in CHAR-1 findings): the broader self-elevation generates forgetfulness of God (CHAR-1), and its verbal expression (CHAR-3) generates forgetfulness of the received quality of goods and uncertain futures.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (S)

The silence on memory in CHAR-4 confirms that CHAR-4's primary register is synchronic (the current cognitive self-picture) rather than diachronic (memory-held identity). CHAR-4 is about the present false self-assessment, not the displacement of past memories.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (S)

The silence on explicit memory-engagement in §3.D may reflect CHAR-5's focus on the present structural condition (current power, current wealth, current fortification) rather than on temporal retrospection. CHAR-5's cognitive confidence is based on present structural goods, not on remembered past goods.

---

#### T3.4 — Affect

##### T3.4.1 — Does this characteristic engage the affective faculty — feeling and emotional experience — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The verse evidence engages affect primarily from the perspective of those who encounter CHAR-1's contempt, not from the perspective of the proud person's own felt experience. Psa 123:4 (vc=33953, M08-A4-VCG-03): "our soul has had more than enough of the scorn of those who are at ease, of the contempt of the proud" — the victim's inner experience of CHAR-1 is one of overwhelming affective saturation under contempt. Psa 13:2 (vc=34241, M08-A4-VCG-03): the enemy's exaltation produces "sorrow in my heart all the day" in the psalmist. Jer 13:17 (vc=34091, M08-A3-VCG-03): "my soul will weep in secret for your pride" — the observer's affective response is grief. From within the proud person's own register, Psa 73:6 (vc=33959, M08-A2-VCG-02) — "pride is their necklace" — suggests the proud person carries their arrogance as an ornament, implying a degree of satisfaction or pleasure in the display, but the evidence does not name a felt emotional state explicitly.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The zid vocabulary carries an affective dimension in its root meaning: boiling, seething — the metaphor implies an inner agitation or heat that propels the will's transgression. Exo 18:11 (vc=34121, M08-B-VCG-01): "Egypt's arrogant dealing with Israel is described with a term for boiling insolence" — the affective quality is heated intensity of inner arrogance. 2Pe 2:10 (vc=4670, M08-B-VCG-03): the "bold man" who is "bold in blasphemy" carries an affective register of reckless daring that the tolmētēs root names.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Yes. 2Cor 7:4 (vc=33917, M08-C-VCG-03): "I am overflowing with joy in all our affliction" — the affective experience of boasting/glorying in the community is joy overflowing even amid suffering; the God-directed boasting of VCG-03 has a direct and evidenced affective dimension of joy. Rom 5:2–3 (vc=33874, vc=33875, M08-C-VCG-03): "we rejoice in hope of the glory of God... we rejoice in our sufferings" — the examined kauchaomai is paired with rejoicing. For VCG-01: the boasting of Pro 20:14 (vc=33357) — buyer boasting of a bargain — implies satisfaction; the inner pleasure of self-glorification is the characteristic's affective reward.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Yes, by displacing appropriate affect. 1Cor 5:2 (vc=33940, M08-D-VCG-01): "you are arrogant [fusioō]. Ought you not rather to mourn?" — CHAR-4 prevents the appropriate affective response (grief over a community moral failure) that the situation demands. The puffed-up cognitive self-picture produces a sense of superiority that displaces the grief that accurate self-assessment (of the community's actual moral state) would generate.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Yes. Isa 47:8 (vc=9563, M08-E-VCG-02): a.din (voluptuous ease, self-indulgence) — the affective register of sensory pleasure and ease is explicitly named as the inner companion of CHAR-5's self-declaration. Eze 16:49 (vc=33979, M08-E-VCG-01): "prosperous ease" (shalvah) paired with Sodom's pride — the affective experience of ease and material comfort is the companion-condition of power-pride. CHAR-5 is distinctively connected to affective ease and pleasure as the felt inner condition that sustains and reinforces the proud self-sufficiency claim.

---

##### T3.4.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair affect in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The evidence is primarily focused on CHAR-1's affective impact on others: crushing contempt (Psa 123:4, vc=33953, M08-A4-VCG-03), oppressive dominance producing sorrow (Psa 13:2, vc=34241), sustained trampling (Psa 56:2, vc=34163, M08-A4-VCG-03: "my enemies trample on me all day long, for many attack me proudly"). Within the proud person, the evidence does not directly address whether CHAR-1 enables or impairs their own affective faculty. Job 41:34 (vc=34614, M08-A4-VCG-04) — Leviathan reigns over "sons of pride" whose defining inner trait is "fierce, fearless self-assertion" — suggests the proud person's affect is characterised by boldness and self-assurance rather than vulnerability, but this is indicative rather than directly analytical of the affective faculty.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (S)

The verse evidence is largely silent on how CHAR-2 specifically affects or is affected by the affective faculty. The zid "boiling" metaphor implies an affective dimension of heated intensity, but no verse in §3.A explicitly describes the emotional experience of the person exercising CHAR-2. The evidence focuses on the will's volitional act and its consequences rather than the felt affective experience.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

CHAR-3's VCG-03 form deepens and channels affect positively: joy, overflow, rejoicing are all evidenced as the affective expressions of God-directed boasting (Rom 5:2–3; 2Cor 7:4). CHAR-3's VCG-01 form engages affect through the self-satisfaction of self-glorification — the boaster derives pleasure from the public recognition their boast seeks. CHAR-3 is one of the more directly affective characteristics in M08: its speech-act dimension includes an affective component (the felt exultation that is expressed).

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4 bypasses appropriate affect by substituting the inflated self-picture for the accurate assessment that would generate appropriate emotional response. 1Cor 5:2 (vc=33940, M08-D-VCG-01): the puffed-up community cannot mourn because their inflated self-assessment has displaced the perception of their actual moral failure — they feel superior when they should feel grief. CHAR-4 does not generate its own positive affect so much as disable the negative affect (grief, shame, appropriate concern) that accurate assessment would produce.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5 enables and sustains the affective experience of ease, security, and self-sufficient pleasure (Isa 47:8: a.din — love of pleasures; Eze 16:49: prosperous ease). These positive affective states reinforce the inner conviction of self-sufficiency and invulnerability — the person who feels secure and pleasured is more likely to make the cognitive self-declaration of CHAR-5. CHAR-5 does not generate unpleasant affect within the person exercising it (unlike CHAR-2's agitated zeal or CHAR-1's potential tension with God); it generates the affective experience of secure ease.

---

##### T3.4.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with affect reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (S)

The verse evidence is largely silent on the proud person's own affective inner experience of CHAR-1. The affective evidence in §3 is concentrated on those who receive CHAR-1's contempt (Psa 123:4, vc=33953; Psa 13:2, vc=34241; Jer 13:17, vc=34091) rather than on the proud person's felt experience of their own pride. This silence about the proud person's inner affective life is consistent with CHAR-1's self-concealing quality noted in T1.5.3: the characteristic appears to generate no internal discomfort or distress in its possessor. The corpus views CHAR-1 from the outside — through its consequences, victims, and divine assessment — rather than from within the proud person's phenomenological experience.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (S)

The silence about the affective inner experience of the person exercising CHAR-2 may reflect the same pattern noted in CHAR-1: the evidence views CHAR-2 primarily from outside (the act, the characterisation, the consequence) rather than from within the phenomenology of the person exercising it.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

The pattern reveals that the affective faculty's exultation/joy is the created ground from which CHAR-3 distorts: the legitimate joy of God-directed glorying (VCG-03) is the same affective capacity that VCG-01 misdirects toward the self. This makes CHAR-3's affective dimension a site of genuine renewal (VCG-03 joy in God) rather than merely a site of failure, distinguishing CHAR-3 from CHAR-1 and CHAR-2 whose evidence is primarily negative.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The pattern reveals that CHAR-4's cognitive distortion has direct affective consequences: the false self-picture generates an affective equanimity (the puffed-up person does not mourn, does not feel the weight of what they should) that is itself a form of moral failure. 1Cor 5:2 (vc=33940): "ought you not rather to mourn?" — the question implies that the correct inner state is grief; CHAR-4 substitutes inflated confidence for appropriate grief.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

The pattern reveals that CHAR-5 is the pride-characteristic most closely associated with positive affective experience (ease, pleasure, security). This is what makes it particularly resistant to internal correction: the person experiencing CHAR-5 feels good — secure, satisfied, powerful — and the positive affective experience reinforces the cognitive self-sufficiency claim and the dispositional heart-pride. The reversal (Lev 26:19: God breaking the proud might) must overcome not just cognitive and dispositional resistance but also the deeply embedded positive affect of structural security.

---

#### T3.5 — Creativity

##### T3.5.1 — Does this characteristic engage the creative faculty — imagination and the capacity to originate — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (S)

The verse evidence is silent on CHAR-1 engaging the creative faculty (imagination, origination, generativity). No verse in §3 links CHAR-1 to the capacity for imagination, creative origination, or novel generation. The vocabulary across M08-A1 through M08-A4 concerns elevation (upward movement of the self above proper station), contempt (relational posture toward others), forgetfulness (memory displacement), and volition (self-assertion) — none of these engage the creative/imaginative register directly.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (S)

The verse evidence is silent on CHAR-2 engaging the creative faculty (imagination, origination). The characteristic operates in the volitional-relational register, not the creative-imaginative one.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (S)

The verse evidence is silent on CHAR-3 engaging the creative faculty directly. CHAR-3 operates in the communicative/social domain rather than the creative-imaginative one.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (S)

The verse evidence is silent on CHAR-4 engaging the creative/imaginative faculty. CHAR-4 operates in the cognitive self-assessment register rather than the creative-imaginative one.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (S)

The verse evidence in §3.D is silent on CHAR-5 engaging the creative/imaginative faculty. CHAR-5 operates in the structural-power and dispositional registers rather than the creative-imaginative one.

---

##### T3.5.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair creativity in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (S)

Silent. No evidence in the 149-verse corpus addresses CHAR-1's relationship to the creative/imaginative faculty in either direction — neither enabling, deepening, bypassing, nor impairing it.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (S)

Silent. No evidence on CHAR-2's relationship to the creative faculty in §3.A.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (S)

Silent. No evidence on CHAR-3's relationship to the creative faculty in §3.B.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (S)

Silent. No evidence on CHAR-4's relationship to the creative faculty.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (S)

Silent. No evidence on CHAR-5's relationship to the creative faculty in §3.D.

---

##### T3.5.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with creativity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (S)

The silence on creativity suggests CHAR-1 does not operate primarily through the imaginative/creative register. Its primary faculties are dispositional/volitional (T1.8), cognitive-perceptual (T3.1–3.2), and relational (T3.11). This pattern of non-engagement may be significant for cross-characteristic comparison: characteristics that do engage creativity as part of their inner-being expression would stand in contrast to CHAR-1's perceptual-volitional profile.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (S)

CHAR-2's silence on creativity confirms its primary register as volitional and relational-authority-transgressing rather than creative-imaginative.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (S)

CHAR-3's silence on creativity confirms its primary communicative/expressive register — it operates through speech and social display, not through imaginative origination.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (S)

CHAR-4's silence on creativity confirms its exclusively cognitive-self-assessment register. It does not engage imagination or creative origination but the mind's self-referential evaluation function.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (S)

CHAR-5's silence on creativity confirms its structural-power and dispositional register — it operates through received structural goods (power, wealth, position) rather than through imaginative origination.

---

#### T3.6 — Volition

##### T3.6.1 — Does this characteristic engage the volitional faculty — the capacity to choose — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Yes, directly and extensively. The volitional faculty is one of CHAR-1's primary registers. Isa 14:13 (vc=34233, M08-A4-VCG-05): "the will declares in the heart an intent to self-exalt to heaven and above God's stars; this inner volitional self-elevation is the essence of the pride portrayed" — the will's declaration is named as the core of CHAR-1 at its most extreme. Dan 11:36 (vc=34235, M08-A1-VCG-02): the king "exalts himself and magnifies himself above every god by his own will" — CHAR-1 as a total exercise of unconstrained will. Num 15:30 (vc=65731, M08-A4-VCG-05): acting "with a high hand" describes "an inner posture of defiant self-exaltation against God, where the will deliberately overrides divine command." 1Ki 11:26 (vc=34237, M08-A1-VCG-02): Jeroboam "lifted up his hand against the king — the inner will asserts itself in rebellion against royal authority." The will is CHAR-1's primary instrument.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Yes, as its primary constitutional faculty. The zid root (boiling presumption) names the will's self-authorising energy directly. Deu 18:20 (vc=34119, M08-B-VCG-01): the prophet "presumes to speak a word... that I have not commanded" — the will claiming unauthorised speech-right. Exo 21:14 (vc=34122, M08-B-VCG-01): "willful, premeditated... a 'boiling' presumption in the will that plans cunning murder." Authadēs (Tit 1:7, vc=42740, M08-B-VCG-03): "self-willed — asserting one's own preferences without regard for legitimate authority." CHAR-2 is the will's characteristic expression in its self-authorising, authority-transgressing mode.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Yes. Gal 6:14 (vc=33869, M08-C-VCG-02): "may I never boast except in the cross" — a volitional renunciation of all worldly boasting-grounds expressed as a volitional commitment. 2Cor 12:9 (vc=33870, M08-C-VCG-02): "I will boast all the more gladly of my weaknesses" — the volitional choice to boast in weakness rather than strength. 2Cor 10:13 (vc=33888, M08-C-VCG-02): Paul "constrains his boasting to the sphere God assigned" — a volitional self-limiting act. The Pauline examined boasting discourse (VCG-02) is essentially a study in the volitional discipline of the boasting-impulse.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Yes, as a secondary dimension. 1Ti 3:6 (vc=33924, M08-D-VCG-02): the new leader who "becomes puffed up with conceit" — the leadership role taken up (a volitional act) in conjunction with insufficient formation generates the conceit. 1Cor 4:18 (vc=33938, M08-D-VCG-01): some have "decided" (behavioural implication) to be puffed up based on their inflated assessment of their freedom — the conceit leads to volitional postures (assuming Paul will not return, therefore acting presumptuously). CHAR-4 engages volition primarily through the actions that the inflated self-picture generates rather than as its primary constitutional seat.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Yes. Eze 16:30 (vc=57959, M08-E-VCG-02): shal.le.tet (imperious self-will) — "impetuousness is located in the heart" and "expressed as brazen, unrestrained harlotry" — the imperious self-will from a position of structural power is CHAR-5's volitional expression. Hab 2:9 (vc=34169, M08-E-VCG-02): "shame on him who builds his house by unjust gain, setting his nest on high" — the wilful strategy of accumulating position through unjust means. Isa 47:8 (vc=9563, M08-E-VCG-02): the declaration "I am, and there is no one besides me" is an act of the will claiming ontological independence.

---

##### T3.6.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair volition in the person — including its three aspects: capacity, interaction with other characteristics, and the constraints under which it operates?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

CHAR-1 does not impair will-capacity but misdirects it — amplifying the will's self-directed agency while systematically bypassing the constraints (divine authority, creaturely limits) under which the will properly operates. Dan 11:36 (vc=34235, M08-A1-VCG-02): "the king shall do as he wills" — CHAR-1 produces a will that acts without external constraint, a maximised volitional capacity unchecked by reverence or submission. Num 15:30 (vc=65731, M08-A4-VCG-05): acting "with a high hand... equivalent to reviling the Lord directly" — the will overrides divine command, removing the normative constraint under which it should operate. The interaction with other characteristics: CHAR-1's volitional amplification feeds into CHAR-2 (presumptuous defiance) and CHAR-3 (boasting) — the will energised by self-elevation generates both the defiant act and the verbal self-proclamation.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 amplifies and misdirects volition: it intensifies the will's self-directing capacity (the boiling energy of zid) while bypassing the constraints (divine authority, appointed human authority) under which the will properly operates. Deu 1:43 (vc=34123, M08-B-VCG-01): "you acted presumptuously and went up" — the will executes its own agenda despite divine prohibition. The will's capacity is not impaired; its constraints are removed. This produces a will of maximum self-assertive energy in minimum legitimate constraint.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

CHAR-3's VCG-01 form is relatively unexamined volitionally — the self-directed boasting acts without the volitional self-discipline that VCG-02 names. VCG-02's examined discourse shows CHAR-3's impulse subjected to volitional discipline: Paul voluntarily restrains, redirects, and bounds his boasting (2Cor 10:13; Gal 6:14; 2Cor 12:9). VCG-03's God-directed boasting is a fully redirected volitional expression of the glorying-impulse. The volitional engagement is primarily in the disciplines applied to CHAR-3 rather than in the characteristic itself.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4 misdirects volition through the inflated self-assessment that generates false confidence about one's own rights and freedoms. 1Cor 4:18 (vc=33938, M08-D-VCG-01): the puffed-up persons act on the presumption that Paul will not challenge them — their inflated cognitive picture generates a volitional posture of unchallenged freedom. 1Ti 6:4 (vc=33925, M08-D-VCG-02): "unhealthy craving for controversy" — the conceited person's will is directed toward intellectual combat as a form of self-validation. Volition is not impaired in capacity but misdirected through the inflated self-picture.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5 amplifies volition in the direction of self-securing and self-assertive action: Eze 16:30 (vc=57959): shal.le.tet as "brazen, unrestrained" self-will — the structural power position enables the will to operate without the relational constraints that vulnerability would impose. Hab 2:9 (vc=34169): wilful accumulation of unjust gain to secure elevated position. CHAR-5 does not impair will-capacity but misdirects it toward the self-securing and self-exalting ends that structural power makes possible.

---

##### T3.6.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with volition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The pattern reveals that CHAR-1 is constitutively volitional at its core: it is not merely a mood or a cognitive error but a settled orientation of the will toward its own sovereignty. Psa 75:6–7 (vc=34301, vc=34230, M08-A4-VCG-05) states the theological frame: "not from the east or from the west... comes lifting up, but it is God who executes judgment, putting down one and lifting up another" — legitimate exaltation is God's volitional prerogative; CHAR-1 is the creature's will usurping that prerogative. Isa 14:13 (vc=34233, M08-A4-VCG-05) at its most extreme names CHAR-1 as a volitional declaration against God's own position. CHAR-1 is, at its constitutional core, the will claiming sovereignty over elevation — refusing to receive standing as gift from God and asserting it as the will's own possession.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 reveals that the volitional faculty's proper operation requires external constraint (divine command, appointed authority) to function rightly; when CHAR-2 removes those constraints, the unconstrained will becomes the instrument of transgression. Psa 19:13 (vc=34095, M08-B-VCG-02): "let not the presumptuous sins have dominion over me" — the presumptuous sins are characterized as internal forces seeking to "gain dominion" over the will, showing that even from within, unconstrained volitional impulses can enslave the will rather than liberate it.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

The pattern reveals that CHAR-3 is uniquely susceptible to volitional discipline and redirection — unlike CHAR-1 (dispositional) and CHAR-2 (transgressive-act), the boasting-impulse can be voluntarily examined, bounded, and redirected (VCG-02 and VCG-03 are the evidenced results). This volitional redirectability is what makes the Pauline examined boasting discourse possible: the same impulse that generates VCG-01 condemned boasting can be volitionally disciplined into VCG-02 and VCG-03.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The pattern reveals that CHAR-4's cognitive distortion generates downstream volitional misdirection: the person who believes themselves above their actual measure will act accordingly — claiming freedoms they do not have (1Cor 4:18), craving controversy that validates their self-assessment (1Ti 6:4). CHAR-4 is volitionally consequential without being volitionally primary.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5's volitional pattern reveals that structural power enables the will to operate without the natural constraints that vulnerability imposes on human agency. The person with structural power (shal.le.tet — Eze 16:30) can act "unrestrained" because the power position removes the relational and physical constraints that would otherwise limit the will. CHAR-5 is therefore the form of pride most directly enabled by external structural conditions — it amplifies the will's reach proportionally to the structural power available.

---

#### T3.7 — Agency

##### T3.7.1 — Does this characteristic engage the agency faculty — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Yes. CHAR-1 is an active, energising characteristic in the agency register. Psa 10:2 (vc=33963, M08-A4-VCG-03): "arrogance is the inner driving force behind the wicked person's hot pursuit of the poor — it is pride operating as agency, propelling oppressive action and entrapment of the vulnerable." Psa 36:11 (vc=33966, M08-A4-VCG-03): arrogance "personified as a foot that tramples and a hand that drives away — an aggressive inner force in the wicked." Psa 140:5 (vc=33954, M08-A4-VCG-02): "the proud person's inner disposition drives outward hostile action — they secretly lay traps and snares, showing that arrogance produces calculating aggression against others." Psa 31:18 (vc=33964, M08-A4-VCG-03): "pride here is the inner attitude that emboldens lying lips to speak insolently against the righteous — it is the motivating disposition behind contemptuous, oppressive speech." CHAR-1 drives specific, forceful, initiated action.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Yes, directly. CHAR-2 is constitutively agential — it is the will's assertion expressed through action. Deu 1:43 (vc=34123, M08-B-VCG-01): "you went up into the hill country" — a specific initiated action. Exo 21:14 (vc=34122): planning and executing murder — premeditated agency. Mar 10:42 (vc=55588, M08-B-VCG-03): rulers "lord it over" and "exercise authority over" others — the domineering agency of CHAR-2 in the social-power register. Mat 24:49 (vc=55613, M08-B-VCG-03): the wicked servant "beats fellow servants" — CHAR-2 as aggressive, self-authorised action against social others.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Yes. Boasting is inherently an agential act — the boaster initiates a public speech-act in the social field. 2Cor 10:13 (vc=33888, M08-C-VCG-02): Paul "constrains his boasting to the sphere God assigned" — boasting as an act with geographic/relational scope, requiring deliberate initiation. 2Cor 11:30 (vc=33873, M08-C-VCG-02): "I will boast of the things that show my weakness" — Paul initiates a specific boasting-act. The VCG-01 condemned form is agential too: Pro 27:1 (vc=33359): "do not boast about tomorrow" — the prohibition addresses an initiated speech-act.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Yes, through the actions the inflated self-picture generates. 1Cor 4:18 (vc=33938, M08-D-VCG-01): "some are arrogant, as though I were not coming to you" — the arrogant persons have taken actions (or adopted postures) on the basis of their presumed freedom from accountability. 1Ti 6:4 (vc=33925, M08-D-VCG-02): the conceited person engages in controversy and quarrels about words — an active, energised agency directed toward intellectual combat. 1Cor 5:2 (vc=33940, M08-D-VCG-01): the puffed-up community's failure to act on moral failure (failing to mourn and address it) is itself an agential failure enabled by CHAR-4.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Yes. Hab 2:9 (vc=34169, M08-E-VCG-02): "shame on him who builds his house by unjust gain, setting his nest on high to keep himself safe" — CHAR-5 generates a specific strategic agency: the deliberate accumulation of position through unjust means for self-securing purposes. Eze 16:30 (vc=57959, M08-E-VCG-02): "brazen, unrestrained harlotry" — specific acts of self-will from a position of structural power. The national proud-might corpus (Eze 30:6–32:12) implies collective national agency directed by CHAR-5: the Egyptian army exercising force from a posture of proud national confidence.

---

##### T3.7.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair agency in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

CHAR-1 enables and amplifies agency directed toward the self's own goals while bypassing the proper relational limits on agency. The proud person acts with heightened force and initiative: Psa 10:2 (vc=33963, M08-A4-VCG-03) — "hotly pursues the poor" — the energy of the agency is marked; Psa 56:2 (vc=34163, M08-A4-VCG-03) — enemies trample "all day long" — sustained, committed action. The bypass of limits is evidenced in Dan 11:36 (vc=34235, M08-A1-VCG-02) — "shall do as he wills" — where CHAR-1 removes all external constraints on agency. Agency is not impaired in capacity; it is misdirected in orientation, amplified in force, and freed from proper constraints. This is what makes CHAR-1 socially and relationally dangerous: not a passive inward self-regard but a forceful outward-driving energy.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 enables and amplifies agency directed by the self-authorising will, bypassing the proper constraints on agency. Mar 10:42 (vc=55588, M08-B-VCG-03): "lord it over" — an energised, forceful exercise of authority without legitimate basis. Exo 21:14 (vc=34122): "willful, premeditated" — the agency is intentional and forceful. CHAR-2 does not impair agency; it maximises it in the wrong direction.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

CHAR-3 enables and expresses agency through the speech-act of boasting. For VCG-01: agency is exercised in making the self-glorifying claim (Pro 25:14 — boasting of a gift; Pro 20:14 — boasting of a bargain). For VCG-02: agency is exercised in the discipline of constrained, bounded self-commendation (2Cor 10:13 — staying within God-assigned sphere). For VCG-03: agency is exercised in the positive God-directed boasting act (Rom 5:2; 1Cor 1:31). CHAR-3 does not impair agency; it channels it into a specific social-communicative direction.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4 misdirects agency through the inflated self-picture: the person acts as if they have resources, freedoms, or standing they do not actually possess. 1Cor 4:19 (vc=33939, M08-D-VCG-01): Paul will expose not the "talk" but the "power" of the arrogant — implying that their agency is generating talk but not actual spiritual power. CHAR-4 generates agency that is disproportionate to the person's actual capacity, producing actions that will be exposed as ungrounded.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5 enables and amplifies agency by providing the structural power-base from which the self-asserting will operates. The person with proud-might (ga.on — Eze 30:6, vc=33996) has actual military capacity available for their agency; the person with fortified height (Jer 49:16, vc=34167) has physical position from which to exercise agency. CHAR-5 does not generate agency from nothing but channels and amplifies the agency that real structural power provides — making it more forceful and more unconstrained.

---

##### T3.7.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with agency reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The pattern reveals that CHAR-1 is an energising characteristic — it generates active inner drive that moves outward as aggression, domination, oppression, and rebellion. Job 41:34 (vc=12089, M08-A4-VCG-04): Leviathan is "king over all the sons of pride" — pride as the defining quality of those with fierce, dominating self-assertion. Psa 36:11 (vc=33966, M08-A4-VCG-03): arrogance personified as foot and hand — agency metaphors for the active force of pride. This energising quality distinguishes CHAR-1 from a passive conceit or self-regarding mood: it generates initiative, force, and organised action in service of the self's elevation above others. The agency finding also illuminates why CHAR-1 and CHAR-2 (presumptuous defiance) are constitutively related: CHAR-1's volitional-agency energy is what generates CHAR-2's specific defiant acts against authority.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 reveals that unconstrained agency is dangerous rather than liberating: the more fully the will's agency is freed from legitimate constraint, the more directly it produces harm — murder (Exo 21:14), oppression of the poor (Psa 119:85, vc=34102), abuse of fellow servants (Mat 24:49, vc=55613), social strife (Pro 13:10, vc=34113). CHAR-2's energised agency is what makes it socially and relationally destructive.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

CHAR-3's agential pattern reveals that the boasting-act itself is a deliberate social initiative — one chooses to boast, chooses the content, chooses the audience. This deliberate quality is what makes the VCG-02 discipline possible (if boasting were involuntary, it could not be examined and constrained) and what makes VCG-01 morally culpable (if it were involuntary, it could not be prohibited).

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4's agency pattern reveals that the characteristic produces actions that consistently exceed actual capacity and standing — the hallmark of an inflated self-picture operating as the basis for action. 1Cor 4:19 (vc=33939): Paul's exposure of the inflated persons will reveal the gap between their agency-claims (talk) and their actual power — this gap is what CHAR-4 generates at the agency level.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5's agency pattern reveals that structural power generates a distinctive form of energised, unconstrained agency: the proud-might nation and the wealth-proud individual both have real structural capacity behind their agency, making CHAR-5 the most practically powerful of the M08 characteristics in terms of agency-impact. The damage CHAR-5 causes (to the poor — Eze 16:49; through unjust gain — Hab 2:9) is enabled by the actual structural power that the characteristic claims as its ground.

---

#### T3.8 — Moral Evaluation

##### T3.8.1 — Does this characteristic engage the moral evaluation faculty — the capacity to assess against a standard of right, wrong, good, and true — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Yes, by bypassing or corrupting it. Pro 16:5 (vc=12083, M08-A1-VCG-03): "Everyone who is arrogant in heart is an abomination to the Lord; be assured, he will not go unpunished" — God's moral assessment of the proud person's heart is "abomination," but this is not the proud person's own self-assessment; the gap between God's assessment and the proud person's self-evaluation is the evidence of CHAR-1's moral-evaluation impairment. Luk 16:15 (vc=60870, M08-A4-VCG-01): "what is exalted among men is an abomination in the sight of God" — what CHAR-1 evaluates as worthy (exaltation, social esteem) God evaluates as abomination; the moral evaluation standards are inverted. Pro 8:13 (vc=33958, vc=33985, M08-A4-VCG-04): "Pride and arrogance and the way of evil and perverted speech I hate" — wisdom names CHAR-1 as categorically incompatible with the fear of the Lord, which is the proper standard for moral evaluation.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Yes, by inverting it. Mal 3:15 (vc=34106, M08-B-VCG-02): "the arrogant are called blessed" — the moral evaluation faculty produces an inverted verdict: CHAR-2 makes the arrogant appear to prosper, causing observers to question the validity of moral standards. Pro 21:24 (vc=34096, vc=34114, M08-B-VCG-02): the scoffer's "deliberate, premeditated force" bypasses moral self-evaluation entirely. Deu 17:12 (vc=34110, M08-B-VCG-02): the presumptuous man disregards the divinely-appointed judge — implying that his own moral evaluation has replaced the divinely-authorised standard.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Yes, by distorting it in VCG-01. Rom 2:17/23 (vc=33882/33883, M08-C-VCG-01): boasting in the Law while breaking it — the moral evaluation of the self as law-keeper is inverted; the boast produces a moral self-portrait that does not match the moral reality. Jam 4:16 (vc=33923, M08-C-VCG-01): "all such boasting is evil" — the divine moral evaluation of VCG-01 boasting is categorical condemnation. For VCG-02: 2Cor 1:12 (vc=33912, M08-C-VCG-02): conscience-grounded boasting — the moral evaluation faculty (conscience) is actively deployed in the examined boasting discourse.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Yes, by corrupting it. 1Ti 6:4 (vc=33925, M08-D-VCG-02): "understanding nothing" — the moral evaluation faculty is comprehensively disabled. 1Cor 5:2 (vc=33940, M08-D-VCG-01): the puffed-up community evaluates a serious moral failure within their midst without the appropriate moral seriousness — CHAR-4 distorts their moral evaluation of the community's actual state. 1Ti 3:6 (vc=33924, M08-D-VCG-02): the conceited leader falls into condemnation without perceiving it — moral evaluation of one's own trajectory is disabled.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Yes, by corrupting it. Eze 16:49 (vc=33979, M08-E-VCG-01): Sodom's CHAR-5 is paired directly with failure to aid the poor and needy — the structural power-pride has corrupted the moral evaluation faculty so thoroughly that the neighbour in need is invisible. 1Ti 6:17 (vc=60878, M08-E-VCG-02): the wealthy warned against hupsēlofroneō — the implication is that wealth-pride distorts the moral evaluation of one's obligations toward others. Hab 2:9 (vc=34169, M08-E-VCG-02): building a house by unjust gain — CHAR-5 has overridden the moral evaluation that would prevent such gain.

---

##### T3.8.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair moral evaluation in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

CHAR-1 impairs moral evaluation by displacing its reference point (God) and replacing it with the self's own evaluation of what is worthy. Psa 10:4 (vc=34074, M08-A2-VCG-02): "all his thoughts are, 'there is no God'" — eliminating the divine reference point removes the moral standard by which one's own position and actions should be assessed. Luk 16:15 (vc=60870, M08-A4-VCG-01): human moral evaluation prizes what God calls abomination — the two standards diverge so completely that CHAR-1 produces an inverted moral assessment framework. Eze 28:17 (vc=34047, M08-A1-VCG-02): wisdom corruption means the faculty that discerns right from wrong is damaged. The moral evaluation faculty is not absent in the proud person — it is active, but evaluating by the wrong standard (the self's elevation as the criterion of worth).

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 bypasses moral evaluation. Jer 43:2 (vc=34105, M08-B-VCG-02): "the insolent men said to Jeremiah, 'You are telling a lie'" — they substitute their own evaluation for the divinely-mediated prophetic word, showing that CHAR-2 treats the self's assessment as the final moral authority. Psa 119:21 (vc=34098, M08-B-VCG-02): the arrogant "wander from your commandments" — the divine moral standard is treated as non-binding; the self's will replaces the commandment as the evaluative criterion.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

VCG-01 impairs moral evaluation by producing a distorted self-assessment that overestimates the self's moral standing (Rom 2:23 — boasting in the law, breaking the law). VCG-02 engages and deepens moral evaluation: 2Cor 1:12 (vc=33912) — the boast grounded in conscience's testimony to "holiness and godly sincerity" requires active moral self-assessment. VCG-03 redirects moral evaluation outward to God as the proper object of glorying. CHAR-3's three registers demonstrate the full spectrum: moral-evaluation-distorting (VCG-01), moral-evaluation-engaging (VCG-02), moral-evaluation-transcending (VCG-03).

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4 severely impairs moral evaluation through the inflated self-picture that overrides accurate moral assessment. The puffed-up person evaluates themselves as competent (1Cor 4:19 — confident in talk), morally superior (1Cor 5:2 — not mourning the moral failure), and spiritually advanced (Col 2:18 — based on claimed spiritual experience) — all false evaluations generated by CHAR-4.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5 bypasses and impairs moral evaluation through the self-sufficiency conviction it generates. Eze 16:49 (vc=33979, M08-E-VCG-01): the person or community with structural power sees themselves as complete and self-sufficient; the moral obligation to aid others arises only when one sees oneself as part of a shared community of need. CHAR-5's self-sufficiency claim ("I am, and there is no one besides me" — Isa 47:8, vc=9563) specifically removes the relational recognition that would ground moral obligation to others.

---

##### T3.8.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with moral evaluation reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The pattern reveals that CHAR-1 produces a systematic divergence between God's assessment and the proud person's self-assessment. Pro 16:5 (vc=12083, M08-A1-VCG-03): heart-pride evaluated as "abomination to the Lord" — from the divine perspective. Luk 16:15 (vc=60870, M08-A4-VCG-01): what human society esteems is "abomination in the sight of God" — the most explicit statement of the divergence. CHAR-1 is morally self-blinding: it produces the very evaluation failures (displacement of God as standard, elevation of the self as criterion) that would be needed to detect CHAR-1 itself. The proud person evaluates their own self-elevation as appropriate or even commendable while God evaluates it as abomination — a divergence that CHAR-1's perceptive closure (T3.1) prevents the person from perceiving.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 produces a self-referential moral evaluation system: the will that transgresses also sets the terms of moral assessment, which is why it evaluates its own transgression as justified. Mal 3:15 (vc=34106): the appearance of prosperity reinforces this inverted evaluation, making CHAR-2's moral framework feel confirmed by external circumstances.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

The pattern reveals that CHAR-3 is uniquely revealing of the moral evaluation faculty: how one boasts (self-directed vs God-directed; examined vs unexamined) is a direct expression of the moral evaluation faculty's condition. The Pauline examined discourse (VCG-02) is essentially an extended exercise in moral evaluation applied to the boasting-impulse, making CHAR-3 the most epistemologically rich of the M08 characteristics in its engagement with moral self-assessment.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The pattern reveals that CHAR-4 is a moral evaluation failure at its core: it is the mind's wrong picture of itself that necessarily includes a wrong moral picture of itself. 1Ti 6:4 (vc=33925): "understanding nothing" — the most comprehensive moral evaluation failure in M08's evidence. The conceited person has a systematically distorted moral evaluation framework because their self-assessment baseline is inflated.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

The pattern reveals that CHAR-5's moral evaluation failure is relational in its structure: the self-sufficiency claim excludes others from the moral horizon, producing the practical contempt for the vulnerable evidenced in Eze 16:49 (Sodom's failure to aid the poor). CHAR-5 is the M08 characteristic whose moral evaluation failure most directly produces social injustice — the proud-might nation and the wealth-proud individual fail to aid others because their CHAR-5 has removed others from their moral consideration.

---

#### T3.9 — Conscience

##### T3.9.1 — Does this characteristic engage the conscience — the acute inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The evidence bears on conscience primarily through its conspicuous absence in the proud person's narrative. 2Ch 26:16 (vc=34044, M08-A1-VCG-01): "when he was strong, he grew proud, to his destruction. For he was unfaithful to the Lord his God" — the progressive pride-growth shows no evidenced conscience-resistance before the catastrophic act of entering the temple. Jer 49:16 (vc=34054, M08-A1-VCG-03): "the horror you inspire has deceived you" — the proud person is deceived by their own state, not convicted by it; conscience would produce conviction, but deception is what CHAR-1 generates instead. Dan 4:37 (vc=34094, M08-A4-VCG-04): pride is "something one walks in — a habitual inner posture" — the habituation language implies that conscience has not been exercising its acute witness-function; the habitual gait of pride does not produce the inner disturbance of conscience.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The evidence suggests CHAR-2 bypasses conscience. The repeated presumption in Neh 9:16 (vc=34120, M08-B-VCG-01) and Neh 9:29 (vc=34126) — "even after warnings, they acted presumptuously again" — evidences a community pattern in which conscience does not generate self-correction even after repeated corrective intervention from God. Psa 119:69 (vc=34100): "the insolent smear me with lies" — the active, calculating deception implies an inner person whose conscience-function has been overridden by the will's self-justifying momentum.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Yes — conscience is uniquely central to CHAR-3's examined form. 2Cor 1:12 (vc=33912, M08-C-VCG-02): "the testimony of our conscience" as the ground of Paul's boasting — conscience's affirmative testimony grounds legitimate self-commendation. This is the most direct engagement with conscience evidenced in M08's §3 corpora: conscience functions as the positive ground for examined boasting. For VCG-01: conscience is bypassed — the self-directed boaster claims what conscience would not confirm (Rom 2:23: breaking the law one boasts in).

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Indirectly. 1Ti 6:4 (vc=33925, M08-D-VCG-02): conceit paired with "understanding nothing" and "unhealthy craving for controversy" — the conscience, which would generate discomfort at the controversy-craving and the epistemic blindness, appears to be inactive. 1Ti 3:6 (vc=33924, M08-D-VCG-02): the person who falls into the devil's condemnation has not registered the inner warning that conscience should provide. CHAR-4's epistemic blindness ("understanding nothing") is the broadest possible description of conscience failure.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (S)

The verse evidence in §3.D is largely silent on direct conscience engagement for CHAR-5. The moral failures that CHAR-5 produces (Eze 16:49; Hab 2:9) imply conscience bypass, but no verse explicitly names conscience-resistance or conscience-bypass in relation to CHAR-5 specifically.

---

##### T3.9.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscience in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

CHAR-1 bypasses and ultimately impairs conscience. The self-sealing pattern (T3.1.3) extends to the conscience: the inner witness that would convict of wrong is silenced alongside the perceptive closure to God (Psa 10:4, vc=34074, M08-A2-VCG-02: "does not seek him") and the cognitive distortion (Eze 28:17, vc=34047). The most direct evidence for conscience bypass is Jer 49:16 (vc=34054, M08-A1-VCG-03): the pride of the heart that "soars in arrogance will be brought down by God, showing exultation in one's own height as a fatal inner error" — but the proud person does not perceive this as error (deception prevents it). If conscience were functioning, the person would perceive the wrongness of their CHAR-1 before external catastrophe arrives; since the wisdom corpus consistently names external catastrophe (Pro 16:18, vc=34073: "pride goes before destruction") as the corrective mechanism, the inference is that conscience is not generating the internal correction that would render external catastrophe unnecessary.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 bypasses and progressively impairs conscience. The deepening scoffer identity (Pro 21:24, vc=34096, M08-B-VCG-02) evidences the conscience-resistant endpoint of sustained CHAR-2: "he acts with arrogant pride [za.don]" habitually and without evidenced internal resistance. The absence of repentance after repeated correction (Neh 9:29: "even after warnings") confirms conscience is not generating the corrective signal that would break the pattern.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

VCG-01 bypasses conscience (the self-directed boaster's claim is not grounded in conscience's testimony). VCG-02 actively engages and deepens conscience (2Cor 1:12: conscience-grounded boasting). VCG-03 transcends conscience toward God-directed glorying grounded in received grace (not one's own moral standing). CHAR-3 is the only M08 characteristic in which conscience functions as a positive ground (VCG-02) rather than merely as what the characteristic bypasses or disables.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4 bypasses and impairs conscience. The inflated self-picture prevents the cognitive assessment that grounds conscience's witness: if the mind's picture of the self is inflated, conscience cannot accurately assess the gap between actual and ideal — the assessment baseline is wrong. 1Cor 5:2 (vc=33940, M08-D-VCG-01): the community should be mourning (a conscience-response) but is instead puffed up — conscience has been displaced by the inflated self-assessment.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (S)

Silent on direct conscience engagement in §3.D. The self-sufficiency conviction (Isa 47:8, vc=9563) and the deception of heart (Obd 3, vc=65674) imply that conscience is bypassed by CHAR-5's structural-power self-assurance, but this is not directly evidenced as a conscience-specific engagement.

---

##### T3.9.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscience reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The pattern reveals that CHAR-1 is conscience-resistant: it does not generate the inner sense of wrongness that would prompt self-correction. This is consistent with the wisdom corpus's consistent naming of external consequences — destruction (Pro 16:18, vc=34073), humiliation (Pro 29:23, vc=33960), divine scattering (Luk 1:51, vc=33930) — as the primary mechanism through which CHAR-1 is addressed. If conscience were generating conviction, the proud person would self-correct before requiring externally imposed reversal. CHAR-1's conscience resistance makes it structurally dependent on external correction — which is the diagnostic pattern for a characteristic that has successfully silenced the internal witness that should have served this function.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 is conscience-resistant in the same way as CHAR-1: the characteristic bypasses the inner witness that would produce self-correction. This is consistent with the external correction mechanism (Deu 17:12: public punishment; Mal 4:1: eschatological fire) being the primary corrective — if conscience were operative, external catastrophe would not be required.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

The pattern reveals that conscience's role in CHAR-3 is diagnostic: VCG-01 boasting lacks conscience-grounding; VCG-02 examined boasting is conscience-grounded; VCG-03 God-directed boasting rests on received grace beyond conscience. Conscience thus functions as the dividing line between condemned and examined boasting — whether the boast is grounded in what conscience can honestly affirm.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4 reveals a distinctive conscience-failure mode: where CHAR-1 and CHAR-2 seem to bypass conscience through the force of the will, CHAR-4 bypasses conscience through epistemic blindness — the mind's false self-picture means the conscience has no accurate data to work with. 1Ti 6:4 (vc=33925): "understanding nothing" — when the cognitive basis for conscience-assessment is comprehensively distorted, conscience cannot function.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (S)

The silence on explicit conscience engagement suggests CHAR-5 bypasses conscience through structural security rather than through the volitional force of CHAR-2 or the cognitive distortion of CHAR-4. The comfortable ease and felt security of CHAR-5 (Isa 47:8: a.din; Eze 16:49: prosperous ease) leave no inner discomfort for conscience to address.

---

#### T3.10 — Conscientiousness

##### T3.10.1 — Does this characteristic engage conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Yes. CHAR-1 engages conscientiousness by distorting its integration: the moral-awareness component is impaired (T3.8–T3.9) while the volitional and action components are preserved and amplified (T3.6–T3.7). The result is a person who acts with considerable force and inner coherence in a morally uncorrected direction. Dan 11:36 (vc=34235, M08-A1-VCG-02): "the king shall do as he wills. He shall exalt himself and magnify himself above every god" — total volitional-action integration, with the will and action cohering toward self-exaltation; but the moral-awareness that would evaluate this as transgression is absent. Eze 28:2 (vc=34040, M08-A1-VCG-02): the prince of Tyre's heart is proud and he "has inwardly claimed divine status" — the inner claim (volitional) and the speech-act (action) are integrated, but the moral assessment of this as "fundamental distortion of inner being" is not shared by the proud person.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Yes, by corrupting it. Exo 21:14 (vc=34122, M08-B-VCG-01): "willful, premeditated" — CHAR-2 involves deliberate planning (high action-integration, high volitional commitment) but directed against a divinely-established limit. The moral-awareness component of conscientiousness is bypassed while the volitional and action components are fully engaged. Deu 18:20 (vc=34119): the false prophet "presumes to speak" — a deliberate, considered act of speech, executed with full volitional and agency integration but without moral constraint.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Yes. 2Cor 10:13 (vc=33888, M08-C-VCG-02): "we do not boast beyond our measure" — conscientiousness in self-commendation means staying within God-assigned spheres. 2Cor 12:6 (vc=33897, M08-C-VCG-02): Paul "voluntarily refrains" from boasting of genuine experiences "so that others judge him by observable works" — high conscientiousness in managing the social impact of self-commendation. Gal 6:4 (vc=33908, M08-C-VCG-02): "let each one test his own work, and then his reason to boast will be in himself alone and not in his neighbour" — the self-testing before boasting is a conscientiousness act.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Yes, by distorting its cognitive baseline. 1Ti 6:4 (vc=33925, M08-D-VCG-02): the conceited person has "an unhealthy craving for controversy" — high volitional-cognitive engagement (conscientious energy) directed toward intellectual combat rather than truth-seeking. The energy is conscientious (deliberate, sustained, committed) but the moral-awareness baseline is corrupted by CHAR-4. Col 2:18 (vc=33941, M08-D-VCG-01): the person with the ungrounded spiritual-experience inflation may be highly conscientious within the framework of their inflated self-assessment.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Yes, in the strategic-agency mode. Hab 2:9 (vc=34169, M08-E-VCG-02): "shame on him who builds his house by unjust gain, setting his nest on high" — the deliberate, strategic accumulation of position through unjust means evidences conscientiousness (organised, goal-directed, sustained effort) deployed in the wrong direction. The strategy of self-securing elevation is intentional and well-organised — a form of corrupted conscientiousness where the volitional and agency components are integrated but the moral-evaluation component is corrupted by CHAR-5.

---

##### T3.10.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscientiousness in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

CHAR-1 distorts conscientiousness by replacing its moral-awareness component with self-will, while preserving and energising its volitional and action components. Num 15:30 (vc=65731, M08-A4-VCG-05): acting "with a high hand" — a deliberate, integrated inner posture-to-action sequence — but directed against God's explicit command. 2Ch 26:16 (vc=34044, M08-A1-VCG-01): Uzziah "grew proud" and then "entered the temple to burn incense on the altar of incense" — a coherent volitional-action sequence, but one that bypasses the moral constraint that forbade it. The integration of will and action is intact; it is the moral filter that CHAR-1 has removed. The result is what might be called corrupted conscientiousness: high agency and volitional coherence in service of morally wrong ends.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 distorts conscientiousness by preserving and energising the volitional and action components while bypassing the moral-awareness component. Mar 10:42 (vc=55588, M08-B-VCG-03): the rulers who "lord it over" act with deliberate, integrated authority — high conscientiousness in service of domineering rather than legitimate authority. The result is organised, forceful, premeditated action in the wrong direction.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

VCG-01 bypasses conscientiousness (boasting without self-testing: Pro 27:1 — boasting about tomorrow without examining the uncertainty). VCG-02 deepens conscientiousness: the Pauline examined discourse is essentially the application of conscientious self-examination to the boasting-impulse (Gal 6:4; 2Cor 10:13; 2Cor 12:6). The VCG-02 examined discourse is uniquely formative — it shows how conscientiousness disciplines an inner-being characteristic rather than merely condemning it.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4 distorts conscientiousness by corrupting the cognitive baseline from which moral-awareness operates. The conscientious person directs effort and attention rightly; CHAR-4 produces effort directed by a false self-picture. 1Ti 6:4 (vc=33925): "craving for controversy and quarrels about words" — the controversy-craving is energised (conscientious energy present) but the moral-awareness that would direct it toward truth is absent.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5 distorts conscientiousness by channelling it toward self-securing and self-exalting ends. Hab 2:9 (vc=34169): the house-builder's strategy is deliberate and sustained (building, setting the nest on high) — high conscientiousness in the wrong direction. Eze 16:30 (vc=57959, M08-E-VCG-02): shal.le.tet — the imperious self-will acts with unrestrained determination from a position of structural power. Conscientiousness is energised by CHAR-5's structural power-base and misdirected toward self-securing ends.

---

##### T3.10.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscientiousness reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The pattern reveals that CHAR-1 produces organised, self-coherent movement in the wrong direction — which is morally more dangerous than incoherent moral failure. The proud person acts deliberately (Dan 11:36, vc=34235: "by his own will"), with planning (Psa 140:5, vc=33954: "secretly lay traps and snares"), and with sustained commitment (Psa 56:2, vc=34163: "all day long"). CHAR-1 does not produce chaos or paralysis; it produces organised initiative in service of the self's elevation above God and others. This is what makes it the root from which CHAR-2 (presumptuous defiance — organised wilful transgression of divine limits) and CHAR-3 (boasting — organised public self-proclamation) grow as outworkings of the same corrupted conscientiousness.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Like CHAR-1, CHAR-2 produces corrupted conscientiousness — organised, coherent, premeditated action (Exo 21:14: planning; Pro 21:24: acting with deliberate arrogant pride) directed against proper limits. This makes CHAR-2 more dangerous than impulsive moral failure: it combines the force of deliberation with the orientation of transgression.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

CHAR-3's conscientiousness pattern reveals that the examined boasting of VCG-02 is the characteristic deployed with full conscientiousness — moral awareness (conscience-grounded), volitional discipline (constraining within God-assigned spheres), and socially responsible action (managing the impact on others). VCG-02 represents the conscientious form of the same impulse that VCG-01 deploys without conscientiousness.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The pattern reveals that CHAR-4 produces a distinctively cognitive form of corrupted conscientiousness: the energy and commitment of the conceited person are present, but their cognitive baseline (what they are being conscientious about) is systematically distorted by the inflated self-picture. Unlike CHAR-2's conscience bypass through volitional force, CHAR-4's is through cognitive miscalibration.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5's conscientiousness pattern reveals that structural power generates the conditions for organised, sustained, energised self-securing action — making CHAR-5's form of corrupted conscientiousness particularly consequential in its social impact. The structural power enables the wilful, sustained agency (Hab 2:9: building by unjust gain; the ga.on military campaigns) to pursue its ends with real capacity behind it.

---

#### T3.11 — Relational Capacity

##### T3.11.1 — Does this characteristic engage the relational capacity — the constitutional equipment for genuine connection with another person — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Yes, extensively and destructively. CHAR-1 impairs relational capacity in both vertical (human-God) and horizontal (human-human) directions. Vertical: Psa 10:4 (vc=34074, M08-A2-VCG-02): "does not seek him; all his thoughts are, 'there is no God'" — the relational capacity for God is foreclosed entirely; Hos 7:10 (vc=34001, M08-A3-VCG-03): "pride of Israel testifies to his face; yet they do not return to the Lord their God" — the relational movement of return to God is blocked; Psa 138:6 (vc=12086, vc=34300, M08-A4-VCG-02): "the haughty he knows from afar" — God maintains relational distance from the proud. Horizontal: Deu 17:20 (vc=34231, M08-A1-VCG-01): king's heart lifted "above his brothers" — the relational posture is hierarchical domination rather than fraternal connection; Psa 123:4 (vc=33953, M08-A4-VCG-03): "the contempt of the proud" as what crushes the psalmist — contempt substituted for connection; Psa 36:11 (vc=33966, M08-A4-VCG-03): arrogance as foot trampling and hand driving away — predatory agency rather than relational reciprocity.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Yes, destructively. CHAR-2 operates across two relational directions. Vertical (against God/divine authority): Deu 1:43 (vc=34123, M08-B-VCG-01) — defying God's prohibition; Deu 18:20 (vc=34119) — speaking against God's commanded word; Psa 86:14 (vc=34097, M08-B-VCG-02) — "they do not set God before them." Horizontal (against appointed human authority and social others): Deu 17:12 (vc=34110) — defying the appointed judge; Psa 119:85 (vc=34102) — "the insolent have dug pitfalls for me"; Mat 24:49 (vc=55613, M08-B-VCG-03) — the wicked servant beating fellow servants; Mar 10:42 (vc=55588) — lording over others.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Yes — CHAR-3 is inherently relational since it is a social-communicative act. VCG-01's relational impact: 1Cor 5:6 (vc=33903, M08-C-VCG-01): community boasting spreads corruption through the relational whole (leaven through the lump); Pro 25:14 (vc=33358): the empty boaster fails the relational expectation (clouds and wind without rain). VCG-03's relational richness: 2Cor 7:4 (vc=33917); 1Th 2:19 (vc=33913); 2Th 1:4 (vc=33881, M08-C-VCG-03) — mutual boasting between Paul and his communities as a relational practice of affirmation and solidarity.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Yes, destructively. 1Cor 8:1 (vc=33935, M08-D-VCG-01): "knowledge puffs up, but love builds up" — CHAR-4 directly displaces love (the relational capacity's proper exercise) with self-inflation. 1Cor 13:4 (vc=33936, M08-D-VCG-01): "love is not arrogant [fusioō]" — CHAR-4 and love are mutually exclusive. 2Cor 12:20 (vc=33942, M08-D-VCG-02): fusiōsis among a cluster of relational sins (quarreling, jealousy, anger, hostility, slander, gossip, conceit, disorder) — CHAR-4 embedded in and generating relational disruption.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Yes, destructively. Eze 16:49 (vc=33979, M08-E-VCG-01): CHAR-5 paired directly with failure to "aid the poor and needy" — the relational obligation to the vulnerable is specifically what CHAR-5 prevents. Isa 47:8 (vc=9563, M08-E-VCG-02): "I shall not sit as a widow or know the loss of children" — the relational posture is one of invulnerability to relational loss; CHAR-5 removes the person from the shared condition of relational vulnerability that grounds genuine connection. Hab 2:9 (vc=34169, M08-E-VCG-02): unjust gain from others — exploiting relational others as the means of building position.

---

##### T3.11.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair relational capacity in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

CHAR-1 severely impairs relational capacity in both directions. Vertically: the God-directed relational capacity is impaired through forgetfulness (Deu 8:14, vc=34223: heart lifted → God forgotten), perceptive closure (Psa 10:4, vc=34074: "does not seek him"), and the consequent divine relational distance (Psa 138:6, vc=12086: "the haughty he knows from afar"). Horizontally: CHAR-1 substitutes hierarchy and contempt for genuine connection. Genuine horizontal relationship requires acknowledgment of the other's worth and standing — CHAR-1 denies this by elevating the self above all others (Deu 17:20, vc=34231). The result is that CHAR-1 generates predatory interaction (Psa 10:2, vc=33963: "hotly pursues the poor"), contemptuous interaction (Psa 123:4, vc=33953), and violent interaction (Psa 73:6, vc=33959: "pride is their necklace; violence covers them as a garment") rather than genuine relational connection.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 severely impairs relational capacity. It substitutes domination and predation for genuine connection in the horizontal direction: Psa 119:85 (vc=34102) — pitfalls dug for the godly; Psa 119:69 (vc=34100) — lies smearing the psalmist.
