In the vertical direction, it breaks the human-to-God relational connection by treating God's authority as a constraint to overcome rather than a relationship to honour. Pro 13:10 (vc=34113, M08-B-VCG-02): "by insolence comes nothing but strife" — CHAR-2's relational consequence is universal: it produces conflict in every relational direction.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

VCG-01 impairs relational capacity through empty social claims (Pro 25:14 — promising what one cannot deliver) and community corruption (1Cor 5:6). VCG-03 deepens relational capacity: mutual boasting between Paul and his communities (2Cor 7:4; 1Th 2:19; 2Th 1:4) is a relational practice of genuine commendation and joy in the other. CHAR-3 is the most relationally complex of the M08 characteristics: its condemned form (VCG-01) corrupts relational capacity, its examined form (VCG-02) manages it conscientiously, and its God-directed form (VCG-03) deepens it through mutual affirmation.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4 severely impairs relational capacity. 1Cor 8:1 (vc=33935): knowledge (without love) inflates — the inflated self-picture prevents the other-directed attention that genuine relationship requires. 1Cor 13:4 (vc=33936): love is not fusioō — the inflation is the direct antithesis of love's self-giving orientation. The conceited mind is too preoccupied with its own inflated self-picture to genuinely perceive, value, and respond to the other.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5 severely impairs relational capacity by generating the self-sufficiency conviction that removes the person from the shared community of need. Isa 47:8 (vc=9563): "I am, and there is no one besides me" — the relational isolation of the self-sufficient declaration; the person who believes they need no one cannot genuinely connect with others. Eze 16:49 (vc=33979, M08-E-VCG-01): the proud, ease-dwelling community does not see the neighbour in need — CHAR-5's structural self-sufficiency renders the other invisible as a subject of genuine relational concern.

---

##### T3.11.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with relational capacity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The pattern reveals that CHAR-1 is fundamentally anti-relational in its structure: it is the characteristic that generates structural relational isolation in both directions simultaneously. Upward: the proud person cannot genuinely receive God because CHAR-1 closes the perceptive and memorial faculties through which God's relational approach would be received (T3.1, T3.3). Downward: the proud person cannot genuinely connect with peers because CHAR-1 positions them above all others as objects of contempt rather than subjects of genuine encounter. Psa 138:6 (vc=12086, vc=34300, M08-A4-VCG-02) states the vertical relational consequence most directly: "though the LORD is high, he regards the lowly, but the haughty he knows from afar" — God himself cannot be genuinely known by the proud person except at the distance that CHAR-1 produces. The characteristic generates isolation from God and domination of others — both substituting for the relational connection that CHAR-1 constitutively forecloses.

---

## T4 — Relational Interfaces (24 prompts)

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 is constitutively anti-relational in the authority-bearing direction: any relationship that involves legitimate constraint on the will is the specific relational target that CHAR-2 transgresses. God's authority, the appointed judge's authority, the prophet's authority, the elder's authority (Isa 3:5, vc=34212, M08-B-VCG-02: "youth being insolent to the elder"), the master's authority (Mat 24:49) — all are relational bonds whose constraint CHAR-2 systematically transgresses. The pattern reveals that CHAR-2 cannot coexist with legitimate authority-bearing relationships.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

The relational pattern reveals that CHAR-3's three VCG registers correspond to three relational postures: self-serving (VCG-01: the boast claims social recognition for the self at the expense of relational honesty), self-disclosing/bounded (VCG-02: the examined boast manages the social relationship with apostolic integrity), and other-affirming/God-directed (VCG-03: the boast celebrates the community's faith and God's grace, deepening relational bonds). CHAR-3's relational complexity is unique within M08.

CHAR-4's relational pattern reveals that cognitive self-inflation and genuine relational capacity are structurally incompatible: 1Cor 8:1 (vc=33935) states this as a structural law — knowledge puffs up (CHAR-4) while love builds up (relational capacity's expression). The two impulses are placed in direct contrast, confirming that CHAR-4 and love occupy the same cognitive space and compete for the same inner direction.

CHAR-5 is the M08 characteristic whose relational failure is most directly evidenced in social injustice: Eze 16:49 (vc=33979) names the failure to aid the poor as the direct consequence of Sodom's power-pride. The structural self-sufficiency of CHAR-5 generates not merely interpersonal contempt (as CHAR-1 and CHAR-2 do) but structural social indifference — the proud-powerful community is blind to the poor neighbour as a moral claim on them.

## T4 — Relational Interfaces (24 prompts)

---

### T4

#### T4.1 — Divine Interface — God to Human

##### T4.1.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating from God toward the human person — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

CHAR-1 does not operate from God toward the human person — God does not possess or extend arrogant self-elevation. What the evidence consistently shows is God's active response to CHAR-1 in the human person: sustained, structural divine opposition. Jam 4:6 (vc=33931, M08-A4-VCG-01): "God opposes the proud, while granting grace to the humble" — the opposition is named as the direct relational response to CHAR-1. 1Pe 5:5 (vc=33934, M08-A4-VCG-01): "God opposes the proud" — repeated citation of the same principle, confirming it as a structural divine disposition. 2Sa 22:28 (vc=34236, M08-A4-VCG-02): "your eyes are on the haughty to bring them down" — God's watchful attention specifically directed at the proud as a target for reversal. Luk 1:51 (vc=33930, M08-A1-VCG-03): "he has scattered the proud in the thoughts of their hearts" — active divine dispersal of the proud at the level of their inner thoughts. The God-to-human direction in CHAR-1's evidence is not extension of the characteristic but active, sustained opposition to it.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 does not operate from God toward the human person — God does not possess presumptuous defiance. What the evidence shows is God's consistent opposition and judicial response to CHAR-2. Deu 17:12 (vc=34110, M08-B-VCG-02): the presumptuous man "shall die; so you shall purge the evil from Israel" — God's judicial response through the appointed legal system. Neh 9:10 (vc=34125, M08-B-VCG-01): "you performed signs and wonders against Pharaoh and all his servants and all the people of his land, for you knew that they acted arrogantly against our ancestors" — divine counter-action to CHAR-2. Mal 4:1 (vc=34107, M08-B-VCG-02): "the arrogant and all evildoers will be stubble; the day that is coming shall set them ablaze" — God's eschatological judgment of CHAR-2.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

CHAR-3 does not operate from God toward the human person. What the evidence shows is God's sovereign design working specifically to eliminate the grounds for human self-directed boasting. 1Cor 1:29 (vc=33877, M08-C-VCG-01): "so that no human being might boast in the presence of God" — God's election of the weak and foolish is designed to prevent CHAR-3's VCG-01 form. Eph 2:9 (vc=65604, M08-C-VCG-01): "not a result of works, so that no one may boast" — the design of grace-salvation is specifically to foreclose the ground for self-directed boasting. God's direction toward the human person in relation to CHAR-3 is foreclosing, redirecting, and commanding redirection (1Cor 1:31: "let the one who boasts, boast in the Lord").

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4 does not operate from God toward the human person. What the evidence shows is God's provision of the accurate measure against which CHAR-4 transgresses, and his judicial response to CHAR-4. Rom 12:3 (vc=60866, M08-D-VCG-02): "God has assigned" the measure of faith by which each person is to assess themselves — God's gift of the proper cognitive measure is the opposite of CHAR-4. 1Ti 3:6 (vc=33924, M08-D-VCG-02): the conceited person falls into "the condemnation of the devil" — God's judicial response to CHAR-4 is condemnation, not extension of the characteristic.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5 does not operate from God toward the human person. What the evidence shows is God's consistent and active opposition to CHAR-5 — specifically the breaking and bringing-down of proud structural might. Lev 26:19 (vc=33982, M08-E-VCG-01): "I will break the pride of your power" — God's active intervention against CHAR-5. Eze 30:6 (vc=33996, M08-E-VCG-01): "those who support Egypt shall fall... her proud might shall come down" — God's judicial direction against Egypt's CHAR-5. Eze 30:18 (vc=33997): "her proud might shall come to an end" — repeated judicial action. The God-to-human direction in relation to CHAR-5 is consistently breaking, humbling, and desolating the structural power that CHAR-5 claims as its self-sufficient ground.

---

##### T4.1.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the basis on which God extends this characteristic — is it conditional, unconditional, covenantal, or responsive?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

God's opposition to CHAR-1 is unconditional and structural in scope — not limited to specific covenantal violators or responsive to extreme cases only. Pro 16:5 (vc=12083, M08-A1-VCG-03): "Everyone who is arrogant in heart is an abomination to the Lord; be assured, he will not go unpunished" — the universal scope marker "everyone" removes covenantal or situational qualification. Jam 4:6 (vc=33931, M08-A4-VCG-01) and 1Pe 5:5 (vc=33934, M08-A4-VCG-01) both cite Pro 3:34 as a standing principle, presenting God's opposition to the proud as a structural divine disposition, not a situational response. Amo 6:8 (vc=34002, M08-A3-VCG-03): "I abhor the pride of Jacob" — divine abhorrence even of Israel's pride within the covenant. Isa 2:12 (vc=33957, M08-A3-VCG-04): "the Lord of hosts has a day against all that is proud and lofty" — universal eschatological scope. The basis is ontological: CHAR-1 competes with God's sole claim to exaltation, so opposition is structural rather than conditional.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

God's opposition to CHAR-2 is structural and grounded in his ordination of the very authority that CHAR-2 transgresses. Deu 17:12 (vc=34110, M08-B-VCG-02): the appointed judge stands "to minister there before the Lord your God" — God has established the authority; transgressing it is transgressing God's own ordination. Deu 18:20 (vc=34119, M08-B-VCG-01): "the prophet who presumes to speak a word in my name that I have not commanded" — God is the source of the word; presuming to speak it is usurping God's communicative sovereignty. The basis is ontological: CHAR-2 violates what God has established, making divine opposition the structural consequence.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

God's design to eliminate VCG-01 boasting is based on the ontological reality that all goods are received from him: 1Cor 4:7 (vc=33871, M08-C-VCG-01): "what do you have that you did not receive?" — the received quality of all creaturely goods makes self-directed boasting logically false. God's design is not arbitrary but grounded in the actual structure of created reality: since everything comes from God, self-glorification is a false attribution; God's design forecloses the false attribution by making the grace-origin of all goods undeniable (Eph 2:8–9).

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

God's response is grounded in his status as the one who assigns proper cognitive measure and judges when it is exceeded. Rom 12:3 (vc=60866, M08-D-VCG-02): "each according to the measure of faith that God has assigned" — God is the measure-giver; exceeding his assigned measure is the structural basis for his corrective response. 1Ti 3:6 (vc=33924, M08-D-VCG-02): the condemnation is not arbitrary but follows the pattern of the adversarial figure's original transgression — God's judgment of CHAR-4 is consistent with his judgment of the adversary's same pattern.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

God's response is grounded in his status as the sole genuine source of all power and strength — which CHAR-5 usurps. Lev 26:19 (vc=33982, M08-E-VCG-01): God "will break the pride of your power" — the power was God-given; CHAR-5's claim to it as a self-sufficient basis generates the divine judgment. 1Ti 6:17 (vc=60878, M08-E-VCG-02): God is "who richly provides everything" — the divine provision of all material goods makes CHAR-5's wealth-pride a false attribution; God's response is grounded in his role as the actual provider that CHAR-5 ignores.

---

##### T4.1.3 — What does God's extension of this characteristic reveal about his disposition toward the human person?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

God's consistent opposition to CHAR-1 reveals three dimensions of his disposition. First, jealousy for his sole exaltation: Isa 2:11 (vc=34601, M08-A3-VCG-04) and 2:17 (vc=34602, M08-A3-VCG-04) — "the Lord alone will be exalted in that day" — the day of judgment re-establishes the divine monopoly on true exaltation that CHAR-1 has trespassed. Second, care for the lowly as the preferred relational posture: 2Sa 22:28 (vc=34236, M08-A4-VCG-02) — "you save a humble people, but your eyes are on the haughty to bring them down" — divine saving-movement toward the humble paired with opposing-movement toward the proud. Psa 138:6 (vc=12086, vc=34300, M08-A4-VCG-02) — "he regards the lowly, but the haughty he knows from afar" — relational proximity to the lowly contrasted with relational distance from the proud. Third, judicial commitment to accountability: Psa 94:2 (vc=33952, M08-A4-VCG-02) — "repay to the proud what they deserve" — the judicial frame confirming that God's opposition to CHAR-1 is not arbitrary but grounded in the justice of the creaturely-Creator order.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

God's response reveals his disposition as the sovereign ordainer and defender of legitimate authority structures. Deu 17:13 (vc=34124, M08-B-VCG-01): "all the people shall hear and fear and not act presumptuously again" — God's judgment is educative as well as punitive; it is designed to generate the fear that blocks CHAR-2. Jer 50:31 (vc=34116, M08-B-VCG-02): "behold, I am against you, O proud one" — direct divine opposition. Neh 9:10 (vc=34125): God "performed signs and wonders" as counter-response to Egypt's CHAR-2 — the divine protective care for his people against those who presumptuously defy his order.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

God's design to redirect boasting toward himself reveals: (a) his jealousy for his own glory as the legitimate object of all exultation (1Cor 1:31: "boast in the Lord" as the commanded alternative); (b) his care for the community's relational integrity (1Cor 5:6: community boasting spreads corruption — God's concern is for the whole community's health); (c) his sovereign purpose to use human weakness as the arena for his glory (2Cor 12:9, vc=33870, M08-C-VCG-02: "my power is made perfect in weakness" — God designs that CHAR-3 be redirected toward his glory precisely through what humans would not choose to boast about).

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

God's response reveals: (a) His role as the accurate Measurer — he is the one whose assessment is the true standard against which all cognitive self-assessment should be calibrated (Rom 12:3, vc=60866); (b) His commitment to judicial consistency — the condemnation of the devil (1Ti 3:6, vc=33924) applies equally when humans replicate the same cognitive self-inflation. God's disposition is toward accurate self-knowledge within proper creaturely bounds as the created order; CHAR-4 transgresses this order and receives the judicial response that the adversary's original transgression received.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

God's consistent breaking of proud might across nations (Israel — Lev 26:19; Egypt — Eze 30:6/30:18/32:12; Edom — Jer 49:16; Babylon — Jer 51:53) reveals: (a) His sovereignty over all structural power — no national or individual structural power is beyond his ability to break; (b) His particular concern for the vulnerable who are failed by CHAR-5's social indifference — Eze 16:49 (vc=33979, M08-E-VCG-01): the failure to aid the poor is God's indictment of Sodom's proud power; (c) His purpose to redirect all structural goods toward his own glory and the service of others rather than toward human self-exaltation.

---

##### T4.1.4 — If the evidence is silent on God-to-human operation, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The evidence is not silent: God's active opposition to CHAR-1 is extensively evidenced (Jam 4:6, vc=33931; 1Pe 5:5, vc=33934; 2Sa 22:28, vc=34236; Luk 1:51, vc=33930; Psa 138:6, vc=12086; Amo 6:8, vc=34002). This prompt is closed by T4.1.1–3.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Not silent: God's opposition to and judgment of CHAR-2 is extensively evidenced (Deu 17:12; Mal 4:1; Jer 50:31; Neh 9:10). See T4.1.1–3.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Not silent: God's active design to redirect CHAR-3 is extensively evidenced (1Cor 1:29; Eph 2:9; 1Cor 1:31; 2Cor 12:9). See T4.1.1–3.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Not silent: God's provision of the proper measure (Rom 12:3) and judicial response to CHAR-4 (1Ti 3:6) are evidenced. See T4.1.1–3.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Not silent: God's active breaking of proud structural might is the primary God-to-human direction evidenced in §3.D (Lev 26:19; Eze 30:6/30:18/32:12/33:28; Jer 49:16; Jer 51:53). See T4.1.1–3.

---

#### T4.2 — Divine Interface — Human to God

##### T4.2.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in the human person's movement toward God — in seeking, supplication, worship, or covenant — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Yes — as the inner state that blocks every form of human-to-God movement. Psa 10:4 (vc=34074, M08-A2-VCG-02): "the wicked does not seek him; all his thoughts are, 'there is no God'" — CHAR-1 displaces the act of seeking God entirely, substituting self-sufficient cognitive closure for the movement of seeking. Hos 7:10 (vc=34001, M08-A3-VCG-03): "the pride of Israel testifies to his face; yet they do not return to the Lord their God, nor seek him, for all this" — the movement of return (repentance, covenant re-engagement) is specifically blocked by CHAR-1. Isa 26:10 (vc=34024, M08-A4-VCG-05): "the wicked person's inner perceptual faculty is closed to the Lord's majesty even in a land of uprightness" — even environmental conditions that should prompt God-ward movement (righteousness all around) are insufficient to overcome CHAR-1's blockage. Deu 8:14 (vc=34223, M08-A1-VCG-01): the heart lifted up forgets God — forgetfulness replaces the memory of God's redemptive acts that would motivate worship and gratitude.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Yes — as the characteristic that directly opposes the human person's movement toward God. Psa 86:14 (vc=34097, M08-B-VCG-02): "they do not set God before them" — CHAR-2 removes God from the directional horizon of the inner person's movement. Neh 9:16 (vc=34120, M08-B-VCG-01): "they did not obey your commandments" — the obedience that is the vehicle of human-to-God movement is specifically what CHAR-2 refuses. Jer 50:29 (vc=34127, M08-B-VCG-01): "she has defied the Lord, the Holy One of Israel" — CHAR-2 directed explicitly against the divine person, inverting the movement of human-to-God approach into direct opposition.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Yes — in two opposite modes. VCG-01 negative: Rom 2:17 (vc=33882, M08-C-VCG-01): "you who call yourself a Jew and rely on the law and boast in God" — the person using religious identity as the ground of self-boasting; the boast is directed "in God" but is actually a self-promotion using religious credentials, not genuine God-directed movement. VCG-03 positive: Phili 3:3 (vc=33879, M08-C-VCG-03): "worship by the Spirit of God and glory in Christ Jesus and put no confidence in the flesh" — the VCG-03 glorying is genuine movement toward God; Rom 5:11 (vc=33876, M08-C-VCG-03): "we also rejoice in God through our Lord Jesus Christ."

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Yes — as the characteristic that distorts the cognitive self-assessment foundational to accurate movement toward God. Rom 12:3 (vc=60866, M08-D-VCG-02): the commanded alternative (sober judgment within God-assigned measure) is the cognitive posture that enables proper human-to-God orientation — CHAR-4 removes this by inflating the self-picture beyond God's assigned measure. 1Ti 3:6 (vc=33924, M08-D-VCG-02): the movement CHAR-4 generates is toward the condemnation associated with the devil's paradigm — the inverse of movement toward God.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Yes — as the inner posture that replaces movement toward God with structural self-sufficiency. Isa 47:8 (vc=9563, M08-E-VCG-02): "you who say in your heart, 'I am, and there is no one besides me'" — the self-sufficient declaration specifically claims the ontological completeness that would make movement toward God unnecessary. 1Ti 6:17 (vc=60878, M08-E-VCG-02): "set their hopes on the uncertainty of riches" rather than on God — CHAR-5's wealth-pride re-directs hope from God to structural goods, inverting the human-to-God movement.

---

##### T4.2.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the inner posture required for this movement?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The evidence reveals the required posture negatively, through what CHAR-1 removes. Psa 131:1 (vc=34059, M08-A1-VCG-03; vc=34224, M08-A2-VCG-01): "my heart is not lifted up; my eyes are not raised too high; I do not occupy myself with things too great and too marvelous for me" — the deliberate inner lowering of the heart and eyes is the posture that enables the God-ward orientation CHAR-1 precludes. Dan 4:37 (vc=34094, M08-A4-VCG-04): after Nebuchadnezzar's CHAR-1 is humbled, he "praises and extols and honours the King of heaven, for all his works are right and his ways are just" — the posture of God-directed praise emerges as CHAR-1 is removed. The required posture for human-to-God movement is its direct opposite: the heart held at creaturely level, not lifted above it; the eyes not raised in prideful claim; the self positioned as receiver and respondent rather than as self-exalted agent.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Evidenced negatively through CHAR-2's precise inversal. Deu 17:13 (vc=34124, M08-B-VCG-01): "all the people shall hear and fear" — hearing and fearing (reverent submission) is the posture for human-to-God movement that CHAR-2 replaces with defiant self-assertion. Psa 19:13 (vc=34095, M08-B-VCG-02): the psalmist's posture of "keep back your servant from presumptuous sins" — the servant orientation that seeks divine restraint is the human-to-God posture that CHAR-2 inverts. 2Pe 2:10 (vc=42739, M08-B-VCG-03): "they do not tremble" — trembling reverence is the human-toward-divine posture; its absence marks CHAR-2.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Jer 9:23–24 (vc=33342 context, M08-C-VCG-01): the implied positive — "let him who boasts boast in this: that he understands and knows me" — the posture required is knowing God, not knowing about one's own attributes. 1Cor 1:31 (vc=33878, M08-C-VCG-03): "let the one who boasts, boast in the Lord" — the posture is Lord-directed exultation. Gal 6:14 (vc=33869, M08-C-VCG-02): "the world has been crucified to me" — the cross-mediated death to worldly boasting-grounds is the required inner posture for God-directed movement.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Rom 12:3 (vc=60866, M08-D-VCG-02) directly names the required posture: "think of yourself with sober judgment, each according to the measure of faith that God has assigned" — accurate, God-referenced cognitive self-assessment within divinely-assigned measure is the posture required for proper human-to-God orientation. CHAR-4 removes this posture by inflating the self-picture.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

1Ti 6:17 (vc=60878, M08-E-VCG-02) most directly evidences the required alternative posture: "set their hopes... on God, who richly provides everything to enjoy" — the posture required for human-to-God movement is the recognition of God as the source of all structural goods, displacing CHAR-5's self-sufficiency claim. Lev 26:19 (vc=33982, M08-E-VCG-01) implies the same: the proper posture toward God-given power is dependence on God rather than confidence in the power itself.

---

##### T4.2.3 — What does the human-to-God direction of this characteristic reveal about the person's relationship with God?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

CHAR-1 in the human-to-God direction reveals a person who has substituted the self for God as the orientation-point of their inner world. Isa 14:13 (vc=34233, M08-A4-VCG-05): "you said in your heart, 'I will ascend to heaven; above the stars of God I will set my throne on high'" — the will moves toward God's position rather than toward God in relationship. Eze 28:2 (vc=34040, M08-A1-VCG-02): "your heart is proud, and you have said, 'I am a god'" — the claiming of divine status is the inverse of worship: instead of the creature moving toward God in reverence, the creature moves toward God's position as competitor. Deu 8:14 (vc=34223, M08-A1-VCG-01): prosperity lifting the heart produces forgetfulness of God — the God-relationship is severed not by explicit rebellion but by the self's satisfying fullness. CHAR-1 reveals a person whose fundamental orientation has rotated from God-ward to self-ward.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 in the human-to-God direction reveals a person who has converted the relationship to God from a covenant of submission into a site of competition or confrontation. Jer 50:29 (vc=34127, M08-B-VCG-01): Babylon "has defied the Lord, the Holy One of Israel" — the defiance is explicitly directed against God's person. 2Pe 2:10 (vc=42739): self-willed people "despise authority and do not tremble before the glorious ones" — the relationship to divine authority is one of active contempt rather than reverent engagement. CHAR-2 reveals a person whose will has made God's authority the object of its transgressive self-assertion.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

CHAR-3's human-to-God direction reveals that the glorying-capacity is structurally designed for God-directed expression (VCG-03 is the revealed telos of the kauchaomai capacity), but that the same capacity misdirects itself toward the self (VCG-01), toward Law-based religious identity (Rom 2:17), or toward human apostolic credentials (2Cor 11:18, vc=33894, M08-C-VCG-02). The human-to-God direction is the proper orientation for the glorying-capacity; CHAR-3's VCG-01 form is the misdirected version.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4 in the human-to-God direction reveals that cognitive self-inflation is a barrier to proper creaturely relationship with God: the inflated self-picture places the self above its God-assigned measure, which is itself a transgression of the proper creaturely-Creator relationship. 1Ti 3:6 (vc=33924): the new leader's conceit leads to "the condemnation of the devil" — the most extreme adversarial paradigm of the creature overreaching its proper cognitive station before God.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5 in the human-to-God direction reveals that structural power is the specific form of self-sufficiency that most completely substitutes for God. Isa 47:8 (vc=9563, M08-E-VCG-02): "I am, and there is no one besides me" — the structural power of Babylon has generated a self-understanding so complete that it claims divine ontological status ("I am" echoing God's own self-identification). This is CHAR-5 at its theological extreme: structural power enabling the creature to claim God's own I-am-ness.

---

##### T4.2.4 — If the evidence is silent on human-to-God operation, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The human-to-God direction is extensively evidenced as blocked, inverted, and misdirected by CHAR-1 (Psa 10:4, vc=34074; Hos 7:10, vc=34001; Isa 26:10, vc=34024; Deu 8:14, vc=34223; Isa 14:13, vc=34233). Not silent.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Human-to-God direction extensively evidenced as blocked and inverted by CHAR-2 (Psa 86:14; Neh 9:16; Jer 50:29; 2Pe 2:10). Not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Human-to-God direction extensively evidenced in both misdirected (VCG-01: religious credential boasting) and genuine (VCG-03: God-directed glorying) forms. Not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Human-to-God direction evidenced as blocked/distorted by CHAR-4 (Rom 12:3; 1Ti 3:6). Not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Human-to-God direction evidenced as replaced by structural self-sufficiency (Isa 47:8; 1Ti 6:17). Not silent.

---

#### T4.3 — Human Interface — Giving

##### T4.3.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being extended by one person toward another — and if so, how does it operate in that giving?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Yes — as contempt, domination, predatory aggression, and oppressive speech. Psa 10:2 (vc=33963, M08-A4-VCG-03): "in arrogance the wicked hotly pursue the poor" — CHAR-1 extended toward others as predatory pursuit; the inner arrogance is "operating as agency, propelling oppressive action." Psa 36:11 (vc=33966, M08-A4-VCG-03): arrogance as "a foot that tramples and a hand that drives away" — CHAR-1 extended as physical/social force that removes and subjugates. Psa 73:6 (vc=33959, M08-A2-VCG-02): "pride is their necklace; violence covers them as a garment" — CHAR-1 displayed outwardly and paired with violence toward others. Psa 17:10 (vc=34028, M08-A1-VCG-03): "with their mouths they speak arrogantly" — CHAR-1 extended through contemptuous speech. Psa 31:18 (vc=33964, M08-A4-VCG-03): pride emboldens "lying lips to speak insolently against the righteous" — CHAR-1 generating offensive relational acts against the godly.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Yes — as domination, predation, and contemptuous treatment. Mar 10:42 (vc=55588, M08-B-VCG-03): rulers "lord it over" and "exercise authority over" their subjects — CHAR-2 extended as domineering social power. Mat 24:49 (vc=55613, M08-B-VCG-03): the wicked servant "beats fellow servants" — CHAR-2 as direct physical aggression against social peers. Psa 119:85 (vc=34102, M08-B-VCG-02): "the insolent have dug pitfalls for me" — predatory scheming against the godly. Isa 3:5 (vc=34212, M08-B-VCG-02): "the youth being insolent to the elder" — CHAR-2 extended as social insolence against age-authority.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Yes, in two forms. VCG-01 self-directed boasting extended toward others as a social claim: Pro 25:14 (vc=33358, M08-C-VCG-01): boasting of a gift never given — the false social claim extended toward those who should receive the gift; Pro 20:14 (vc=33357): the buyer's duplicitous boast extended toward potential others in the marketplace. VCG-03 community affirmation extended toward others: 2Cor 7:14 (vc=33898, M08-C-VCG-03): Paul's boasting about the Corinthians to Titus — the boast extended as commendation of the community toward a third party; 2Th 1:4 (vc=33881): Paul boasting about the Thessalonians in churches — the boast as relational commendation extended outward.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Yes — as partisan favouritism, contemptuous presumption, and intellectual condescension. 1Cor 4:6 (vc=33937, M08-D-VCG-01): puffed up "in favour of one against another" — the inflation extended toward others through partisan dismissal of one leader in favour of another. 1Cor 4:18 (vc=33938, M08-D-VCG-01): "as though I were not coming" — CHAR-4 directed toward Paul as contemptuous presumption about his absence. 1Cor 8:1 (vc=33935, M08-D-VCG-01) context: knowledge-conceit directed toward weaker believers who lack the knowledge — intellectual condescension toward those with less knowledge.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Yes — as structural contempt, social indifference to the vulnerable, and exploitation. Eze 16:49 (vc=33979, M08-E-VCG-01): the CHAR-5 of Sodom expressed toward the poor and needy as active failure to aid — the structural ease-pride generates social indifference to others' need. Hab 2:9 (vc=34169, M08-E-VCG-02): building by "unjust gain" from others — CHAR-5 expressed toward social others as economic exploitation. Eze 16:30 (vc=57959, M08-E-VCG-02): shal.le.tet — brazen, unrestrained self-will directed outward toward social others from a position of structural power.

---

##### T4.3.2 — What inner conditions or orientations in the giver enable genuine extension of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The extension of CHAR-1 toward others is enabled by: settled elevated self-assessment relative to those toward whom it is directed — Psa 123:4 (vc=33953, M08-A4-VCG-03): "those who are at ease" whose contempt flows from their inner security in their own position; Psa 73:6 (vc=33959, M08-A2-VCG-02): "pride is their necklace" — pride as a displayed ornament worn from a settled inner state. Material or power advantage: the ga.on proud-might corpus (M08-E) establishes that structural power without accountability enables the outward extension of CHAR-1 as domination. Absence of relational accountability: Dan 11:36 (vc=34235, M08-A1-VCG-02) — "the king shall do as he wills" — unconstrained power enabling the fullest extension. The enabling conditions are internal (settled self-elevation) rather than external — CHAR-1 extends outward from an inner posture that has been established, not from a reactive impulse.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The enabling conditions for CHAR-2 directed toward others: (a) perceived power advantage — Mar 10:42 (vc=55588): "rulers who lord it over" — structural power position that enables domineering; Mat 24:49 (vc=55613): servant who assumes "my master is delayed" — perceived absence of accountability; (b) contempt for others' legitimate standing — Psa 119:69 (vc=34100): lying against the psalmist; Psa 119:85 (vc=34102): setting pitfalls; (c) the settled insolent identity — Pro 21:24 (vc=34096, M08-B-VCG-02): the scoffer as a stable person-type from whose inner posture CHAR-2 flows outward.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

For VCG-01: alazoneia as the inner disposition (Jam 4:16, vc=33866) — the inner boasting-orientation generates the social claim. Trust in creaturely assets (Psa 49:6, vc=33355, M08-C-VCG-01): confidence in one's wealth enables the boast about one's wealth. For VCG-03: genuine love for the community (2Cor 7:4, vc=33917: "I have great pride in you; I am filled with comfort") — relational affection grounds the God-directed community boast.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The enabling conditions for CHAR-4 extended toward others: (a) perceived cognitive superiority (knowledge without love — 1Cor 8:1, vc=33935: knowing more than others generates inflation); (b) partisan tribal alignment (1Cor 4:6, vc=33937: loyalty to one leader over another creates us-vs-them cognitive inflation); (c) perceived absence of accountability (1Cor 4:18, vc=33938: the presumed absence of authority enables contemptuous confidence toward the absent authority figure).

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

The enabling conditions for CHAR-5 directed toward others: (a) structural power that makes the other's resistance or response ineffective (Eze 16:30: shal.le.tet — imperious, unrestrained self-will enabled by structural authority); (b) the self-sufficiency conviction that renders others as objects rather than subjects of genuine moral concern (Isa 47:8: "I am, and there is no one besides me" — the relational frame that excludes the other); (c) material ease that masks the other's need (Eze 16:49: prosperous ease enabling the neglect of the poor and needy).

---

##### T4.3.3 — What does the evidence reveal about what the person must have received or become before they can genuinely give this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The evidence indicates that CHAR-1 is generated internally rather than received from outside and passed on. Mar 7:22 (vc=33928, M08-A4-VCG-01): pride among "the evil things that flow out of a person" — the generative direction is outward from within. 2Ti 3:2 (vc=1899, M08-A4-VCG-01): filautos (self-love) as the root from which pride, boasting, and arrogance all flow — the person must have developed the self-love root orientation before CHAR-1 can be extended outward. The occasion-triggers (prosperity — Deu 8:14, vc=34223; power — 2Ch 26:16, vc=34044; beauty — Eze 28:17, vc=34047) confirm that CHAR-1's extension begins when the person has received goods from God and then misattributed them as self-generated, activating the self-love root into the CHAR-1 posture that then extends outward toward others as contempt and domination.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 extended toward others requires: the settled inner posture of za.don/zed insolence as a dispositional state (Pro 21:24, vc=34096, M08-B-VCG-02), the cognitive self-deception that overestimates one's own authority (Obd 3, vc=34108; Jer 49:16, vc=34115, M08-B-VCG-02), and the removal of God-fear from the inner horizon (Psa 86:14, vc=34097). These are not received from outside but generated internally from the self-authorising will.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

For VCG-01: the self-origination illusion (1Cor 4:7, vc=33871 — the inner cognitive state of treating received goods as self-generated) and the alazoneia inner orientation. For VCG-03: receiving grace, reconciliation, and community relationship — 2Cor 7:4 (vc=33917): Paul's overflowing comfort and joy are the received conditions from which the community boast emerges; Rom 5:11 (vc=33876): receiving reconciliation through Christ is what grounds the God-directed boasting.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4 requires the receipt of some cognitive content (knowledge — 1Cor 8:1; partisan allegiance — 1Cor 4:6; spiritual experience — Col 2:18, vc=33941) which is then misprocessed into self-inflation. The characteristic requires received content to inflate — unlike CHAR-1 which generates from the self-love root without external stimulus. CHAR-4 is specifically triggered by received cognitive goods (knowledge, experience, allegiance) that generate the false self-picture through misattribution.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5 requires the receipt of genuine structural goods: military power (Eze 30:6 — Egypt's actual military might), material wealth (Eze 28:5 — Tyre's actual wealth), physical height/fortification (Jer 49:16 — Edom's actual mountain fortress), or ease (Eze 16:49 — Sodom's actual material abundance). Unlike CHAR-1 (which arises from the self-love root without structural prerequisites), CHAR-5 specifically requires the prior receipt of genuine structural power or position as its enabling condition. The characteristic is the misuse of genuine goods, not a delusion about goods one does not have.

---

##### T4.3.4 — If the evidence is silent on the giving direction, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The giving direction is extensively evidenced as contempt, predatory aggression, and domination (Psa 10:2, vc=33963; Psa 36:11, vc=33966; Psa 73:6, vc=33959; Psa 17:10, vc=34028; Psa 31:18, vc=33964). Not silent.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Giving direction evidenced as domination, predation, and contemptuous insolence (Mar 10:42; Mat 24:49; Psa 119:85; Isa 3:5). Not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Giving direction evidenced in two forms: VCG-01 social self-claim and VCG-03 community commendation. Not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Giving direction evidenced as partisan favouritism, contemptuous presumption, and intellectual condescension (1Cor 4:6; 1Cor 4:18; 1Cor 8:1 context). Not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Giving direction evidenced as structural contempt, social indifference, and exploitation (Eze 16:49; Hab 2:9; Eze 16:30). Not silent.

---

#### T4.4 — Human Interface — Receiving

##### T4.4.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being received by a person from another — and if so, how does it operate in that reception?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Yes — as the crushing experience of contempt, oppressive dominance, and sustained trampling. Psa 123:4 (vc=33953, M08-A4-VCG-03): "our soul has had more than enough of the scorn of those who are at ease, of the contempt of the proud" — reception of CHAR-1 as saturating contempt that overwhelms the inner person. Psa 13:2 (vc=34241, M08-A4-VCG-03): the enemy's exaltation over the psalmist produces "sorrow in my heart all the day" — reception as sustained oppressive weight on the inner person. Psa 56:2 (vc=34163, M08-A4-VCG-03): "my enemies trample on me all day long, for many attack me proudly" — reception as sustained physical and relational assault operating "from a position of felt superiority." Psa 140:5 (vc=33954, M08-A4-VCG-02): "the arrogant have hidden a trap for me, and with cords they have spread a net" — reception as calculating predatory entrapment.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Yes — as sustained oppression and unjust social aggression. Psa 119:51 (vc=34099, M08-B-VCG-02): "the insolent utterly deride me, yet I do not turn away from your law" — the psalmist receives sustained contemptuous derision from the insolent. Psa 119:85 (vc=34102): "the insolent have dug pitfalls for me" — predatory entrapment as the form of received CHAR-2. Psa 119:122 (vc=34103): "let not the insolent oppress me" — oppression as the sustained experience of receiving CHAR-2 from another. Psa 86:14 (vc=34097): "a band of ruthless men seek my life; they do not set God before them."

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Yes. 2Cor 9:4 (vc=33920, M08-C-VCG-03): Paul and the Macedonians arriving to find the Corinthians unprepared would receive Paul's boasting about their readiness as an exposed empty claim — the boasting creates a social debt in those who receive it. 1Cor 5:6 (vc=33903, M08-C-VCG-01): the community receiving its members' boasting undergoes corruption (leaven) — the boast is received by the community and produces internal moral decay. VCG-03: 2Cor 1:14 (vc=33907): mutual boasting — each receiving the other's boasting as relational affirmation.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Yes — as communal disorder and relational disruption. 2Cor 12:20 (vc=33942, M08-D-VCG-02): fusiōsis in a cluster of relational sins that Paul fears finding in Corinth — the community receives CHAR-4 as one element of a broader relational disorder pattern. 1Cor 5:2 (vc=33940, M08-D-VCG-01): the community that should be mourning is instead puffed up — the community as a whole has received CHAR-4's cognitive distortion, preventing collective appropriate response to moral failure.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Yes — as structural exploitation and social neglect. Eze 16:49 (vc=33979, M08-E-VCG-01): the poor and needy receive CHAR-5 as the absence of aid from those with structural power and ease — received as social abandonment. Hab 2:9 (vc=34169, M08-E-VCG-02): those from whom unjust gain is taken receive CHAR-5 as economic exploitation in the service of another's self-securing elevation. The victims of CHAR-5 are primarily those with less structural power — the poor (Eze 16:49), those exploited for another's gain (Hab 2:9).

---

##### T4.4.2 — What inner conditions enable or block reception of this characteristic from another person?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (S)

The verse evidence is silent on the inner conditions that enable or block the impact of CHAR-1 when received from another. Psa 123:4 (vc=33953, M08-A4-VCG-03) evidences that the psalmist is overwhelmed by the proud person's contempt, but the verse does not specify what inner conditions would mitigate or prevent this impact. Psa 131:1 (vc=34059, vc=34224) presents the deliberate inner posture that refuses CHAR-1 for the self, but this is about not possessing CHAR-1 rather than about resisting it when directed toward oneself by another. The evidence does not address the victim's inner conditions as a variable in reception.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (S)

The verse evidence is silent on the inner conditions that enable or block the impact of CHAR-2 when received. The psalmist's response to received CHAR-2 is appeal to God (Psa 119:122; Psa 86:14) and steadfastness in God's law (Psa 119:51), but the evidence does not specify these as conditions that mitigate the impact.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

The evidence reveals that reception depends on the boasting register. VCG-01 boasting by others: 2Cor 11:16–17 (vc=33893, vc=33922, M08-C-VCG-02): the expected reception of CHAR-3 is "foolishness" — listeners perceive it as foolishness. VCG-02 examined boasting: 2Cor 5:12 (vc=33872, M08-C-VCG-02): Paul invites the Corinthians to have something to say to those who boast in outward appearance — the community's ability to receive examined boasting is presented as a resource.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (S)

The verse evidence in §3.C is largely silent on specific inner conditions that enable or block the reception of CHAR-4 from another. The community context of 1Cor 4–5 evidences a community that has received CHAR-4 without evidenced resistance, but the evidence does not specify what inner conditions determine this.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (S)

The verse evidence is largely silent on the inner conditions that determine how CHAR-5's social impact is received by victims. The evidence focuses on the structural dynamic (the powerful neglecting the powerless) rather than on the victim's inner-being conditions.

---

##### T4.4.3 — What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic from another but does not receive it?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (S)

The verse evidence does not directly address the inner-being state of a person who encounters CHAR-1 from another and successfully resists its crushing impact. The psalmist's experience in Psa 123:4 (vc=33953, M08-A4-VCG-03) is of being overwhelmed rather than successfully resisting. What the evidence does offer is the experience of the psalmist who brings CHAR-1 to God: Psa 94:2 (vc=33952, M08-A4-VCG-02) — "Rise up, O judge of the earth; repay to the proud what they deserve!" — the person under CHAR-1's impact turns to God's judicial authority rather than directly resisting. This suggests a theologically-directed coping posture (appeal to divine justice), but the evidence does not name the inner-being state of one who encounters CHAR-1 from another without being overcome by it.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The psalmist's testimony provides direct evidence. Psa 119:51 (vc=34099, M08-B-VCG-02): "the insolent utterly deride me" — sustained derision pressing on the inner person; the psalmist maintains inner stability through adherence to divine law. Psa 119:78 (vc=34101): "the insolent have wronged me with falsehood; as for me, I will meditate on your precepts" — the inner response to received CHAR-2 is doubled commitment to the divine standard that CHAR-2 despises. Psa 86:14 (vc=34097): facing "a band of ruthless men" the psalmist turns to God as the rescuing judge. The inner-being state is pressed-upon, appealing to God, and anchored in the divine law the insolent reject.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

For VCG-01 reception: 1Cor 5:6 (vc=33903, M08-C-VCG-01): community receiving boasting = corruption spreading; 2Cor 9:4 (vc=33920): receiving empty boasting creates social embarrassment and exposure. For VCG-03 reception: 2Cor 7:4 (vc=33917): receiving Paul's boasting about them generates "overflowing joy" in Paul; 1Th 2:19 (vc=33913): the community received as Paul's boasting-object becomes his "hope and joy and crown of boasting" — the receiving community is in a state of being loved and commended.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

2Cor 12:20 (vc=33942, M08-D-VCG-02) provides the indirect evidence: Paul fears finding fusiōsis (conceit/inflation) alongside quarreling, jealousy, anger, hostility, slander, gossip, and disorder — all relational disorders that co-occur with CHAR-4 as its relational consequences. The person who receives CHAR-4 from another (the target of the conceited person's condescension or contempt) experiences the same relational pattern — strife, hostility, quarreling. The community of 1Cor 5:2 that has collectively received CHAR-4 is in a state of inappropriate equanimity (not mourning when they should be).

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (S)

The verse evidence in §3.D does not directly describe the inner-being state of those who receive CHAR-5 from structural power. Eze 16:49 (vc=33979) identifies the poor and needy as the object of CHAR-5's neglect but does not describe their inner experience.

---

##### T4.4.4 — If the evidence is silent on the receiving direction, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The receiving direction is evidenced as overwhelming inner saturation, sustained sorrow, and predatory entrapment (Psa 123:4, vc=33953; Psa 13:2, vc=34241; Psa 56:2, vc=34163; Psa 140:5, vc=33954). Inner conditions enabling or blocking reception (T4.4.2–3) are silent.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The inner experience of receiving CHAR-2 is evidenced in the Psa 119 corpus and Psa 86:14 as sustained oppression and appeal to God. Not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Receiving direction evidenced in both corrupt (VCG-01) and joy-generating (VCG-03) forms. Not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Receiving direction evidenced as community relational disorder and inappropriate equanimity (2Cor 12:20; 1Cor 5:2). Inner conditions for reception are largely silent (T4.4.2).

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (S)

The inner experience of receiving CHAR-5 is largely silent in §3.D. The victims of CHAR-5 are identified (poor and needy — Eze 16:49; those exploited — Hab 2:9) but their inner-being states are not described. Confirmed.

---

#### T4.5 — Human Interface — Boundaries

##### T4.5.1 — Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic operates differently within existing relational bonds versus across relational distance or difference?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The evidence shows CHAR-1 operating within both close relational bonds and across distance, with no evidence that proximity changes its essential character. Within close bonds: Deu 17:20 (vc=34231, M08-A1-VCG-01) — the king's heart lifted "above his brothers" — the relational bond is the covenant community; CHAR-1 operates as hierarchical self-elevation within that bond. 2Ch 26:16 (vc=34044, M08-A1-VCG-01): Uzziah's pride manifesting within his covenant relationship with God — the closest relational bond. Across distance: the national-pride corpus (M08-A3) evidences CHAR-1 in international contexts — Moab's pride against Israel (Isa 16:6, vc=33989, M08-A3-VCG-01), Babylon's pride as a global power (Isa 13:19, vc=33987, M08-A3-VCG-02). The characteristic operates across both registers without apparent difference in structure, though its specific relational consequences (contempt, domination) are shaped by the relational context.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The evidence shows CHAR-2 operating both within close relational bonds and across distance. Within close bonds: Mat 24:49 (vc=55613, M08-B-VCG-03): the servant who beats "fellow servants" — within the same household/community bond. Mar 10:41 (vc=55587): the ten disciples' indignation at James and John — within the inner circle. Isa 3:5 (vc=34212, M08-B-VCG-02): "youth being insolent to the elder" — within the intergenerational community bond. Across distance: Jer 50:29 (vc=34127, M08-B-VCG-01): Babylon's defiance of the Holy One of Israel — the great power's CHAR-2 against God.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Yes. Within close relational bonds: 2Cor 7:4 (vc=33917) and 1Th 2:19 (vc=33913, M08-C-VCG-03) — Paul's boasting about his communities is deeply relational, grounded in shared history and genuine love. The VCG-02 corpus (2Cor 10–12) shows CHAR-3 operating within a strained relational bond (Paul and the Corinthians in conflict) — the examined boasting serves the relational purpose of defending apostolic integrity within an existing community relationship. Across relational distance: VCG-01 boasting of wealth or achievements is more typical of cross-distance social display.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The evidence evidences CHAR-4 operating within close relational bonds specifically. 1Cor 4:6 (vc=33937, M08-D-VCG-01): the Corinthian community's partisan conceit within the community — existing bonds of loyalty to teachers becoming the occasion for inter-group inflation. 1Cor 5:2 (vc=33940, M08-D-VCG-01): the community's collective CHAR-4 response to an internal moral failure — within the existing bond of the community. 2Cor 12:20 (vc=33942, M08-D-VCG-02): Paul's fear of finding fusiōsis within the Corinthian community he knows personally.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

The evidence evidences CHAR-5 operating primarily in the structural-power relational register, where distance from the vulnerable is itself a product of the structural elevation. Eze 16:49 (vc=33979, M08-E-VCG-01): Sodom's CHAR-5 creates the relational distance from the poor — the ease-dwelling community is structurally separated from the needy neighbour. Obd 3 (vc=65674, M08-E-VCG-02): "you who live in the clefts of the rock, in your lofty dwelling" — the physical elevation creates the relational distance from others that reinforces CHAR-5's self-sufficiency conviction.

---

##### T4.5.2 — Does this characteristic operate within covenantal contexts only, or does it cross covenantal boundaries?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

CHAR-1 crosses covenantal boundaries consistently. Within Israel's covenant: Amo 6:8 (vc=34002, M08-A3-VCG-03) — "I abhor the pride of Jacob"; Hos 5:5 (vc=34000, M08-A3-VCG-03) — "the pride of Israel testifies to his face." Outside the covenant: Isa 16:6 (vc=33989, M08-A3-VCG-01) — Moab's pride; Isa 13:19 (vc=33987, M08-A3-VCG-02) — Babylon's pride. NT evidence confirms the trans-covenantal scope: Rom 1:30 (vc=33932, M08-A4-VCG-01) — haughtiness as a vice of a morally disordered mind generally; 2Ti 3:2 (vc=33933, M08-A4-VCG-01) — arrogance as a characteristic of "people" in the last days without covenantal limitation. Isa 2:12 (vc=33957, M08-A3-VCG-04) addresses "all that is proud and lofty" universally. CHAR-1 is a universal human characteristic whose divine assessment and consequence are consistent regardless of covenantal status.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

CHAR-2 crosses covenantal boundaries. Within covenant: Israel's repeated presumption (Deu 1:43; Neh 9:16/29), the false prophet from within Israel (Deu 18:20), the presumptuous judge-defier from within Israel's community (Deu 17:12). Outside covenant: Pharaoh/Egypt (Exo 18:11, vc=34121; Neh 9:10), Babylon (Jer 50:29, vc=34127; Jer 50:31, vc=34116). NT: self-willed false teachers and domineering leaders without covenantal qualification (2Pe 2:10; Tit 1:7). CHAR-2 is a universal human characteristic not limited to covenantal context.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

CHAR-3 crosses covenantal boundaries. Within covenant: Rom 2:17/23 (vc=33882/33883, M08-C-VCG-01) — boasting in the Law from within Jewish covenantal identity. Outside covenant: 1Jo 2:16 (vc=33865, M08-C-VCG-01): "the pride of life" (alazoneia) as a worldly disposition without covenantal qualification. Rom 1:30 (vc=33867): alazōn in a universal vice catalogue. The NT examines CHAR-3 across both Jewish-covenantal and Gentile-universal contexts.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The 12-verse §3.C corpus is entirely from Pauline NT communities (1Cor, 2Cor, Col, Rom, 1Ti, 2Ti). There is no Hebrew OT evidence in CHAR-4's corpus. Within the NT corpus, CHAR-4 is evidenced across multiple communities (Corinthian — 1Cor/2Cor; Roman — Rom 12:3; Colossian — Col 2:18; Pastoral — 1Ti/2Ti). The evidence addresses Christian community contexts without restricting CHAR-4 to a specific covenantal framework — Rom 12:3 addresses believers in general.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

CHAR-5 crosses all covenantal boundaries, evidenced across: Israel (Lev 26:19, vc=33982; Eze 33:28, vc=33999), Sodom (Eze 16:49, vc=33979), Egypt (Eze 30:6–32:12, M08-E-VCG-01), Tyre (Eze 28:5, vc=34046), Edom (Jer 49:16, vc=34167; Obd 3, vc=65674), Babylon (Isa 47:8, vc=9563; Jer 51:53, vc=65670), Judah/Eze 19:11 rulers (vc=54398), and the wealthy in NT communities (1Ti 6:17, vc=60878). CHAR-5 is the M08 characteristic most extensively evidenced across different national and cultural contexts — its structural-power medium operates wherever power and wealth exist.

---

##### T4.5.3 — What does the evidence reveal about the relational scope of this characteristic — who is included and who is not?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The relational scope of CHAR-1 is universal — no person, people, or period is evidenced as exempt from either possessing CHAR-1 or being subject to God's opposition to it. Pro 16:5 (vc=12083, M08-A1-VCG-03): "everyone who is arrogant in heart" — scope is universal by definition. Isa 2:12 (vc=33957, M08-A3-VCG-04): "the Lord of hosts has a day against all that is proud and lofty" — the eschatological judgment encompasses all, without national, ethnic, or covenantal qualification. The day-of-the-Lord corpus (M08-A3-VCG-04) — Deu 32:27 (vc=65750), Isa 2:11–12, 2:17, 10:33, 25:11 — addresses collective humanity as the subject of CHAR-1's universal expression and universal judgment. Job 41:34 (vc=12089, vc=34614, M08-A4-VCG-04): "he is king over all the sons of pride" — the category "sons of pride" encompasses creatures universally.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The relational scope is comprehensive: CHAR-2 is evidenced in individuals (Deu 18:20: the false prophet), communities (Neh 9:16: the ancestors collectively), nations (Jer 50:29: Babylon), and in every historical period from the Exodus to the NT. Pro 11:2 (vc=34109, M08-B-VCG-02): "when arrogance comes, disgrace follows" — stated as a universal pattern without covenantal or situational limitation.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Universal scope. VCG-01 applies to wise, mighty, and rich without qualification (Jer 9:23, vc=33342), to Gentiles (Rom 1:30, vc=33867), and to law-keepers (Rom 2:23, vc=33883). VCG-03 applies within the Christian community specifically (Rom 5:2; Phili 3:3; 1Th 2:19). VCG-02 is specifically Pauline-apostolic but evidences principles of legitimate self-commendation with broader applicability (Gal 6:4, vc=33908: "each one test his own work" — universally addressed).

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4's evidenced relational scope is the NT Christian community in multiple locations. Rom 12:3 (vc=60866, M08-D-VCG-02): the universal address ("to everyone among you") applies CHAR-4's correction universally within the believing community. 2Ti 3:4 (vc=33926, M08-D-VCG-02): tufoō in the end-times character list — universal eschatological scope without community limitation. CHAR-4's scope is broad within the human community, though the 12-verse corpus addresses it specifically through NT community contexts.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

The relational scope is universal in the structural-power domain: any nation, community, or individual with real structural power (military, economic, positional, geographical) is evidenced as a potential site of CHAR-5. The ga.on proud-might corpus covers Israel and Judah, Egypt, Sodom, Tyre, Edom, and Babylon — the full historical range of ancient Near Eastern power-holders. 1Ti 6:17 (vc=60878, M08-E-VCG-02) extends the scope to individual wealth-holders in NT communities. CHAR-5's scope is wherever structural power exists.

---

##### T4.5.4 — If the evidence is silent on relational boundaries, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Relational scope confirmed as universal: CHAR-1 is evidenced across individuals, communities, and nations without covenantal or ethnic limitation. Not silent.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Relational scope confirmed as universal across covenantal, national, and historical contexts. Not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Relational scope confirmed as universal (VCG-01), community-specific (VCG-03), and apostolic-examined (VCG-02). Not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Relational scope evidenced as NT community-wide, with universal application (Rom 12:3). Not silent.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Relational scope confirmed as universal across nations, communities, and historical periods wherever structural power exists. Not silent.

---

#### T4.6 — Spiritual Beings Interface

##### T4.6.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to other spiritual beings — angelic or adversarial — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Partially. Dan 11:36 (vc=34235, M08-A1-VCG-02): "the king shall do as he wills. He shall exalt himself and magnify himself above every god" — CHAR-1 explicitly directed against the divine order, extending beyond any single deity to claim supremacy over "every god." Isa 14:13 (vc=34233, M08-A4-VCG-05): "I will ascend to heaven; above the stars of God I will set my throne on high" — the will's self-elevation into the heavenly domain, claiming ascendancy above the heavenly order. 2Ki 19:22 (vc=34160, vc=65755, M08-A4-VCG-05) and Isa 37:23 (vc=34304, M08-A4-VCG-05): the Assyrian king's pride directed against "the Holy One of Israel" with eyes lifted to the heights and voice raised — CHAR-1 operating as defiance directed against the divine person specifically. These verses evidence CHAR-1 in the vertical-against-God direction but do not directly address other spiritual beings (angelic or adversarial) as distinct from God.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Yes. 2Pe 2:10 (vc=4670, vc=42739, M08-B-VCG-03): "the bold man [tolmētēs]... bold in blasphemy" and "self-willed, they do not tremble before the glorious ones" — CHAR-2 directed against spiritual beings designated as "glorious ones." This is the most direct evidence in the 45-verse corpus of CHAR-2 operating in the spiritual-beings interface. The "glorious ones" (whether angelic beings or other spiritual authorities) are the specific object of CHAR-2's self-willed refusal to tremble — the reckless boldness of tolmētēs is directed precisely at what should command reverence.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (S)

The verse evidence in §3.B does not evidence CHAR-3 operating in relation to angelic or adversarial spiritual beings specifically. The spiritual reference points in VCG-03 are God/Christ/Spirit as the objects of God-directed boasting (Phili 3:3: worship by the Spirit; 1Cor 1:31: boast in the Lord) rather than other spiritual beings.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Yes — through the adversarial paradigm reference. 1Ti 3:6 (vc=33924, M08-D-VCG-02): "he may become puffed up with conceit and fall into the condemnation of the devil" — the devil is explicitly invoked as the paradigm case of CHAR-4's judgment. This is the most direct connection between a human inner-being characteristic and adversarial spiritual activity in M08: CHAR-4's conceited cognitive self-inflation replicates the adversarial paradigm and receives the same condemnation.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (S)

The verse evidence in §3.D does not directly evidence CHAR-5 operating in relation to angelic or adversarial spiritual beings. The characteristic operates in the human structural-power register.

---

##### T4.6.2 — Is this characteristic a site of adversarial activity — something that can be attacked, distorted, or weaponised by adversarial spiritual powers?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (G)

The verse evidence in §3 is silent on adversarial spiritual powers distorting, attacking, or weaponising CHAR-1. No verse in the 149-verse corpus directly addresses Satan, demons, or adversarial spiritual beings in relation to CHAR-1's operation. The Isa 14:13 passage (vc=34233, M08-A4-VCG-05) carries adversarial/Satanic resonances in the Christian interpretive tradition, but its primary referent in the evidence as read is the Babylonian king's inner volitional declaration ("you said in your heart"). Whether adversarial spiritual beings exploit CHAR-1 as a site of attack would require cross-cluster verse investigation beyond the current §3 corpus. Noted as a gap.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (G)

The verse evidence in §3.A does not directly address adversarial spiritual powers distorting or exploiting CHAR-2. 2Pe 2:10 (vc=42739) addresses CHAR-2 directed against spiritual beings but from the human side, not adversarial beings exploiting CHAR-2 in humans. Whether adversarial spiritual powers weaponise CHAR-2 would require cross-cluster investigation beyond §3.A. Noted as a gap.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (G)

The verse evidence in §3.B does not directly address adversarial spiritual powers exploiting or weaponising CHAR-3. 1Jo 2:16 (vc=33865, M08-C-VCG-01): "the pride of life is not from the Father but is from the world" — the worldly origin of CHAR-3 may imply adversarial influence, but this is not directly evidenced. Noted as a gap.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

1Ti 3:6 (vc=33924, M08-D-VCG-02) evidences the adversarial connection most directly: "the condemnation of the devil" — the devil is not simply an analogy but the historical paradigm case whose condemnation CHAR-4 participates in. Whether this implies active adversarial exploitation of human CHAR-4 (the devil weaponising it) or merely parallel condemnation is not directly evidenced in §3.C. The verse names CHAR-4 as falling into the adversary's condemnation-category, which is at minimum a typological connection and may imply adversarial exploitation.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (G)

The verse evidence does not directly address adversarial spiritual powers exploiting CHAR-5. Given CHAR-5's structural basis (real power and wealth), the question of adversarial exploitation is plausible but not evidenced in §3.D. Noted as a gap.

---

##### T4.6.3 — Is this characteristic communicated, strengthened, or mediated through angelic ministry in the evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (S)

The verse evidence is silent on angelic ministry in relation to CHAR-1. No verse in §3 evidences angelic involvement in the generation, expression, strengthening, or reversal of CHAR-1. The 149-verse corpus contains no angelic-ministry content pertaining to this characteristic.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (S)

The verse evidence is silent on angelic ministry in relation to CHAR-2 in §3.A.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (S)

The verse evidence is silent on angelic ministry in relation to CHAR-3 in §3.B.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (S)

The verse evidence is silent on angelic ministry in relation to CHAR-4 in §3.C.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (S)

The verse evidence is silent on angelic ministry in relation to CHAR-5 in §3.D.

---

##### T4.6.4 — If the evidence is silent on the spiritual beings interface, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (S)

The evidence is silent on the spiritual beings interface in two of its three dimensions: (a) adversarial spiritual activity in relation to CHAR-1 is a gap (T4.6.2 — insufficient evidence, further investigation needed); (b) angelic ministry in relation to CHAR-1 is not evidenced (T4.6.3). The partial evidence for T4.6.1 (CHAR-1 directed against the divine order, including Dan 11:36 and Isa 14:13) concerns the human-to-God vertical direction rather than the human-to-other-spiritual-beings interface specifically.

---

Angelic ministry in relation to CHAR-2 not evidenced. Adversarial exploitation of CHAR-2 is a gap (T4.6.2). Direct evidence of CHAR-2 toward "glorious ones" is confirmed in 2Pe 2:10 (vc=4670, vc=42739).
