Its noun derivatives kauchēma (G2745) name the object/ground of boasting (1Cor 9:15, vc=33905: "my ground for boasting") and kauchēsis (G2746) names the act itself (2Cor 1:12, vc=33912: "the testimony of our conscience... our boasting"). Alazoneia (G0212) operates as a noun (the quality of boastful display — Jam 4:16, vc=33866; 1Jo 2:16, vc=33865). Alazōn (G0213) as a substantive adjective/noun names the person-type (the braggart — Rom 1:30, vc=33867; 2Ti 3:2, vc=33868). The grammatical range covers: verb (the act), person-type noun (the braggart), quality noun (the boastful disposition), and ground noun (the boasting-object) — covering every grammatical angle of the characteristic.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Taking fusioō (G5448) as the primary term: it operates as a verbal form (to inflate — passive and active) across all its §3.C uses: "is puffed up" (present passive — 1Cor 4:6, vc=33937: "some are puffed up"), "puffs up" (present active — 1Cor 8:1, vc=33935: "knowledge puffs up"). Its nominal derivative fusiōsis (G5450) operates as a noun naming the quality/condition (2Cor 12:20, vc=33942). Huperfroneō (G5252) operates as a verb with complement: "think more highly [than you ought]" (Rom 12:3, vc=60866) — the verb requiring a comparative object to complete its meaning. Tufoō (G5187) operates in the passive: "being puffed up" (perfect passive — 1Ti 3:6, vc=33924: "puffed up with conceit"; 1Ti 6:4, vc=33925: "puffed up"; 2Ti 3:4, vc=33926: "swollen with conceit"). The grammatical dominance of the passive voice for tufoō is significant: the person is described as being-in-a-state-of-inflation rather than actively inflating themselves — the inflated condition is named as something that has happened to them.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Taking ga.on (H1347) as the primary term: it operates primarily as a noun naming the quality of proud might — "the pride of your power" (Lev 26:19, vc=33982: "ga.on 'uz'khem"); "Egypt's proud might" (Eze 30:6, vc=33996: "ga.on Mitsrayim"). Ga.on functions as a construct genitive qualifier (the pride OF your power; the proud might OF Egypt) — it names an inner quality that belongs to an entity possessing structural power. It does not operate as a verb in §3.D (unlike ga.vah which is verbal in Eze 28:5). The grammatical range: construct genitive noun (naming the proud-might quality of a power-holding entity). Ma.rom operates as a noun (place of height: Jer 49:16; Obd 3; Hab 2:9; Eze 19:11) — naming the physical-structural position rather than the inner quality. Hupsēlofroneō (G5309) operates as a verb in 1Ti 6:17 — an action commanded against.

---

##### T7.1.3 — What is the semantic range of the primary term — across what breadth of meaning does it operate?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The rum (H7311A/H7312) root has the widest semantic range of any CHAR-1 term, operating across four distinct meaning registers evidenced in the broader biblical corpus: (a) CHAR-1 register — human arrogant self-elevation (Deu 8:14, vc=34223; Isa 14:13, vc=34233; Dan 11:36, vc=34235 — the current corpus); (b) M22 register — divine exaltation and genuine majesty (the 122 set-aside M22-register rum verses confirm this range is present in the same term); (c) God-lifting-up the humble — the righteous lifted up by God's act (Psa 75:10, vc=34264, M08-A4-VCG-05: "the horns of the righteous shall be lifted up" — God as the agent); (d) Providential elevation of the Israelite community out of Egypt (Exo 14:8, vc=34239, M08-A4-VCG-05: going out "with a high hand" — bold, God-enabled). The g-'-h root similarly ranges from human pride (M08 register) to divine majesty (M22 register). The semantic range of the primary terms encompasses the full elevation spectrum — from the creature's illegitimate self-elevation (CHAR-1), through God's proper exaltation of the humble, to God's own genuine majesty (M22).

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Zid operates across two primary semantic registers within the biblical corpus: (a) CHAR-2 register — wilful presumptuous transgression of a divine limit (Deu 1:43; Deu 18:20; Neh 9:10/16/29; Jer 50:29 — the current corpus); (b) physical cooking sense — "the pottage he was boiling" (Gen 25:29) — the physical boiling from which the metaphor derives. The semantic range is narrower than CHAR-1's rum/ga.on terms: zid's primary figurative meaning in the Hebrew Bible is specifically the presumptuous, wilful quality of transgression, without the broader range across divine majesty and legitimate elevation. This narrower semantic range confirms CHAR-2 as a more specifically targeted characteristic than CHAR-1's broader elevation vocabulary.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Kauchaomai has the widest semantic range of any CHAR-3 term, spanning: (a) condemned self-directed boasting (VCG-01: Rom 2:17, vc=33882: boasting in the law while breaking it; 1Cor 1:29, vc=33877: the boasting that God's election is designed to eliminate); (b) Pauline examined self-commendation (VCG-02: 2Cor 10:13, vc=33888: bounded boasting within God-assigned sphere; 2Cor 12:9, vc=33870: boasting of weaknesses); (c) God-directed glorying (VCG-03: Rom 5:2, vc=33874: boasting in hope of God's glory; Phili 3:3, vc=33879: glorying in Christ Jesus). This three-register semantic range is the most complex of any term in M08: the same verb covers all three moral evaluations depending on direction. Ha.lal similarly spans self-directed boasting (VCG-01) and God-directed praise (the set-aside M22 ha.lal verses that carry the praise register).

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Fusioō operates across two primary semantic registers in the NT: (a) CHAR-4 register — cognitive self-inflation (1Cor 4:6; 4:18; 4:19; 5:2; 8:1; 13:4; Col 2:18 — M08-D-VCG-01); (b) No significant positive or divine-attribute register — unlike rum/ga.on (CHAR-1's vocabulary) or kauchaomai (CHAR-3's vocabulary), fusioō does not appear in a divine-majesty or approved-form register. The semantic range is narrower and more uniformly negative than CHAR-1's or CHAR-3's vocabulary: fusioō is consistently used for the condemned form of cognitive self-inflation, without the multi-register spanning of the other M08 vocabulary. This confirms CHAR-4 as the most lexically focused of the M08 characteristics.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Ga.on (H1347) in M08-CHAR-5 operates in the proud-might subset — a subset of its broader semantic range. Beyond CHAR-5, ga.on spans: (a) M22 divine majesty/exaltation (Exo 15:1 — "I will sing to the Lord, for he has triumphed gloriously [ga.on]" — set aside in Phase 5.5 as M22 content); (b) M23 legitimate national strength (set aside in Phase 5.5 — 122 M22-register verses including legitimate strength uses). The §3.D corpus retains only the proud-might subset where ga.on evidences strength misused as self-exaltation. Ma.rom similarly spans M22 (God's lofty dwelling — set aside) and M23 (fortified heights as legitimate military strategy) alongside the CHAR-5 register. The semantic range of the primary CHAR-5 terms is thus deliberately subset through the Phase 5.5 set-aside process.

---

##### T7.1.4 — Does the vocabulary include terms that distinguish distinct aspects of this characteristic — disposition versus act, received versus given, condition versus quality?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Yes, across three dimensions. Disposition versus act: the noun/adjective forms (ga.on, ga.a.vah, ge.eh, ga.vo.ah, huperēfanos) name the dispositional quality or person-type; the verbal forms (rum, ga.vah, ga.ah) name the act of rising or being proud. Pro 16:5 (vc=12083, M08-A1-VCG-03) — "arrogant in heart" (ga.vo.ah) — dispositional; Dan 11:36 (vc=34235, M08-A1-VCG-02) — "he shall exalt himself" (rum verb active) — act. Settled habitual condition versus acute episode: Dan 4:37 (vc=34094, M08-A4-VCG-04) — "those who walk in pride" (ge.vah) — the settled habitual condition of a habituated inner posture; Dan 5:20 (vc=34129, M08-A1-VCG-02) — "his heart was lifted up" (rum passive) — a specific moment of acute elevation. Person-type versus quality: ge.eh (H1343) — the proud person as a type (Job 40:11, vc=33949: "look on everyone who is proud/ge.eh"); ga.on, ga.a.vah — the quality of pride itself. The vocabulary is grammatically differentiated to address CHAR-1 across its full range of manifestation.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Yes. Disposition vs act: za.don (dispositional quality of presumptuousness) vs zid (the verbal act of acting presumptuously). Person-type: zed (the insolent/arrogant person who habitually exhibits CHAR-2). The graduated register: M08-B-VCG-01 (zid — the acute boiling-over act), M08-B-VCG-02 (za.don/zed — the habitual insolence quality and person-type), M08-B-VCG-03 (authadēs, tolmētēs, archō — NT precision terms for self-will and reckless boldness). The vocabulary distinguishes CHAR-2 as act (zid), quality (za.don), and person-type (zed) — the same three-level structure evidenced in CHAR-1 but through different terms.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Yes. Disposition vs act: alazoneia (inner boasting disposition) vs kauchaomai (the verbal/social act of boasting). Person-type: alazōn (the braggart — a stable social identity type — 2Ti 3:2, vc=33868; Rom 1:30, vc=33867). Ground/object: kauchēma (the object one boasts in or about — 1Cor 9:15, vc=33905: apostolic conduct; Phili 1:26, vc=33909: boasting in Christ Jesus). Act itself: kauchēsis (the activity of boasting — 2Cor 1:12, vc=33912: the boasting grounded in conscience). The vocabulary has full grammatical differentiation across disposition, act, person-type, and ground.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Yes. State vs act: tufoō (the state of being inflated — passive) vs fusioō (the active process of inflating — knowledge inflates). Quality vs instance: fusiōsis (the quality of inflation as communal disorder — 2Cor 12:20, vc=33942) vs fusioō (specific instances of puffing up). Measure-exceeding: huperfroneō (the specific cognitive act of exceeding the warranted measure — Rom 12:3, vc=60866) as distinguished from the inflation metaphors. The vocabulary thus distinguishes CHAR-4 as a state (tufoō), a process (fusioō), a communal quality (fusiōsis), and a measure-exceeding cognitive act (huperfroneō).

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Yes. Inner pride vs structural medium: ga.on (inner proud-might confidence) vs ma.rom (physical height as structural medium). Dispositional state vs volitional expression: ga.vah (the heart's settled proud state — Eze 28:5) vs shal.le.tet (the imperious volitional expression of that pride — Eze 16:30). Collective national vs individual: ga.on proud-might (primarily collective national — Egypt, Israel — M08-E-VCG-01) vs hupsēlofroneō (individual wealth-holders — 1Ti 6:17 — M08-E-VCG-02). Affective ground vs cognitive claim: a.din (the affective ease that sustains CHAR-5 — Isa 47:8) vs the ontological self-declaration that CHAR-5 generates ("I am, and there is no one besides me" — Isa 47:8, cognitive). The vocabulary is grammatically and semantically differentiated across the full range of CHAR-5's expression.

---

##### T7.1.5 — Does the vocabulary include a term for the structural opposite or absence of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Not within CHAR-1's own vocabulary, but the evidence consistently pairs CHAR-1 with its structural opposite through contrast. Psa 131:1 (vc=34059, M08-A1-VCG-03) negates the rum root itself: "my heart is NOT lifted up [rum]; my eyes are NOT raised too high" — the absence of CHAR-1 is expressed through its own vocabulary negated. Jam 4:6 (vc=33931, M08-A4-VCG-01) and 1Pe 5:5 (vc=33934, M08-A4-VCG-01) name the opposite explicitly: "gives grace to the humble" — tapeinophrosynē (humility, M09) as CHAR-1's named structural opposite. Pro 29:23 (vc=33960, M08-A4-VCG-04): "he who is lowly in spirit will obtain honour" — anav/lowly as the contrast term. The structural opposite vocabulary belongs to M09 rather than M08-CHAR-1, but it is consistently co-deployed with CHAR-1's vocabulary in the same verses.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Not within CHAR-2's own vocabulary, but the evidence consistently pairs CHAR-2 with its opposite through contrast. Pro 11:2 (vc=34109, M08-B-VCG-02): "when arrogance [za.don] comes, disgrace follows, but with the humble is wisdom" — the humble (anav) as the named opposite. Deu 17:13 (vc=34124, M08-B-VCG-01): "all the people shall hear and fear" — fear (yir.ah) as the inner posture that opposes CHAR-2's fearlessness. Psa 19:13 (vc=34095, M08-B-VCG-02): the psalmist as "your servant" — the servant posture as the relational orientation that CHAR-2's self-willed defiance inverts. The structural opposite vocabulary belongs primarily to the fear-of-God and humility registers (M09-adjacent).

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Not within CHAR-3's own vocabulary, but the evidence consistently pairs CHAR-3 with its opposite through context. Pro 27:2 (adjacent to vc=33359): "let another praise you, and not your own mouth" — receiving-praise-from-another as the opposite of self-boasting. 1Cor 4:7 (vc=33871): "if you received it" — the acknowledgment of received goods is the opposite cognitive posture to the boasting-as-if-not-received. The structural opposite of CHAR-3 is the posture of grateful attribution — acknowledging God as the source of all goods (1Cor 4:7) and receiving commendation from others (Pro 27:2) rather than self-asserting.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Yes, within the same verse. Rom 12:3 (vc=60866, M08-D-VCG-02): "think with sober judgment [sōphronos]" — the same verse that commands against huperfroneō provides the positive alternative: sōphronos (soberly, soundly, within proper measure). 1Cor 8:1 (vc=33935, M08-D-VCG-01): "love builds up [oikodomeō]" — love's building-up is the structural opposite of knowledge's puffing-up within the same verse. The evidence uniquely provides the structural opposite within the same sentences that name CHAR-4, making the alternative immediately legible.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

1Ti 6:17 (vc=60878, M08-E-VCG-02) provides the structural opposite within the same verse: "not to be haughty [hupsēlofroneō]... but... to be generous and ready to share." Generosity and readiness to share are the named opposites of wealth-haughtiness in the NT corpus. The OT corpus implies the structural opposite through the Sodom indictment (Eze 16:49, vc=33979): the positive alternative to CHAR-5 is aiding the poor and needy — the use of structural goods in service of others rather than as the ground for self-elevation.

---

##### T7.1.6 — Does the vocabulary include a person-type term — a term for the one who habitually possesses or exercises this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Yes, explicitly. Ge.eh (H1343): the proud person as a type — Job 40:11 (vc=33949, M08-A4-VCG-02): "everyone who is proud [ge.eh]"; Job 40:12 (vc=33951): "look on everyone who is proud [ge.eh]"; Psa 94:2 (vc=33952, M08-A4-VCG-02): "repay to the proud [ge.eh] what they deserve"; Pro 15:25 (vc=33955, M08-A4-VCG-02): "the proud [ge.eh] person's house." Ga.vo.ah (H1364) functions as a person-type adjective: Psa 101:5 (vc=12085, M08-A1-VCG-03): "an arrogant heart [ga.vo.ah]"; Psa 138:6 (vc=12086, M08-A4-VCG-02): "the haughty [ga.vo.ah] he knows from afar." Huperēfanos (G5244): the arrogant person in NT usage — Luk 1:51 (vc=33930, M08-A1-VCG-03): "the proud [huperēfanos] in the thoughts of their hearts"; Jam 4:6 (vc=33931): "God opposes the proud [huperēfanos]." Additionally, Job 41:34 (vc=34614, M08-A4-VCG-04) evidences a collective person-type: "sons of pride [bene sha.chats]" — a group-level person-type designation for those whose defining inner characteristic is fierce self-assertion.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Yes. Zed (H2086) is the primary person-type term — the arrogant/insolent person as a stable type. Psa 119:21 (vc=34098, M08-B-VCG-02): "the insolent [zed], accursed ones"; Psa 86:14 (vc=34097): "arrogant men [zed] have risen up against me"; Psa 119:51 (vc=34099): "the insolent [zed] utterly deride me"; Pro 21:24 (vc=34096, M08-B-VCG-02): identified as "scoffer." Additionally, tolmētēs (G5113) in 2Pe 2:10 (vc=4670, M08-B-VCG-03) functions as a person-type: the "bold man" who is recklessly presumptuous.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Yes. Alazōn (G0213) — the braggart/boaster as a stable social identity type. Rom 1:30 (vc=33867, M08-C-VCG-01): alazōn in a universal vice catalogue as a person-type. 2Ti 3:2 (vc=33868, M08-C-VCG-01): alazōn in the end-times character list — a type characterised by boastfulness alongside self-love and arrogance. The alazōn is the person for whom public self-assertion is a defining social characteristic.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (S)

The verse evidence does not include a dedicated person-type term for CHAR-4 within §3.C. The fusiōsis noun (2Cor 12:20, vc=33942) names the quality rather than the person-type. There is no equivalent of CHAR-2's zed (the insolent person-type) or CHAR-3's alazōn (the braggart) within CHAR-4's specific vocabulary. The arrogant person of 1Cor 4:18 (vc=33938) is named descriptively as "some" who "are puffed up" rather than through a stable person-type term.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Partially. The ga.on corpus addresses collective national person-types (Egypt — Eze 30:6; Israel — Lev 26:19; Sodom — Eze 16:49) as entities characterised by proud might, but without a stable individual person-type noun. Hupsēlofroneō in 1Ti 6:17 (vc=60878, M08-E-VCG-02) is addressed to "the rich in this present age" as a collective category of person-type. The CHAR-5 corpus addresses communities and categories of people rather than naming a specific individual-level person-type term.

---

##### T7.1.7 — Does the vocabulary include a supplication or seeking term — a term for the act of seeking this characteristic from another?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (S)

The verse evidence is silent on a supplication or seeking term within CHAR-1's vocabulary. CHAR-1 is characterised by its refusal to seek — Psa 10:4 (vc=34074, M08-A2-VCG-02): "does not seek him" — rather than by any term for seeking CHAR-1 from another. CHAR-1 generates itself internally (Mar 7:22, vc=33928: "flows out of a person") rather than being received through seeking from an external source. No seeking/supplication term for CHAR-1 is evidenced in §3.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Yes — uniquely within M08. Psa 19:13 (vc=34095, M08-B-VCG-02): "keep back your servant also from presumptuous sins; let them not have dominion over me" — the psalmist's prayer against CHAR-2 is a seeking/supplication term of resistance. This is not a term for seeking CHAR-2 from another but for seeking deliverance from CHAR-2's internal dominion-seeking impulses. The prayer against CHAR-2 is itself a finding: it confirms that CHAR-2 is understood as an internal impulse that requires divine restraint, not merely an external behaviour to be regulated.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (S)

The verse evidence in §3.B does not include a supplication or seeking term directed toward CHAR-3. Unlike CHAR-2 (which has Psa 19:13's prayer against presumptuous sins), CHAR-3 lacks a direct prayer-against formulation in its 70-verse corpus. The closest is 1Cor 1:29 (vc=33877): God's elective design is described as specifically aimed at eliminating human boasting — but this is descriptive of God's purpose, not a human supplication against CHAR-3.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (S)

The verse evidence is silent on a supplication or seeking term for CHAR-4 in §3.C. No prayer-against-CHAR-4 formulation appears in the corpus, unlike CHAR-2's Psa 19:13 prayer against presumptuous sins.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (S)

The verse evidence is silent on a supplication or seeking term directed against CHAR-5 in §3.D. No prayer-against formulation appears, unlike CHAR-2's Psa 19:13 ("keep back your servant from presumptuous sins"). The evidence for resistance to CHAR-5 is instructional (1Ti 6:17 — "charge them not to be haughty") rather than supplicatory.

---

##### T7.1.8 — What does the relationship between the OT Hebrew vocabulary and the NT Greek vocabulary reveal about continuity or development of this characteristic across the Testaments?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The OT Hebrew vocabulary is markedly richer and more varied for CHAR-1: at least 13 distinct terms from two root families (g-'-h and r-w-m) name CHAR-1 from multiple angles — spatial metaphor (rum, ga.vah, ga.on), dispositional quality (ga.a.vah, ge.vah), person-type adjective (ge.eh, ga.vo.ah), verbal act (rum, ga.ah, ga.vah). The NT Greek vocabulary is more economical: huperēfanos/huperēfania (the primary NT pair), hupsēlos (high/lofty — Luk 16:15, vc=60870; Rom 11:20, vc=60876; Rom 12:16, vc=60877, M08-A4-VCG-01), and filautos (G5367, 2Ti 3:2, vc=1899, M08-A4-VCG-01) as the generative root. The OT vocabulary is predominantly spatial-metaphorical and broad in register; the NT vocabulary concentrates on person-type and quality terms with greater psychological precision. Continuity: the same characteristic is named across both testaments through the same spatial-elevation metaphor. Development: the NT huperēfanos (appearing above others) adds the social-visibility dimension explicitly, and filautos (self-love) names the root motivation with greater analytical specificity than the OT vocabulary does.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Strong continuity with NT refinement. The OT Hebrew vocabulary (zid/za.don/zed) names CHAR-2 through the lens of presumptuous transgression of divine law and appointed authority — primarily within covenantal settings (Deu, Neh, Psa 119). The NT Greek vocabulary (authadēs, tolmētēs, archō) refines the characterisation in three directions: (a) authadēs (Tit 1:7, vc=42740) shifts emphasis to the self-pleasing volitional orientation that generates CHAR-2 — naming the root motivation rather than the act; (b) tolmētēs (2Pe 2:10, vc=4670) extends CHAR-2 to the spiritual-beings interface (boldness against glorious ones) beyond the OT's primarily human-authority focus; (c) archō in M08-B-VCG-03 uses narrative-temporal marking to identify the onset of presumptuous relational assertions in NT episode-sequences. The NT develops the self-will (authadēs) and spiritual-authority (tolmētēs) dimensions of CHAR-2 that are implicit in the OT vocabulary but not explicitly theorised.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

The OT Hebrew vocabulary for CHAR-3 is relatively sparse (ha.lal in its self-directed sense, ro.hav) compared to the NT Greek's rich kauchaomai family. The OT evidences the prohibition (Jer 9:23, vc=33342: the three prohibitions), the wisdom observation (Pro 25:14, 27:1), and the prophetic condemnation (Jer 49:4, vc=33360). The NT develops CHAR-3 dramatically: the Pauline examined discourse (2Cor 10–12) is unparalleled in depth and sophistication — it is the NT's extended engagement with the boasting-impulse's examination, discipline, and redirection. The NT development reveals that the Christ-event (cross and resurrection) provides the theological framework within which CHAR-3 can be not merely condemned (OT) but examined, bounded, and redirected (NT). The kauchaomai family's three-register span (VCG-01/02/03) is largely a NT development from the OT's primarily prohibitive treatment.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

CHAR-4 has no OT Hebrew component — the 12-verse corpus is entirely NT Greek. This is analytically significant: CHAR-4's specific vocabulary (fusioō, tufoō, huperfroneō) appears to be distinctively Hellenistic, without direct Hebrew equivalents. The cognitive self-inflation register of fusioō/tufoō is not evidenced in the OT Hebrew wisdom tradition's vocabulary for pride (which is dominated by the g-'-h and r-w-m roots naming spatial elevation). CHAR-4 as a discrete, specifically cognitive characteristic may represent a NT development in the conceptualisation of pride — the Greek psychological vocabulary's capacity to distinguish the cognitive self-assessment faculty as a specific location for pride's operation gives CHAR-4 a precision that the Hebrew vocabulary does not provide.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

The OT Hebrew vocabulary for CHAR-5 (ga.on, ma.rom, ga.vah, shal.le.tet, a.din, qo.mah) is rich and diverse, spanning the national-collective (ga.on proud-might corpus) and the individual-structural (ma.rom fortification, ga.vah wealth-pride). The OT's primary frame is national-imperial: Egypt, Israel, Sodom, Edom, Babylon, Tyre are the subjects. The NT Greek vocabulary (hupsēlofroneō — 1Ti 6:17) is a single term, shifting the frame from national-imperial to individual-community: "the rich in this present age" as the primary subject. The NT development moves CHAR-5 from the prophetic-national register to the pastoral-individual register — same characteristic, different subject scale. The OT provides the structural-national depth; the NT provides the individual-pastoral application.

---

##### T7.1.9 — Is there a term newly coined in the NT period for this characteristic — and if so, what does that coinage reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Huperēfanos (G5244) and huperēfania (G5243) appear to be distinctly Hellenistic-period terms that do not have direct Hebrew equivalents. The compound structure — huper (above, over) + phainomai (to appear, to be visible) — names CHAR-1 through the social-appearance register: the arrogant person is one who presents themselves as above others in the social field. This is a more psychologically specific coinage than the Hebrew height vocabulary: it names not just the upward direction of self-elevation but the social-comparative and visibility dimension — the proud person is one who actively manifests superiority to others. Filautos (G5367, 2Ti 3:2, vc=1899, M08-A4-VCG-01) — self-lover — also appears to be a NT-period term naming the root motivational structure of CHAR-1 (love of self as the generative root) with a precision the Hebrew vocabulary does not supply. These NT coinages reveal that the NT period brought analytic refinement to CHAR-1's characterisation: moving from primarily spatial-metaphorical (Hebrew height) to social-comparative (huperēfanos) and root-motivational (filautos) description.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Authadēs (G0829) appears to be a Hellenistic compound term (auto — self + hēdomai — to please) that names CHAR-2's motivational root with analytical precision not present in the Hebrew vocabulary. The term names the self-pleasing volitional orientation — the will that satisfies its own preferences without constraint from legitimate authority — as the generative inner disposition of CHAR-2. This is a NT-period coinage that adds motivational specificity: where zid names the boiling-over act and za.don names the insolent quality, authadēs names the self-referential will that generates both. Tit 1:7 (vc=42740, M08-B-VCG-03) deploys it as a disqualifier for church leadership — the self-willed person cannot lead because their will is unconstrained by legitimate authority.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Alazoneia (G0212) and alazōn (G0213) are Hellenistic Greek terms that appear in the NT with their established Greco-Roman social-psychology meaning: the alazōn is a stock character type in Greek comedy — the boastful imposter who claims more than they possess. The NT deploys this existing social-type vocabulary to name CHAR-3's person-type dimension (2Ti 3:2; Rom 1:30). This is not a NT coinage but a borrowing from Hellenistic social discourse that provides CHAR-3 with a culturally recognisable person-type (the stock braggart figure of Greek social analysis). The NT's distinctive theological contribution is not the term but the framework (cross, received grace) within which CHAR-3 is examined.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Fusioō (G5448) and its noun fusiōsis (G5450) appear to be relatively rare in pre-NT Greek — their specific application to cognitive self-inflation within the inner-being register appears to be developed within the Pauline corpus. The term's dominance in Pauline community contexts (1Cor: 6 of 7 uses; 2Cor: 1 use) suggests it may be a Pauline innovation or at least a Pauline-specialised application of an existing term. The cognitive specificity of "inflation" as a metaphor for the mind's false self-assessment is a conceptual development of significant precision: it names not just self-elevation (CHAR-1's rum/ga.on) but specifically the inflation of the cognitive self-picture beyond its actual substance.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Hupsēlofroneō (G5309) combines hupsēlos (high/lofty — a common Greek term) with froneō (to think/set the mind — shared with huperfroneō of CHAR-4 and the phronēsis wisdom vocabulary). The compound appears to be a specifically Pauline formation naming the cognitive-dispositional elevation that wealth generates — not well-attested in pre-NT Greek literature. The coinage reveals that the NT period identified a specific compound for wealth-grounded haughtiness: the structural elevation of the rich person (hupsēlos — high) combined with the resulting inner cognitive orientation (froneō — thinking/mindset), naming the characteristic as the thinking of the high. The parallel with CHAR-4's huperfroneō (thinking-above-measure) confirms the huper-/hupsēlos/froneō family as the NT's preferred vocabulary for cognitive self-elevation pride across CHAR-4 (cognitive inflation) and CHAR-5 (wealth-grounded haughtiness).

---

##### T7.1.10 — What does the full vocabulary arc reveal about this characteristic's complete semantic range?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The full vocabulary arc — spanning at least 20 distinct Hebrew and Greek terms in the 149-verse CHAR-1 corpus — reveals that arrogant self-elevation is one of the most lexically rich characteristics in the programme's evidence base. The semantic range covers: (a) Spatial-metaphorical (height/elevation): rum (H7311A/H7312), ga.vah (H1361), ga.on (H1347), ga.vo.ah (H1364), ma.rom (H4791), qo.mah (H6967), hupsēlos (G5308) — the core upward-movement metaphor; (b) Dispositional quality: ga.a.vah (H1346), ge.vah (H1466), ge.ah (H1344), ga.on (H1347), huperēfania (G5243) — the settled inner posture; (c) Person-type: ge.eh (H1343), ga.vo.ah (H1364), huperēfanos (G5244), sha.chats (H7830 — fierce self-asserting creatures) — the one who characteristically bears CHAR-1; (d) Volitional-act: rum (verb active), ga.ah (H1342 — to rise), ga.vah (verb) — the act of self-elevation; (e) Root-motivation: filautos (G5367) — the generative self-love orientation; (f) Social-appearance: huperēfanos (G5244) — the one who presents above others. The arc from Hebrew spatial metaphor to Greek social-comparative to NT motivational root reveals a progressive analytical refinement across the Testaments, with the Hebrew establishing the spatial metaphor and the NT developing the social and motivational precision.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The full vocabulary arc across zid, za.don, zed (OT) and authadēs, tolmētēs, archō (NT) reveals CHAR-2 as a characteristic with a narrower but more precisely targeted semantic range than CHAR-1. The range covers: (a) act register: zid (the boiling-over act), archō (the initiation of the presumptuous action); (b) dispositional quality: za.don (the insolent inner quality), authadēs (the self-willed orientation); (c) person-type: zed (the insolent person), tolmētēs (the recklessly bold person); (d) prayer-resistance term: Psa 19:13 (presumptuous sins as object of resistant prayer). The vocabulary arc is consistent: all terms name the self-authorising will's transgression of an established authority, from different angles (act, quality, type, motivational root). The NT adds motivational precision (authadēs) and extends the scope to spiritual beings (tolmētēs).

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

The full vocabulary arc — ha.lal, ro.hav (OT) and kauchaomai/kauchēma/kauchēsis, alazoneia/alazōn (NT) — reveals CHAR-3 as the M08 characteristic with the broadest positive valence within its vocabulary: the kauchaomai family spans condemnation (VCG-01), examination (VCG-02), and commendation (VCG-03). This is unique in M08: no other characteristic's primary vocabulary spans all three moral evaluations with the same terms. The arc reveals that the glorying/boasting capacity is not inherently evil but direction-dependent — making CHAR-3 the M08 characteristic closest to the M22 praise-register at the vocabulary level.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The full vocabulary arc (fusioō, tufoō, fusiōsis, huperfroneō) reveals CHAR-4 as the most lexically focused of the M08 characteristics: four terms, all from the same cognitive-inflation semantic domain, with no cross-register spanning (unlike CHAR-1's rum/ga.on or CHAR-3's kauchaomai). The arc consistently names: cognitive inflation without actual substance (fusioō), cognitive obscuration by self-generated smoke (tufoō), the measure-exceeding cognitive act (huperfroneō), and the communal disorder this produces (fusiōsis). The vocabulary arc is entirely NT and entirely Pauline (except 2Ti's tufoō), confirming CHAR-4 as a characteristic distinctively developed in the NT's engagement with community formation.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

The full vocabulary arc — ga.on, ma.rom, ga.vah, shal.le.tet, a.din, qo.mah (OT) and hupsēlofroneō (NT) — reveals CHAR-5 as the most structurally diverse vocabulary set in M08: seven distinct terms spanning the collective (ga.on — national proud might), the spatial (ma.rom, qo.mah — height), the dispositional (ga.vah — heart-pride), the volitional (shal.le.tet — imperious self-will), the affective (a.din — voluptuous ease), and the cognitive-individual (hupsēlofroneō). This breadth reflects CHAR-5's multi-dimensional character: it operates through the widest range of structural media (military, geographic, economic, political, affective) of any M08 characteristic. The arc confirms CHAR-5 as M08's structural-power register — the characteristic that engages all the faculties (dispositional, volitional, cognitive, affective) through the specific medium of received structural goods.

---

#### T7.2 — Verse and Literary Interpretation

##### T7.2.1 — What is the function of this characteristic's primary term within its primary verse — what role does it play in the sentence and argument?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Taking rum (H7311A) in Deu 8:14 (vc=34223, M08-A1-VCG-01) as the primary verse: "then your heart will be lifted up [rum], and you will forget the Lord your God." Rum functions here as the passive/reflexive verbal pivot in the conditional-consequence sentence structure: prosperity received (preceding context: eating and being full — Deu 8:12–13) → heart lifted up [rum] → God forgotten (the consequence). The grammatical function is causal-transitional: rum names the inner movement that is the pivot between the before-state (material satisfaction received) and the after-state (spiritual forgetfulness). The sentence argument is: conditions of blessing, when they activate CHAR-1 (heart lifted up), produce the specific downstream consequence of divine forgetfulness. Rum therefore bears the entire analytical weight of the verse's argument at the causal hinge-point. Without rum, the sentence has no mechanism for the connection between prosperity and forgetfulness — rum is what makes the connection intelligible.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Taking zid in Deu 18:20 (vc=34119, M08-B-VCG-01): "the prophet who presumes [zid] to speak a word in my name that I have not commanded him to speak, or who speaks in the name of other gods, that same prophet shall die." Zid functions as the participial qualifier of "the prophet" — naming the defining inner quality of the transgression (presumptuousness) as what constitutes the capital offence. The grammatical function is definitional-qualificatory: zid distinguishes this prophet's speech from legitimate prophecy not by the form of the speech but by the inner quality of the speaker's self-authorising will. The verse's argument rests on zid as the diagnostic criterion: it is the inner presumptuous claim to speak God's word that God did not command that constitutes the transgression, not merely the content of the speech.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Taking kauchaomai in 1Cor 1:31 (vc=33878, M08-C-VCG-03): "let the one who boasts [kauchaomai], boast in the Lord." The verb functions here as a commanded act — not a prohibition but an imperative redirection. The grammatical function is command/commission: Paul redirects the boasting-impulse rather than eliminating it. The theological argument of 1Cor 1:26–31 rests on this: since God has chosen the weak and foolish to shame the strong (1Cor 1:27), the proper response is not silence (the boasting-capacity suppressed) but God-directed boasting (the boasting-capacity redirected). Kauchaomai carries the entire transformational logic: the same verb that names VCG-01's condemned boasting (1Cor 1:29: "no human being might boast") is the verb that commands VCG-03's God-directed exultation (1Cor 1:31: "let the one who boasts, boast in the Lord").

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Taking fusioō in 1Cor 8:1 (vc=33935, M08-D-VCG-01): "knowledge puffs up [fusioō], but love builds up [oikodomeō]." Fusioō functions as the main verbal predicate of a structural antithesis: knowledge → fusioō (inflate) vs love → oikodomeō (build up). The grammatical function is contrastive-evaluative: the two actions are placed in direct antithesis. Fusioō's specific function is to name the characteristic outcome of knowledge when received without love — not that all knowledge inflates, but that knowledge-without-love inflates. The verse's argument rests on fusioō as the diagnostic term: it names what happens to the inner person when cognitive goods are processed without the relational anchor of love.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Taking a.din in Isa 47:8 (vc=9563, M08-E-VCG-02) as the primary verse: "you who love pleasures [a.din], who sit securely, who say in your heart, 'I am, and there is no one besides me; I shall not sit as a widow or know the loss of children.'" A.din functions as the participial characteriser of the addressee — "you who love pleasures" identifies the affective ground of CHAR-5 before the verse states its cognitive-declarative climax. The grammatical function is characterising-prior-to-indicting: the verse first characterises the inner affective orientation (pleasure-love/ease) that generates CHAR-5, then names the inner declaration it produces ("I am, and there is no one besides me"). A.din provides the causal affective ground from which the self-declaration emerges — it is the generating-ground term for what the verse then names as the declaration of self-completeness.

---

##### T7.2.2 — What literary form carries the primary verse evidence (narrative, psalm, wisdom, prophecy, epistle, apocalyptic) — and what does that form require for responsible interpretation?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The 149-verse CHAR-1 corpus spans five distinct literary forms. (a) Wisdom/instruction (≈15 verses: Pro, Job, Ecc — M08-A4-VCG-04): requires interpretation as generalised counsel about inner-being patterns, not situational description; Pro 16:18 (vc=34073) and Pro 16:5 (vc=12083) are structural wisdom maxims and should be read as pattern-statements, not absolute predictions about individual cases. (b) Prophetic oracle (≈12 verses: Isa, Jer, Eze, Hos, Amo, Zep, Zec — M08-A3): requires attention to the oracle's addressee and its rhetorical function (judgment speech, lament, warning); Isa 16:6 (vc=33969, vc=33989, M08-A3-VCG-01) is a report of collective pride in the context of a Moab judgment oracle. (c) Historical narrative (≈8 verses: 2Ch, Dan, 1Ki — M08-A1-VCG-01/02): requires attention to narrative context and whether the claim is normative or descriptive of a specific episode; 2Ch 26:16 (vc=34044) is a narrative explanation of Uzziah's fall, not a universal law. (d) Psalmic/prayer (≈9 verses: Psa — M08-A2, M08-A4-VCG-02/03): requires sensitivity to the speaker's perspective and petition-form; Psa 131:1 (vc=34059, vc=34224) is a first-person vow, not a generalised description. (e) NT epistolary (≈8 verses: Mar, Luk, Rom, 2Ti, Jam, 1Pe — M08-A4-VCG-01): requires contextualisation within each epistle's theological argument; Jam 4:6 (vc=33931) cites Pro 3:34 within an argument about worldliness vs submission to God.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The §3.A corpus spans four primary literary forms. (a) Covenant instruction (Deu — M08-B-VCG-01): legal instruction establishing the standard and consequence for CHAR-2; requires reading as binding legal regulation within covenant context. (b) Historical narrative/prayer (Neh 9, M08-B-VCG-01): retrospective historical confession of communal CHAR-2; requires sensitivity to the penitential context and the narrator's theological framing. (c) Wisdom maxim (Pro 11:2, 13:10, 21:24 — M08-B-VCG-02): structural wisdom observations stated as general patterns; requires interpretation as pattern-statements rather than case-descriptions. (d) Psalmic/prayer (Psa 19:13, Psa 86, Psa 119 — M08-B-VCG-02): first-person experiential testimony of CHAR-2's social impact and prayer for deliverance; requires sensitivity to the speaker's relational experience.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Five literary forms span §3.B. (a) Wisdom proverb (1Ki 20:11, vc=33353; Pro 20:14, vc=33357; Pro 25:14, vc=33358; Pro 27:1, vc=33359, M08-C-VCG-01): memorable observations that name CHAR-3's foolishness through analogy (clouds/wind without rain; premature armour-boasting). (b) Prophetic prohibition (Jer 9:23, vc=33342, M08-C-VCG-01): direct divine word prohibiting three forms of creaturely boasting. (c) Pauline epistolary instruction (Rom 2:17/23; 1Cor 1:29/31; 1Cor 4:7; Eph 2:9 — M08-C-VCG-01 and VCG-03): theological argument establishing the grounds and limits of legitimate boasting. (d) Pauline apologetic discourse (2Cor 10–12, M08-C-VCG-02): the most extended examination of CHAR-3 in the NT, requiring interpretation within the specific context of Paul's defence against rivals' claims. (e) Pauline doxological/relational (1Th 2:19; 2Th 1:4; Phili 1:26; 2:16; Heb 3:6 — M08-C-VCG-03): the positive deployments of the boasting vocabulary in community relationships and eschatological orientation.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The entire §3.C corpus is NT epistolary. Two primary forms: (a) Community corrective instruction (1Cor — M08-D-VCG-01): Paul addressing specific community dysfunction (partisan conceit, community CHAR-4 over moral failure, knowledge-conceit); requires interpretation within the specific community crisis addressed. (b) Pastoral/leadership instruction (1Ti/2Ti/Tit — M08-D-VCG-02): Paul addressing character requirements for leaders (1Ti 3:6) and characterising the false teacher (1Ti 6:4) and end-times moral collapse (2Ti 3:4); requires attention to the normative/descriptive distinction in pastoral epistles. Additionally: theological instruction (Rom 12:3 — community address) and christological ethics (Col 2:18 — address to ungrounded spiritual practice).

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Four primary literary forms span §3.D. (a) Covenant stipulation (Lev 26:19, vc=33982, M08-E-VCG-01): conditional covenant warning — if Israel walks contrary to God, their power-pride will be broken; requires interpretation within the covenantal if-then structure. (b) Prophetic oracle against nations (Eze 7:24; 30:6/30:18/32:12/33:28; 16:49; 28:5; Jer 49:16; 51:53; Obd 3; Hab 2:9 — M08-E-VCG-01/02): the dominant form; direct divine address to a nation or city naming CHAR-5 and announcing judgment; requires attention to oracle-addressee and rhetorical purpose (judgment speech, woe, taunt). (c) Prophetic lament (Eze 19:11, vc=54398, M08-E-VCG-02): lament over the fallen rulers of Judah using the vine-metaphor; requires sensitivity to the lamentation form. (d) NT pastoral instruction (1Ti 6:17, vc=60878, M08-E-VCG-02): direct charge to Timothy to instruct the wealthy; requires interpretation within the context of pastoral formation of individual persons.

---

##### T7.2.3 — What is the logical structure of key arguments in the verse evidence — what are the premises and conclusions?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Four argument structures are evidenced. First, causal-conditional (Deu 8:14, vc=34223, M08-A1-VCG-01): premise — prosperity is received; mechanism — heart is lifted up; conclusion — God is forgotten. The argument presupposes that CHAR-1 is the inner mechanism that converts received blessing into spiritual displacement of God. Second, structural wisdom law (Pro 16:18, vc=34073, M08-A1-VCG-03): premise — CHAR-1 (haughty spirit/pride) is present; conclusion — destruction/fall follows necessarily. The argument is a structural observation stated as an invariant pattern with no exception clause. Third, divine-prerogative declaration (Psa 75:6–7, vc=34301, vc=34230, M08-A4-VCG-05): premise — lifting up does not originate from east, west, or wilderness (i.e., from any human direction); conclusion — God alone executes judgment, putting down one and lifting up another. The argument makes CHAR-1 structurally impossible as a legitimate act: if exaltation is exclusively God's prerogative, then self-exaltation is a prerogative-usurpation with no valid basis. Fourth, structural opposition (Jam 4:6, vc=33931, M08-A4-VCG-01): premise — God opposes the proud; premise — God gives grace to the humble; conclusion — arrogance and humility produce structurally opposite divine responses. The argument frames CHAR-1 as determinative of the divine relational response.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Three argument structures are evidenced. First, conditional-judicial (Deu 17:12, vc=34110, M08-B-VCG-02): if-condition — the man presumes to disobey the appointed judge; consequence — he shall die; purpose — "so you shall purge the evil from Israel." The argument combines diagnostic criterion + consequence + social-purification purpose. Second, structural wisdom law (Pro 11:2, vc=34109; Pro 13:10, vc=34113, M08-B-VCG-02): premise — CHAR-2 is present; invariant conclusion — disgrace follows (Pro 11:2) / strife comes (Pro 13:10). Third, intercessory prayer (Psa 19:13, vc=34095, M08-B-VCG-02): premise — presumptuous sins seek dominion over the will; request — divine restraint ("keep back your servant"); goal — blamelessness. The argument reveals CHAR-2 as an inner dominating force requiring external (divine) restraint.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Three argument structures. First, received-goods argument (1Cor 4:7, vc=33871, M08-C-VCG-01): premise — everything you have was received; conclusion — boasting as if it were self-generated is logically false. This is the most formally tight argument against CHAR-3: it grounds the condemnation in ontological fact (all goods are received) rather than merely in moral prohibition. Second, elective-design argument (1Cor 1:27–31, vc=33877/33878, M08-C-VCG-01/03): God chose the weak to shame the strong in order to eliminate human boasting and redirect it to the Lord. Third, boundary argument (2Cor 10:13, vc=33888, M08-C-VCG-02): Paul limits his boasting to the sphere God assigned him — the argument is that legitimate self-commendation has God-defined boundaries that the self must not exceed.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Three argument structures. First, contrastive structural law (1Cor 8:1, vc=33935, M08-D-VCG-01): premise — knowledge without love; conclusion — inflation (CHAR-4) results; alternative — love produces building-up. The argument implies a structural law: cognitive goods processed without love inevitably inflate; with love they build. Second, qualification-conditional (1Ti 3:6, vc=33924, M08-D-VCG-02): if a new convert is given leadership → he may become conceited → and fall into the devil's condemnation. The qualification ("recent convert") is the diagnostic criterion — the argument uses formation-status as the risk variable. Third, God-measure standard (Rom 12:3, vc=60866, M08-D-VCG-02): premise — God has assigned each person a measure of faith; command — do not exceed that measure in cognitive self-assessment; alternative — think soberly according to that measure.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Three argument structures. First, covenantal conditional (Lev 26:19, vc=33982, M08-E-VCG-01): if-condition — Israel walks contrary to God; consequence — "I will break the pride of your power." The argument grounds God's breaking of CHAR-5 in covenantal violation — power-pride is the inner symptom of the violation; breaking it is the covenantal consequence. Second, prophetic reversal argument (Eze 30:6, vc=33996; Jer 49:16, vc=34167; Obd 3, vc=65674): premise — the nation holds structural height/power; declaration — God will bring it down. The argument rests on the contrast between present structural height and its coming reversal — the very structural goods that generate CHAR-5 will be removed. Third, pastoral charge (1Ti 6:17, vc=60878, M08-E-VCG-02): premise — God richly provides everything; command — do not be haughty; alternative — be generous and ready to share. The argument grounds the anti-CHAR-5 command in God's role as the actual provider of all structural goods.

---

##### T7.2.4 — What contextual setting carries the primary verse evidence (judicial, liturgical, covenantal, communal, eschatological) — and what does that setting reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Four primary contextual settings are evidenced. (a) Covenantal: Deu 8:14 (vc=34223, M08-A1-VCG-01) and Hos 13:6 (vc=34232, M08-A1-VCG-01) sit within covenantal instruction/warning — CHAR-1 is addressed as the danger that threatens the covenant relationship from within; the setting reveals that CHAR-1 is first and most pressingly a problem for the covenant community, not merely for pagans. (b) Judicial/eschatological: the day-of-the-Lord material (M08-A3-VCG-04: Isa 2:12, vc=33957; Isa 10:33, vc=54395/65781) places CHAR-1 in the context of divine judicial assembly and eschatological reversal — the setting reveals CHAR-1's ultimate trajectory. (c) Communal-liturgical: the psalmic corpus (Psa 131:1, vc=34059/34224; Psa 75:4–10, vc=34244–34264, M08-A4-VCG-05) addresses CHAR-1 within worship and prayer settings — the setting reveals CHAR-1 as a live threat within the worshipping community that requires active liturgical counter-posture (the Psa 131 vow). (d) Wisdom-formative: the Proverbs material (Pro 16:5, vc=12083; Pro 16:18, vc=34073; Pro 29:23, vc=33960, M08-A4-VCG-04) addresses CHAR-1 as a subject of formative instruction — the setting reveals CHAR-1 as a characteristic that requires active wisdom-teaching to address.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Three primary contextual settings. (a) Covenant-legal: Deu 17:12–13 (vc=34110/34124) and Deu 18:20 (vc=34119, M08-B-VCG-01) — the judicial-legal setting of Israel's covenant administration; CHAR-2 is addressed as a capital legal offence within a structured divine-human covenant. (b) Penitential-historical: Neh 9:10–29 (M08-B-VCG-01) — community prayer of confession; CHAR-2 is named as the defining pattern of Israel's historical failure in relation to God's covenant. (c) Wisdom-formative: Pro 11:2, 13:10, 21:24 (M08-B-VCG-02) — the formation context of wisdom instruction; CHAR-2 is named as a characterological failure with predictable consequences.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Four primary settings. (a) Community instruction (1Cor — VCG-01 and VCG-03): CHAR-3 addressed within a specific community's internal problems (factional boasting — 1Cor 3:21; community corruption — 1Cor 5:6). (b) Apostolic self-defence (2Cor 10–12 — VCG-02): CHAR-3 examined in the context of Paul defending his apostolic integrity against rivals whose boasting challenged his authority. (c) Wisdom formation (Pro, Jer 9:23 — VCG-01): CHAR-3 addressed in formative contexts where character is being shaped. (d) Doxological/eschatological (1Th, Phili, Heb — VCG-03): CHAR-3 positively deployed in contexts of community commendation and future orientation toward Christ.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Three primary settings. (a) Community formation (1Cor — M08-D-VCG-01): CHAR-4 addressed within the context of a specific community experiencing partisan divisions, knowledge-conceit, and moral failure — requiring the correction of cognitive inflation as part of community formation. (b) Leadership qualification (1Ti/Tit — M08-D-VCG-02): CHAR-4 addressed in the context of identifying character requirements for church leaders — the conceited person is disqualified; the formation context is the path of qualification. (c) Theological-ethical instruction (Rom 12 — M08-D-VCG-02): CHAR-4 addressed within the theological framework of the body of Christ and the proper ordering of spiritual gifts — each member thinking accurately within their God-assigned measure.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Three primary settings. (a) National-imperial judgment contexts (Eze 30–32 — Egypt; Jer 49 — Edom; Jer 51 — Babylon; Obd — Edom; Hab 2 — unspecified power): God's judicial address to nations with structural power, requiring CHAR-5 to be read as a characteristic of collective political entities. (b) Covenantal-Israel contexts (Lev 26:19; Eze 7:24; 16:49; 33:28): CHAR-5 addressed as Israel's own characteristic within the covenant, requiring attention to the covenant-infidelity frame. (c) Individual formation contexts (1Ti 6:17): CHAR-5 addressed as a danger for individual wealthy persons within the NT community, requiring the pastoral-formation frame.

---

##### T7.2.5 — Does any verse function as the primary anchor for this characteristic — the verse that most fully and directly expresses its essential character?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The strongest candidate for the primary anchor of CHAR-1 is Pro 16:5 (vc=12083, M08-A1-VCG-03): "Everyone who is arrogant in heart is an abomination to the Lord; be assured, he will not go unpunished." This verse names: (a) the constitutional location — "in heart"; (b) the subject scope — "everyone," universal and unconditional; (c) the divine moral evaluation — "an abomination to the Lord," the strongest evaluative term in the wisdom corpus; (d) the structural consequence — "he will not go unpunished," stated as categorical certainty. No other single verse in the 149-verse corpus combines all four of these dimensions simultaneously with comparable economy. A strong secondary anchor candidate is Psa 75:6–7 (vc=34301, vc=34230, M08-A4-VCG-05): "not from the east or from the west... comes lifting up, but it is God who executes judgment, putting down one and lifting up another" — which grounds CHAR-1's structural impossibility as a legitimate act in the divine prerogative of exaltation.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The strongest candidate for the primary anchor of CHAR-2 is Psa 19:13 (vc=34095, M08-B-VCG-02): "keep back your servant also from presumptuous sins; let them not have dominion over me, then I shall be blameless, and I shall be innocent of great transgression." This verse reveals: (a) the constitutional nature of CHAR-2 as inner impulses that seek to "gain dominion over" the will — naming CHAR-2's volitional-dominating quality; (b) the need for divine restraint — CHAR-2 cannot be overcome by the person alone; (c) the connection to blamelessness — CHAR-2's absence is the condition for integrity before God; (d) the link to "great transgression" — CHAR-2 is named as the path to the most serious moral failure. No other single verse in §3.A combines these four elements simultaneously.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

The strongest candidate is 1Cor 1:29–31 (vc=33877, vc=33878, M08-C-VCG-01/03), which together provide: (a) the condemned form's ground — "no human being might boast in the presence of God" (v.29); (b) the transformative logic — God's elective design specifically forecloses human self-boasting grounds; (c) the commanded alternative — "let the one who boasts, boast in the Lord" (v.31). This two-verse unit is the most comprehensive single statement of CHAR-3's full arc (from condemned VCG-01 form through redirected VCG-03 form) in the 70-verse corpus. A secondary candidate is Jer 9:23 (vc=33342, M08-C-VCG-01): the threefold prohibition that names all three primary boasting-grounds (wisdom, might, wealth) simultaneously.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The strongest candidate is 1Cor 8:1 (vc=33935, M08-D-VCG-01): "knowledge puffs up [fusioō], but love builds up." This verse: (a) names the characteristic (fusioō) through its primary metaphor; (b) identifies the trigger (knowledge without love); (c) names the structural opposite (love building up); (d) reveals the community consequence (unbuilt-up community vs built-up community). All in eight words. No other verse in §3.C condenses these four elements simultaneously. A secondary candidate is Rom 12:3 (vc=60866, M08-D-VCG-02): "do not think of yourself more highly than you ought, but think with sober judgment, each according to the measure of faith that God has assigned" — which adds the God-measure framework that 1Cor 8:1 lacks.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

The strongest candidate is Isa 47:8 (vc=9563, M08-E-VCG-02): "you who love pleasures, who sit securely, who say in your heart, 'I am, and there is no one besides me; I shall not sit as a widow or know the loss of children.'" This verse: (a) names the affective generative ground (a.din — love of pleasures, voluptuous ease); (b) names the inner positional security claim ("sit securely" — the structural confident posture); (c) delivers the most comprehensive inner self-declaration in M08's entire evidence base ("I am, and there is no one besides me" — combining self-sufficiency, ontological claim, and relational self-completeness); (d) names the specific relational vulnerabilities CHAR-5 denies ("not sit as a widow, not know the loss of children"). No other verse in §3.D combines all four dimensions of CHAR-5 simultaneously.

---

##### T7.2.6 — What does the primary anchor verse reveal that no other verse reveals?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Pro 16:5 (vc=12083, M08-A1-VCG-03) reveals four things that no other single verse in the corpus does simultaneously: (a) Universality without exception — "everyone who is arrogant in heart": the universal quantifier makes CHAR-1's divine assessment invariant across person, situation, and covenant status; no other verse states this scope so explicitly for CHAR-1. (b) The deepest divine evaluation language — "an abomination to the Lord" (tōʿăbat yhwh): this is the language used for the most offensive violations of the divine-human order; no other CHAR-1 verse applies this specific evaluative term to CHAR-1 in its heart-form. (c) Punitive certainty — "be assured, he will not go unpunished": stated as categorical assurance, not as a warning about possibility; the certainty language is distinctive to this verse within the wisdom maxim pattern. (d) Constitutional precision — "in heart": naming the specific inner location as the basis of the assessment, not outward behaviour. Together these four elements make Pro 16:5 the single most comprehensive statement of CHAR-1's essential character, divine assessment, and structural consequence in the corpus.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Psa 19:13 (vc=34095, M08-B-VCG-02) reveals uniquely: (a) CHAR-2 as an internal impulse — "presumptuous sins" seeking "dominion" over the will — naming the inner-dominating quality that other verses name only through its external expression. The presumptuous sins have an inner agency that contests the will's proper orientation. No other verse in §3.A so directly identifies CHAR-2 as an inner force seeking dominion within the person; (b) the connection between absence of CHAR-2 and blamelessness — "then I shall be blameless" — making CHAR-2 the specific inner-being barrier to moral integrity; (c) the link to "great transgression" (phe.sha gadol) — identifying CHAR-2 as the inner gateway to the most serious category of moral failure, not merely a minor deviation.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

1Cor 1:31 (vc=33878) uniquely reveals that CHAR-3's remedy is not elimination of the boasting-impulse but its redirection: "let the one who boasts, boast in the Lord" — the command preserves the impulse while redirecting it. No other verse in §3.B states this so directly: the boasting-capacity itself is not condemned but commanded toward its proper object. This makes the verse the pivot of CHAR-3's entire three-VCG structure: the impulse that VCG-01 deploys toward self, and VCG-02 examines with discipline, is VCG-03 commanded toward God as its sole legitimate object.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

1Cor 8:1 (vc=33935, M08-D-VCG-01) uniquely reveals: (a) The trigger/counter logic in a single antithesis: knowledge → inflation; love → building. No other verse in §3.C states both the generating mechanism (knowledge) and the blocking mechanism (love) within the same contrastive structure. (b) The relational consequence of CHAR-4 as the inverse of love's community-building: the inflated person fails to build others up because cognitive self-focus replaces other-directed love. (c) The implication that knowledge and love are in competition for the same inner space: one inflates; the other builds — they are mutually exclusive responses to received cognitive goods.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Isa 47:8 (vc=9563, M08-E-VCG-02) uniquely reveals: (a) The ontological extremity of CHAR-5's self-declaration: "I am, and there is no one besides me" — this is the self-declaration that belongs to God alone (the divine I-am); CHAR-5 at its logical extreme claims the ontological status of the divine self-existence, making it the most theologically extreme form of pride in M08's evidence. (b) The relational self-completion claim: "I shall not sit as a widow or know the loss of children" — CHAR-5 specifically denies the relational vulnerabilities of grief, loss, and dependence. The self-sufficient person believes themselves immune to the relational losses that define creaturely existence. (c) The ease-as-ground connection: the affective ease (a.din) is what sustains the inner posture that makes the self-declaration possible. The verse is the M08 evidence base's single most comprehensive statement of what structural-power pride looks like from the inside.

---

#### T7.3 — Human Science Frameworks

##### T7.3.1 — Which human science framework (psychology, moral philosophy, developmental psychology, sociology, anthropology, or other) is most useful as an interpretive lens for this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Per the science extract's T7.3.1 prompt reference note and the programme's curated science review: social psychology and positive psychology (Section 1 — Tracy and Robins' two-facet pride model) is most useful for CHAR-1's dispositional-emotional register, particularly for understanding the distinction between authentic pride (achievement-based) and hubristic pride (global self-elevation). Clinical psychology's narcissism research (Section 2 — Twenge and Campbell; Keltner) is most useful for CHAR-1's arrogance/haughtiness sub-register, especially the grandiose narcissism model's cognitive (elevated self-evaluation schema) and motivational (dominance-seeking, resistance to authority) dimensions. Evolutionary psychology and social psychology (Section 3 — Henrich and Gil-White's prestige-dominance distinction; Keltner's power paradox) is most useful for M08-A3's collective/national pride register, where status-seeking and dominance motivation operate at group level. For CHAR-1 specifically — the dispositional elevation of the heart — narcissism research (Section 2) and Tracy and Robins' hubristic-pride facet (Section 1) are the most directly illuminating.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Clinical psychology's narcissism research (Section 2 of the science extract — Twenge and Campbell; Keltner) is most useful for CHAR-2's arrogance and self-will dimensions, particularly grandiose narcissism (overt, exhibitionistic, domineering) and the self-will component (authadēs — refusing to be constrained by others). Evolutionary psychology and social psychology (Section 3 — Henrich and Gil-White's prestige-dominance distinction; Keltner's power paradox) is most useful for M08-B-VCG-03's domineering authority register: Mar 10:42 (vc=55588) — "rulers who lord it over others" — maps directly onto the dominance pole of Henrich and Gil-White's distinction (status imposed through intimidation and force rather than freely conferred respect/prestige).

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Social psychology's impression management research (Section 4 of the science extract — Goffman's self-presentation framework; Jones and Pittman's self-promotion strategy) is most directly relevant for CHAR-3's social-display dimension (alazoneia, alazōn, the public self-assertion). Self-enhancement bias research (the tendency to view oneself more positively than objective evidence warrants) is most relevant for the cognitive distortion dimension of VCG-01 boasting (1Cor 4:7 — boasting as if not received; 2Cor 10:12 — self-comparison without understanding). The Tracy and Robins two-facet pride model (Section 1) remains relevant: CHAR-3's VCG-01 aligns with hubristic pride's expression; VCG-03's God-directed glorying aligns with nothing in the model (it has no analogue for God-directed boasting).

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Clinical psychology's narcissism research (Section 2 of the science extract — Twenge and Campbell; Keltner) is most relevant, specifically the cognitive component of narcissism: the belief in one's superiority as the core cognitive self-assessment. Tracy and Robins' two-facet pride model (Section 1) is also directly relevant — hubristic pride (global self-evaluation "I am great" independent of specific achievement) maps onto CHAR-4's inflation "without factual basis" (Col 2:18, vc=33941). Grandiose narcissism's cognitive core (the elevated self-evaluation schema that generates the narrative of superiority) is the closest scientific analogue to CHAR-4's fusioō/huperfroneō vocabulary.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Evolutionary psychology and social psychology (Section 3 of the science extract — Henrich and Gil-White's prestige-dominance distinction; Keltner's power paradox) is most directly relevant for CHAR-5's structural-power register. Keltner's power paradox research — that the acquisition of power reliably reduces empathy and increases self-focus — directly illuminates CHAR-5's Eze 16:49 pattern: national power-and-ease reliably generates the failure to aid the poor. Henrich and Gil-White's prestige-dominance distinction maps onto CHAR-5's two sub-registers: the ga.on military-might corpus (M08-E-VCG-01) maps onto dominance-based status (imposed through force), while 1Ti 6:17's wealthy persons are more prestige-adjacent. For CHAR-5's individual wealth-pride dimension (1Ti 6:17), Section 2 (narcissism research — power and accountability) is also relevant.

---

##### T7.3.2 — Where the human science framework illuminates the verse evidence — making a finding more coherent or complete — what does it reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Three illuminations from the science framework are directly relevant to CHAR-1's evidence. First, Tracy and Robins' two-facet model (Section 1) illuminates the verse evidence's implicit distinction between the prosperity-triggered heart-elevation (M08-A1-VCG-01 — Deu 8:14, Hos 13:6: "when they became full... their heart was lifted up") and the dispositional global self-elevation of the wisdom corpus (M08-A1-VCG-03 — Pro 16:5: "arrogant in heart"). The former corresponds to authentic pride (triggered by specific conditions of achievement/success), the latter to hubristic pride (global self-evaluation as superior). The science framework helps name this distinction that the evidence evidences but does not explicitly theorise. Second, Keltner's power paradox (Section 2 — power reliably reduces empathy and increases self-focus) directly illuminates the prosperity-trigger pattern evidenced in T5.2 and T5.4: why does material success generate pride (Deu 8:14; 2Ch 26:16; Eze 28:17)? The power paradox research supplies the psychological mechanism — power and success systematically shift inner focus toward the self and away from others and God, which is precisely what the verse evidence describes. Third, narcissism research's characterisation of grandiose narcissism as cognitively entrenched and treatment-resistant (Section 2) illuminates T3.9's finding that CHAR-1 is conscience-resistant and self-sealing: if the science framework identifies grandiose narcissism as resisting the vulnerability required for psychological change, this is convergent with the evidence's consistent pattern of CHAR-1 as internally uncorrectable, requiring external catastrophic reversal.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Two primary illuminations. First, Keltner's power paradox (Section 2 — power reliably reduces empathy and increases self-focus) illuminates why CHAR-2 is evidenced in persons and groups holding structural power: Mar 10:42 (vc=55588, M08-B-VCG-03): rulers lording over their subjects; Jer 50:29 (vc=34127): Babylon's imperial CHAR-2 against God; Mat 24:49 (vc=55613): the wicked servant enabled by perceived absence of accountability. The power paradox explains the mechanism: acquired or perceived power systematically generates the self-focus and authority-contempt that CHAR-2 evidences. Second, grandiose narcissism's resistance to correction (Section 2: "resists the vulnerability required for psychological change") illuminates Neh 9:29's pattern of repeated presumption despite warnings — the person characterised by CHAR-2 has the treatment-resistant quality that makes repeated divine correction insufficient.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Three illuminations. First, Goffman's impression management (Section 4): self-promotion as one of five impression management tactics illuminates CHAR-3's social-strategic dimension — the boaster is not merely expressing inner pride but managing others' perception of them. This illuminates Pro 20:14 (vc=33357: the buyer's duplicitous boast after negotiation) as a calculated impression-management tactic. Second, self-enhancement bias: the empirically robust finding that humans systematically overestimate their positive qualities illuminates 1Cor 4:7's "as if you did not receive it" — self-directed boasting is the social expression of a cognitive self-enhancement bias that misattributes received goods as self-generated. Third, social media and narcissism amplification (Section 4 note): the observation that social media environments reward self-display has been shown to increase self-promotion as a practised behaviour — this illuminates CHAR-3 as environmentally responsive, consistent with the verse evidence's attention to cultural contexts of boasting (the rivals' boasting in 2Cor 11:18 is "according to the flesh" — culturally normed).

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Three illuminations. First, narcissism research's identification of the grandiose self-evaluation schema as cognitively entrenched and resistant to disconfirming evidence illuminates 1Ti 6:4 (vc=33925, M08-D-VCG-02): "understanding nothing" — the science framework explains the mechanism: inflated self-evaluation schemas actively resist evidence that would disconfirm them, producing the comprehensive epistemic blindness the verse names. Second, the two-facet model's hubristic pride (independent of specific achievement — global self-evaluation) illuminates Col 2:18 (vc=33941, M08-D-VCG-01): inflation "without factual basis" — the hubristic pride model specifically identifies inflation without achievement grounding as a diagnostic feature. Third, the power paradox research (Keltner — power reduces empathy and increases self-focus) illuminates why knowledge and leadership generate CHAR-4: receiving cognitive goods (knowledge) or positional goods (leadership) systematically shifts inner focus toward self-assessment and away from others, generating the inflation dynamic.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Three illuminations. First, Keltner's power paradox (power reliably reduces empathy and increases self-focus) directly illuminates the Eze 16:49 (vc=33979, M08-E-VCG-01) and Isa 47:8 (vc=9563) pattern: why does structural power generate self-sufficiency claims and social indifference? The power paradox research supplies the psychological mechanism — power systematically shifts inner focus toward the self and away from others, generating CHAR-5's specific relational failure (not aiding the poor; declaring "there is no one besides me"). Second, the evolutionary psychology of dominance (Section 3 — dominance-seeking arising from competitive contexts, power without accountability) illuminates CHAR-5's shal.le.tet (Eze 16:30, vc=57959) — imperious self-will from a position of structural power. Power without accountability (the condition the powerful occupy) generates the unrestrained self-will that shal.le.tet names. Third, Section 3's note on testosterone levels influencing competitive dominance behaviour illuminates CHAR-5's VCG-01 military-might corpus — the national-martial context where competitive dominance is most viscerally present.

---

##### T7.3.3 — Where the verse evidence and the human science framework diverge, what does the divergence reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

The primary divergence is at the deepest level of evaluation. Per the science extract (Section 1, T7.3.3 note): science distinguishes authentic pride (healthy, achievement-based, prosocial) from hubristic pride (pathological, narcissistic) and treats only the latter as problematic. The verse evidence's critique of CHAR-1 is more thoroughgoing on two counts. First, even achievement-based pride becomes CHAR-1 in the evidence when it forgets the giver: Deu 8:14 (vc=34223, M08-A1-VCG-01) — prosperity and satisfaction received from God activate the heart-lift and God-forgetfulness; 2Ch 26:16 (vc=34044, M08-A1-VCG-01) — genuine strength and achievement activate pride. These are precisely the "authentic pride" scenarios (specific, achievement-triggered) that science treats as healthy — but the verse evidence diagnoses them as the occasions of CHAR-1 when they generate forgetfulness of God as their source. Second, the biblical critique is grounded in creaturely ontology, not social dysfunctionality: even a person who achieves genuine greatness must acknowledge God as the source of their capacity (Psa 75:7, vc=34230: "it is God who executes judgment, putting down one and lifting up another"). The science framework treats pride as a psychological phenomenon assessed by its social consequences; the verse evidence treats CHAR-1 as a theological phenomenon assessed by the creature's proper orientation to the Creator. This is a genuine register divergence, not merely a difference of degree.

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

The primary divergence is in the register of critique. The science framework treats self-assertion, boundary-testing, and even domineering behaviour as pathological primarily when they cause social dysfunction (narcissistic personality disorder, interpersonal problems, reduced empathy). The verse evidence's critique of CHAR-2 operates at the theological level: Deu 18:20 (vc=34119, M08-B-VCG-01) names as the defining offence speaking "a word in my name that I have not commanded" — the issue is not social dysfunction but theological usurpation of divine communicative sovereignty. The science framework cannot locate this dimension of CHAR-2 because it operates without the theological category of divinely-established authority as the normative reference point. What science calls "authoritarian personality" or "dominance-seeking," the verse evidence names as the creature's will asserting itself against the Creator's established order — a qualitatively different critique.

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

The primary divergence is that the science framework has no category for VCG-03 God-directed boasting as a legitimate and commanded form of the glorying-impulse. Section 4 (impression management) treats all self-promotion as socially strategic behaviour aimed at managing others' perception of the self; it has no framework for boasting directed toward God as its object (Rom 5:2; Phili 3:3). The verse evidence's VCG-03 material is simply outside the science framework's horizon: glorying in God, boasting in the cross, exulting in received reconciliation (Rom 5:11, vc=33876) cannot be accommodated within impression management theory because its "audience" is not a social other but God, and its "content" is not the self's attributes but received grace. The divergence reveals that the biblical framework's critique of CHAR-3 is not merely social (protect modesty norms) but ontological (the boasting-impulse has a proper object — God — that social psychology cannot perceive).

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

The primary divergence: the science framework treats cognitive self-inflation (grandiose narcissism, hubristic pride) as primarily a social-relational problem (it damages relationships, reduces empathy, generates interpersonal dysfunction). The verse evidence (Rom 12:3, vc=60866) locates the problem in a different register: the person exceeds the "measure of faith that God has assigned" — the problem is not primarily social-relational but ontological (transgressing the God-given measure). 1Ti 3:6 (vc=33924): "the condemnation of the devil" — the judicial trajectory of CHAR-4 is not social dysfunction (the science framework's concern) but participation in the adversarial paradigm's condemnation (a theological category). The divergence reveals that CHAR-4's critique operates at the level of the creature's proper cognitive station before God, which the science framework cannot access.

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

The primary divergence: the science framework treats power-induced self-focus and reduced empathy as psychological consequences of power acquisition — structural-psychological effects, not moral failures per se. The verse evidence's critique of CHAR-5 operates at the theological level: Lev 26:19 (vc=33982, M08-E-VCG-01): "I will break the pride of your power" — God's judicial response is to the theological transgression of claiming self-sufficient power that belongs to God as creator and sustainer. Isa 47:8 (vc=9563): "I am, and there is no one besides me" — the self-declaration usurps the divine I-am; the science framework cannot locate this theological dimension. Second divergence: the science framework has no category for the eschatological trajectory — the consistent movement toward desolation (Eze 33:28) and shame (Hab 2:9) as the structural end of CHAR-5 is a theological claim about the created order, not a psychological prediction.

---
