##### T7.3.4 — Does the human science framework surface any aspect of this characteristic that the verse evidence has not yet addressed — and does that absence require further verse investigation?

**[CHAR-1] Arrogant self-elevation** (E)

Per the science extract (Section 2, T7.3.4 note): the shame-as-underlying-vulnerability dynamic in narcissism (vulnerable narcissism uses grandiosity as a defence against underlying shame) may surface a connection between M07 (shame) and M08 (CHAR-1) that the verse evidence for CHAR-1 alone has not addressed. The 149-verse CHAR-1 corpus is silent on whether CHAR-1 ever evidences shame as its underlying driver or defensive cover. The evidence consistently presents CHAR-1 as characterised by ease and self-satisfaction (Psa 123:4 — "those who are at ease") rather than by hidden shame anxiety. However, the science framework raises the question of whether there is a CHAR-1 variant in the evidence that is shame-driven rather than satisfaction-driven — a form of compensatory arrogance that masks inner fragility. This would require cross-cluster examination of M07 (shame) and M08 verse sets to test. A second gap: Keltner's power paradox documents that power acquisition systematically reduces empathy — but the verse evidence does not address the empathy-reduction dimension of CHAR-1 explicitly (though Psa 17:10, vc=34028: "they close their hearts to pity" may be the nearest evidence point). Whether reduced empathy capacity is a constitutive feature of CHAR-1 rather than just a correlate is not conclusively evidenced and would benefit from further verse investigation in adjacent clusters addressing compassion and relational capacity.

---

**[CHAR-2] Presumptuous defiance** (E)

Two dimensions are surfaced. First, the Section 2 note on shame as the underlying vulnerability in narcissism (vulnerable narcissism using grandiosity to avoid shame exposure) raises the question of whether CHAR-2 ever evidences an underlying shame-drive — particularly in the social-insolence register of the Psa 119 zed corpus. Psa 119:51 (vc=34099): the insolent's contemptuous derision of the psalmist could be read as shame-projection (making the godly law-keeper the object of contempt because their godliness exposes the insolent person's failure). The §3.A corpus does not directly evidence shame-as-root for CHAR-2, but this would benefit from cross-cluster investigation with M07 (shame). Second, the Section 3 note on hereditary moderate heritability of dominance as a personality trait raises the question of whether CHAR-2 as a communal/generational pattern (Neh 9:16/29) carries a social-hereditary dimension beyond the cultural-communal transmission already evidenced — the §3.A corpus does not address this.

---

**[CHAR-3] Boasting and self-display** (E)

Two dimensions are surfaced. First, Section 4's observation about social media environments amplifying self-promotion raises the question of whether CHAR-3's scale of expression is environmentally sensitive — the verse evidence condemns CHAR-3 regardless of scale, but the science framework notes that specific social environments systematically increase the frequency and intensity of self-promotion. The §3.B corpus does not address environmental amplification as a dimension of CHAR-3's operation. Second, Section 4's note on self-promotion arising from "motivation to be perceived positively by others" — the underlying social-approval motivation — surfaces a question about whether CHAR-3 is driven more by a need for social validation (seeking others' approval) or by genuine inner pride (asserting one's own worth). The §3.B corpus evidences both (alazoneia as inner disposition vs kauchaomai as social act) but does not explicitly address the relative weight of social-approval-seeking vs genuine self-exaltation as the motivational driver of VCG-01 boasting.

**[CHAR-4] Vain conceit** (E)

Two aspects are surfaced. First, Section 2's note on the distinction between grandiose narcissism (overt, exhibitionistic) and vulnerable narcissism (covert, hypersensitive) raises the question of whether CHAR-4 also evidences a covert form. The §3.C corpus evidences the overt form (1Cor 4:18 — the arrogant persons are presuming openly; 1Cor 8:1 — knowledge-conceit expressing itself in the community). Whether a covert, shame-based form of cognitive self-inflation (inflation as compensation for underlying shame) is present in §3.C is not directly evidenced — this would require cross-cluster examination with M07 (shame). Second, the cognitive dissonance research tradition (people resist evidence that disconfirms their self-assessment) provides a mechanism for 1Ti 6:4's "understanding nothing" that the verse evidence does not explicitly theorise: the inflated self-assessment actively generates cognitive resistance to disconfirming information, producing the comprehensive epistemic blindness the verse names as the consequence of conceit.

**Batch 3 · Tier T7 PASS — 20/20 prompts, [CHAR-4] markers verified.**

**[CHAR-5] Pride of power and position** (E)

Two aspects surfaced. First, Section 3's note on hereditary moderate heritability of dominance as a personality trait raises the question of whether CHAR-5's national-generational transmission (the ga.on proud-might of Egypt evidenced across multiple Eze texts as a sustained national characteristic) has any biological-hereditary dimension alongside its cultural-structural transmission. The §3.D corpus evidences cultural-structural generational transmission (Eze 33:28 — Israel's proud might across the historical period) but does not address biological factors. Second, Keltner's observation that power paradox effects are partially reversible when power is shared or accountability structures are imposed illuminates why 1Ti 6:17's instruction (charge them to be generous and ready to share) is specifically identified as the corrective for hupsēlofroneō: sharing wealth (redistributing structural power) reduces the self-focus that generates CHAR-5. The science framework thus supplies the psychological mechanism for why generosity is CHAR-5's antidote, complementing the theological reasoning (God is the provider) that 1Ti 6:17 itself gives.
